## κἀγώ (id: 002510000000000)

κἀγώ
====

κἀγώ (G2504)

pers.pron

92\.1 · Discourse Referentials · Speaker

I too, I indeed \= καί \+ ἐγώ; a reference to the speaker, with an added feature of emphasis in the form ἐγώ The terminology ‘first, second, and third persons’ reflects the normal order in Greek in which the so\-called first person always occurred first in any listing of participants. The second person would be in the second position, and similarly, the third person would be in a third relative position. To preserve that order in English, however, could imply impoliteness, and it is for that reason that it is preferable to translate [JHN 10:30](https://ref.ly/Luke10:30) as ‘the Father and I are one.’

[MAT 2:8](https://ref.ly/Matt2:8) · [MAT 10:32](https://ref.ly/Matt10:32) · [MAT 10:33](https://ref.ly/Matt10:33) · [MAT 11:28](https://ref.ly/Matt11:28) · [MAT 16:18](https://ref.ly/Matt16:18) · [MAT ## καθαιρέω (id: 002513000000000)

καθαιρέω
========

καθαιρέω (G2507)

15\.110 · Linear Movement · Come/Go Down, Descend

to bring down, to lower to cause something or someone to be lowered or brought down For another interpretation of καθαιρέω in [MRK 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36), see [15\.199](#15.199).

[MRK 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36)

15\.199 · Linear Movement · Carry, Bear

to bring down, to take down to bring something down from one point to another For another interpretation of καθαιρέω in [MRK 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36), see [15\.110](#15.110).

[MRK 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46) · [LUK 1:52](https://ref.ly/Mark1:52) · [LUK 23:53](https://ref.ly/Mark23:53) · [ACT 13:29](https://ref.ly/John13:29)

20\.54 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Destroy

to destroy, to tear down, destruction to destroy completely by tearing down and dismantling It may be important in rendering [LUK 12:18](https://ref.ly/Mark12:18) to indicate clearly that there is purpose in tearing down the barns, and that presumably materials resulting from the dismantling of the barns would be used in building bigger ones.

[LUK 12:18](https://ref.ly/Mark12:18) · [2CO 10:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:4)

20\.42 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Destroy

to destroy, to conquer to destroy by conquering and overpowering

[ACT 13:19](https://ref.ly/John13:19)

13\.38 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to do away with, to remove, to eliminate to cause a state to cease1

[ACT 19:27](https://ref.ly/John19:27)

1 There are undoubtedly some significant differences of meaning in this series in [13\.38](#13.38), but it is not possible to determine the distinctive differences on the basis of existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 15:36; Mark 15:46; Luke 1:52; Luke 23:53; Acts 13:29; Luke 12:18; 2 Corinthians 10:4; Acts 13:19; Acts 19:27


## καθαίρω (id: 002514000000000)

καθαίρω
=======

καθαίρω (G2508)

καθαρός

79\.49 · Features of Objects · Clean, Dirty

to make clean, to cleanse, to clean to cause something to become clean In [JHN 15:2](https://ref.ly/Luke15:2) the meaning of καθαίρω may also be understood as ‘to prune branches’ (see [43\.12](#43.12)), thus playing on two distinct meanings of καθαίρω.

[JHN 15:2](https://ref.ly/Luke15:2)

43\.12 · Agriculture

to take away, to prune, to cut off to cut away or cut back unproductive branches or to cut back productive branches so they can produce better

[JHN 15:2](https://ref.ly/Luke15:2)

* **Associated Passages:** John 15:2


## καθάπερ (id: 002515000000000)

καθάπερ
=======

καθάπερ (G2509)

cj

64\.15 · Comparison

just as, precisely as an emphatic marker of comparison between events and states1

[ROM 4:6](https://ref.ly/Acts4:6) · [ROM 12:4](https://ref.ly/Acts12:4) · [1CO 10:10](https://ref.ly/Rom10:10) · [1CO 12:12](https://ref.ly/Rom12:12) · [2CO 1:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:14) · [2CO 3:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:13) · [2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18) · [2CO 8:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:11) · [1TH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Col2:11) · [1TH 3:6](https://ref.ly/Col3:6) · [1TH 3:12](https://ref.ly/Col3:12) · [1TH 4:5](https://ref.ly/Col4:5) · [HEB 4:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:2)

1 It may be of interest to note that in Greek NT manuscripts καθάπερ and καθώσπερ are often alternative forms. As in the case of ὥσπερ and ὡσπερεί ([64\.13](#64.13)) in contrast with ὡς\[a] and ὡσεί\[a] ([64\.12](#64.12)), so καθάπερ and καθώσπερ appear to be somewhat more emphatic than καθά and καθώς\[c] ([64\.14](#64.14)).

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 4:6; Romans 12:4; 1 Corinthians 10:10; 1 Corinthians 12:12; 2 Corinthians 1:14; 2 Corinthians 3:13; 2 Corinthians 3:18; 2 Corinthians 8:11; 1 Thessalonians 2:11; 1 Thessalonians 3:6; 1 Thessalonians 3:12; 1 Thessalonians 4:5; Hebrews 4:2

ἅπτω

## καθαρίζω (id: 002517000000000)

καθαρίζω
========

καθαρίζω (G2511)

ἀκαθαρσία · ἀκάθαρτος · διακαθαίρω · διακαθαρίζω · ἐκκαθαίρω · καθαρισμός · καθαρός · καθαρότης · περικάθαρμα

79\.49 · Features of Objects · Clean, Dirty

to make clean, to cleanse, to clean to cause something to become clean

[MAT 23:25](https://ref.ly/Matt23:25) · [MAT 23:26](https://ref.ly/Matt23:26) · [MRK 7:19](https://ref.ly/Matt7:19) · [LUK 11:39](https://ref.ly/Mark11:39) · [EPH 5:26](https://ref.ly/Gal5:26) · [JAS 4:8](https://ref.ly/Heb4:8)

53\.28 · Religious Activities · Purify, Cleanse

to cleanse, to purify to cleanse from ritual contamination or impurity The set of terms having the stem καθαρ appears to focus upon the elimination of ritual impurities. From an anthropological standpoint, this means the elimination of ritual contamination, or, in other words, negative taboo. This series of terms with the stem καθαρ appears to contrast with ἁγνίζω\[a] and ἁγνισμός\[a], ἁγιασμός\[b], and ἅγιος\[b] ([53\.44](#53.44), [53\.45](#53.45), [53\.46](#53.46)) focus upon a positive state of consecration and dedication to God and may be regarded as reflecting the acquisition of so\-called positive taboo, that is to say, a state of holiness.\|In [ACT 10:15](https://ref.ly/John10:15) the cleansing obviously involves not physical cleansing, but ritual cleansing, that is to say, the elimination of so\-called negative taboo or ritual defilement.\|ἐκαθαρίσθη αὐτοῦ ἡ λέπρα ‘his leprosy was cleansed’ [MAT 8:3](https://ref.ly/Matt8:3): The cleansing or healing of leprosy involved religious, physiological, and sociological implications. Since leprosy was regarded as a defilement and hence made a person ritually unacceptable, it also meant excommunication from normal social life. The removal of leprosy was regarded as an important religious matter, and the healing had to be verified by the priests before an individual was regarded as ritually cleansed. In a number of languages, however, it is quite impossible to speak of ‘cleansing a leper,’ for this would mean only ‘giving a bath to a leper.’ Accordingly, it may be essential to say ‘to heal a leper’ or ‘to cure a leper’ or even ‘to make a person’s leprosy disappear.’ In such instances it is usually essential to have some kind of marginal note or glossary explanation so as to indicate the religious implications of leprosy and the resulting ritual defilement.

[MAT 23:26](https://ref.ly/Matt23:26) · [MAT 8:3](https://ref.ly/Matt8:3) · [MAT 8:3](https://ref.ly/Matt8:3) · [ACT 10:15](https://ref.ly/John10:15) · [ACT 11:9](https://ref.ly/John11:9) · [ACT 15:9](https://ref.ly/John15:9) · [2CO 7:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:1) · [TIT 2:14](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:14) · [HEB 9:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:14) · [HEB 9:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:22) · [HEB 9:23](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:23) · [HEB 10:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:2) · [JAS 4:8](https://ref.ly/Heb4:8) · [1JN 1:7](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:7) · [1JN 1:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:9)

23\.137 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

to heal and make ritually pure, to heal and to make ritually acceptable to heal a person of a disease which has caused ceremonial uncleanness Since καθαρίζω\[c] implies two changes of state, (1\) the healing of a disease and (2\) the making of a person ritually pure or acceptable, it may be necessary in some languages, and particularly in certain contexts, to render καθαρίζω\[c] in a relatively explicit manner, namely, ‘to heal and to make ritually acceptable’ or ‘... ceremonially clean.’

[MAT 8:2](https://ref.ly/Matt8:2) · [MAT 8:3](https://ref.ly/Matt8:3) · [MAT 8:3](https://ref.ly/Matt8:3) · [MAT 10:8](https://ref.ly/Matt10:8) · [MAT 11:5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5) · [MRK 1:40](https://ref.ly/Matt1:40) · [MRK 1:41](https://ref.ly/Matt1:41) · [MRK 1:42](https://ref.ly/Matt1:42) · [LUK 4:27](https://ref.ly/Mark4:27) · [LUK 5:12](https://ref.ly/Mark5:12) · [LUK 5:13](https://ref.ly/Mark5:13) · [LUK 7:22](https://ref.ly/Mark7:22) · [LUK 17:14](https://ref.ly/Mark17:14) · [LUK 17:17](https://ref.ly/Mark17:17)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:25; Matthew 23:26; Mark 7:19; Luke 11:39; Ephesians 5:26; James 4:8; Matthew 8:3; Acts 10:15; Acts 11:9; Acts 15:9; 2 Corinthians 7:1; Titus 2:14; Hebrews 9:14; Hebrews 9:22; Hebrews 9:23; Hebrews 10:2; 1 John 1:7; 1 John 1:9; Matthew 8:2; Matthew 10:8; Matthew 11:5; Mark 1:40; Mark 1:41; Mark 1:42; Luke 4:27; Luke 5:12; Luke 5:13; Luke 7:22; Luke 17:14; Luke 17:17


## καθαρισμός (id: 002518000000000)

καθαρισμός
==========

καθαρισμός (G2512)

noun · καθαρίζω

53\.28 · Religious Activities · Purify, Cleanse

cleansing, purification act of cleansing from ritual contamination or impurity The set of terms having the stem καθαρ appears to focus upon the elimination of ritual impurities. From an anthropological standpoint, this means the elimination of ritual contamination, or, in other words, negative taboo. This series of terms with the stem καθαρ appears to contrast with ἁγνίζω\[a] and ἁγνισμός\[a], ἁγιασμός\[b], and ἅγιος\[b] ([53\.44](#53.44), [53\.45](#53.45), [53\.46](#53.46)) focus upon a positive state of consecration and dedication to God and may be regarded as reflecting the acquisition of so\-called positive taboo, that is to say, a state of holiness.

[MRK 1:44](https://ref.ly/Matt1:44) · [LUK 2:22](https://ref.ly/Mark2:22) · [LUK 5:14](https://ref.ly/Mark5:14) · [JHN 2:6](https://ref.ly/Luke2:6) · [JHN 3:25](https://ref.ly/Luke3:25) · [HEB 1:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:3) · [2PE 1:9](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 1:44; Luke 2:22; Luke 5:14; John 2:6; John 3:25; Hebrews 1:3; 2 Peter 1:9


## καθαρός (id: 002519000000000)

καθαρός
=======

καθαρός (G2513)

adj · καθαρίζω

79\.48 · Features of Objects · Clean, Dirty

clean, clear pertaining to not being dirty

[MAT 23:26](https://ref.ly/Matt23:26) · [MAT 27:59](https://ref.ly/Matt27:59) · [LUK 11:41](https://ref.ly/Mark11:41) · [JHN 13:10](https://ref.ly/Luke13:10) · [JHN 13:10](https://ref.ly/Luke13:10) · [JHN 13:11](https://ref.ly/Luke13:11) · [HEB 10:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:22) · [REV 15:6](https://ref.ly/Jude15:6) · [REV 19:8](https://ref.ly/Jude19:8) · [REV 19:14](https://ref.ly/Jude19:14) · [REV 21:18](https://ref.ly/Jude21:18) · [REV 21:18](https://ref.ly/Jude21:18) · [REV 21:21](https://ref.ly/Jude21:21)

53\.29 · Religious Activities · Purify, Cleanse

clean, pure pertaining to being ritually clean or pure In [LUK 11:41](https://ref.ly/Mark11:41) καθαρός may be rendered in some languages as ‘pure in the eyes of God’ or even ‘right in the eyes of God.’\|In a number of languages there is simply no relationship between physical cleanness and ritual acceptability or purity. Accordingly, it may be necessary to render καθαρός in [LUK 11:41](https://ref.ly/Mark11:41) and similar contexts as ‘acceptable to God’ or ‘good in God’s eyes’ or ‘good as God thinks.’

[MAT 5:8](https://ref.ly/Matt5:8) · [LUK 11:41](https://ref.ly/Mark11:41) · [JHN 15:3](https://ref.ly/Luke15:3) · [ACT 18:6](https://ref.ly/John18:6) · [ACT 20:26](https://ref.ly/John20:26) · [ROM 14:20](https://ref.ly/Acts14:20) · [1TI 1:5](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:5) · [1TI 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:9) · [2TI 1:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:3) · [2TI 2:22](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:22) · [TIT 1:15](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:15) · [TIT 1:15](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:15) · [TIT 1:15](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:15) · [JAS 1:27](https://ref.ly/Heb1:27)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:26; Matthew 27:59; Luke 11:41; John 13:10; John 13:11; Hebrews 10:22; Revelation 15:6; Revelation 19:8; Revelation 19:14; Revelation 21:18; Revelation 21:21; Matthew 5:8; John 15:3; Acts 18:6; Acts 20:26; Romans 14:20; 1 Timothy 1:5; 1 Timothy 3:9; 2 Timothy 1:3; 2 Timothy 2:22; Titus 1:15; James 1:27

53\.28 · Religious Activities · Purify, Cleanse

cleansing, purification act of cleansing from ritual contamination or impurity The set of terms having the stem καθαρ appears to focus upon the elimination of ritual impurities. From an anthropological standpoint, this means the elimination of ritual contamination, or, in other words, negative taboo. This series of terms with the stem καθαρ appears to contrast with ἁγνίζω\[a] and ἁγνισμός\[a], ἁγιασμός\[b], and ἅγιος\[b] ([53\.44](#53.44), [53\.45](#53.45), [53\.46](#53.46)) focus upon a positive state of consecration and dedication to God and may be regarded as reflecting the acquisition of so\-called positive taboo, that is to say, a state of holiness.

## καθέδρα (id: 002521000000000)

καθέδρα
=======

καθέδρα (G2515)

noun · ἑδραῖος

6\.111 · Artifacts · Furniture

seat, stool, chair a piece of furniture used for sitting; differs widely in shape and materials; often made of a wooden or cane frame with the seat woven of reeds or made of wood; with or without a back

[MAT 21:12](https://ref.ly/Matt21:12) · [MAT 23:2](https://ref.ly/Matt23:2) · [MRK 11:15](https://ref.ly/Matt11:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 21:12; Matthew 23:2; Mark 11:15


## καθέζομαι (id: 002522000000000)

καθέζομαι
=========

καθέζομαι (G2516)

ἑδραῖος

17\.12 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Sit

to sit, to sit down, to be seated, sitting to be in a seated position1

[MAT 26:55](https://ref.ly/Matt26:55) · [LUK 2:46](https://ref.ly/Mark2:46) · [JHN 4:6](https://ref.ly/Luke4:6) · [JHN 11:20](https://ref.ly/Luke11:20) · [JHN 20:12](https://ref.ly/Luke20:12) · [ACT 6:15](https://ref.ly/John6:15) · [ACT 20:9](https://ref.ly/John20:9)

1 There are certain technical problems involved in treating the series καθέζομαι, κάθημαι\[a], καθίζω\[a] ([17\.12](#17.12)) and συγκάθημαι, συγκαθίζω\[a] ([17\.13](#17.13)), since there appears to be an alternation in meaning between (1\) being in a position and (2\) assuming such a position. It would be possible to set up two distinct meanings or to assume that the respective forms are essentially ambiguous. In general, however, the participial forms indicate a state of being, while the non\-participial forms imply assuming a particular position of being seated. However, there are certain subtle differences in the tenses of the participial forms, and hence one cannot determine precisely what are the referential distinctions.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:55; Luke 2:46; John 4:6; John 11:20; John 20:12; Acts 6:15; Acts 20:9


## καθεξῆς (id: 002523000000000)

adv · ἔχω

61\.1 · Sequence

in order, in sequence, one after another a sequence of one after another in time, space, or logic The expression ‘from Samuel’ in [ACT 3:24](https://ref.ly/John3:24) seems to include Samuel. Therefore, one may also render [ACT 3:24](https://ref.ly/John3:24) as ‘Samuel and all the prophets who came after him.’

## καθεύδω (id: 002524000000000)

καθεύδω
=======

καθεύδω (G2518)

εὔδω

23\.66 · Physiological Processes and States · Sleep, Waking

to sleep, to be asleep, sleep the state of being asleep In some languages sleep is expressed by an idiom, for example, ‘his soul had wandered away’ or ‘his eyes had disappeared.’ Though an expression such as ‘his soul had wandered away’ might appear in some languages to have misleading theological implications, it really means only ‘to sleep.’

[MAT 8:24](https://ref.ly/Matt8:24) · [MAT 9:24](https://ref.ly/Matt9:24) · [MAT 13:25](https://ref.ly/Matt13:25) · [MAT 25:5](https://ref.ly/Matt25:5) · [MAT 26:40](https://ref.ly/Matt26:40) · [MAT 26:43](https://ref.ly/Matt26:43) · [MAT 26:45](https://ref.ly/Matt26:45) · [MRK 4:27](https://ref.ly/Matt4:27) · [MRK 4:38](https://ref.ly/Matt4:38) · [MRK 5:39](https://ref.ly/Matt5:39) · [MRK 13:36](https://ref.ly/Matt13:36) · [MRK 14:37](https://ref.ly/Matt14:37) · [MRK 14:37](https://ref.ly/Matt14:37) · [MRK 14:40](https://ref.ly/Matt14:40) · [MRK 14:41](https://ref.ly/Matt14:41) · [LUK 8:52](https://ref.ly/Mark8:52) · [LUK 22:46](https://ref.ly/Mark22:46) · [1TH 5:6](https://ref.ly/Col5:6) · [1TH 5:7](https://ref.ly/Col5:7) · [1TH 5:7](https://ref.ly/Col5:7) · [1TH 5:10](https://ref.ly/Col5:10)

23\.104 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

to be dead, to have died (figurative extension of meaning of καθεύδω\[a] ‘to sleep,’ [23\.66](#23.66)) to sleep, as a euphemistic expression for the state of being dead Some translators have attempted to preserve the figure of speech in καθεύδω\[b] and κοιμάομαι\[b] by translating to sleep rather than to have died or to be dead. Such a practice, however, has resulted in misunderstanding in a number of instances and has sometimes led to the doctrine of so\-called soul\-sleep.

[EPH 5:14](https://ref.ly/Gal5:14) · [1TH 5:10](https://ref.ly/Col5:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:24; Matthew 9:24; Matthew 13:25; Matthew 25:5; Matthew 26:40; Matthew 26:43; Matthew 26:45; Mark 4:27; Mark 4:38; Mark 5:39; Mark 13:36; Mark 14:37; Mark 14:40; Mark 14:41; Luke 8:52; Luke 22:46; 1 Thessalonians 5:6; 1 Thessalonians 5:7; 1 Thessalonians 5:10; Ephesians 5:14

to remain, to stay, to reside, to inhabit, to be, to settle to remain for some time in a place, often with the implication of a settled situation

1 There are certain technical problems involved in treating the series καθέζομαι, κάθημαι\[a], καθίζω\[a] ([17\.12](#17.12)) and συγκάθημαι, συγκαθίζω\[a] ([17\.13](#17.13)), since there appears to be an alternation in meaning between (1\) being in a position and (2\) assuming such a position. It would be possible to set up two distinct meanings or to assume that the respective forms are essentially ambiguous. In general, however, the participial forms indicate a state of being, while the non\-participial forms imply assuming a particular position of being seated. However, there are certain subtle differences in the tenses of the participial forms, and hence one cannot determine precisely what are the referential distinctions.

## καθοράω (id: 002535000000000)

καθοράω
=======

καθοράω (G2529)

ὁράω

27\.7 · Learn · Learn

[ROM 1:20](https://ref.ly/Acts1:20)1

1 ROM 1:20 Some persons might insist that καθοράω refers primarily to the sensory act of perception, but since the qualities spoken of in [ROM 1:20](https://ref.ly/Acts1:20) are invisible, obviously the perception is a mental one and not a sensory one. Furthermore, the process of learning about these invisible qualities must be distinguished from the process of understanding, which is introduced in [ROM 1:20](https://ref.ly/Acts1:20) by a form of the verb νοέω (see [32\.2](#32.2)).

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 1:20


## καθότι (id: 002536000000000)

[LUK 1:7](https://ref.ly/Mark1:7) · [LUK 19:9](https://ref.ly/Mark19:9) · [ACT 2:24](https://ref.ly/John2:24) · [ACT 17:31](https://ref.ly/John17:31)

78\.53 · Degree · Up To, As Much As, To the Degree That \[Marked Extent of Degree]

to the degree that, just as in accordance with a degree as specified by the context There may be a number of problems of restructuring in rendering the relationship between clauses marked by καθό\[b], καθώς\[a], and καθότι\[b]. For example, in the case of [1PE 4:13](https://ref.ly/Jas4:13) it may be necessary to translate καθὸ κοινωνεῖτε τοῖς τοῦ Χριστοῦ παθήμασιν χαίρετε as ‘how much you share Christ’s sufferings is how much you can rejoice.’

[ACT 2:45](https://ref.ly/John2:45) · [ACT 4:35](https://ref.ly/John4:35)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:7; Luke 19:9; Acts 2:24; Acts 17:31; Acts 2:45; Acts 4:35

to the degree that, just as in accordance with a degree as specified by the context There may be a number of problems of restructuring in rendering the relationship between clauses marked by καθό\[b], καθώς\[a], and καθότι\[b]. 89\.86 · Relations · Manner

how, in what manner a marker of an event indicating how something took place

[ACT 15:14](https://ref.ly/John15:14) · [3JN 1:3](https://ref.ly/2John1:3)

## καθώσπερ (id: 002538000000000)

καθώσπερ
========

καθώσπερ (G2509a)

cj

64\.15 · Comparison

just as, precisely as an emphatic marker of comparison between events and states1

[HEB 5:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:4)

1 It may be of interest to note that in Greek NT manuscripts καθάπερ and καθώσπερ are often alternative forms. As in the case of ὥσπερ and ὡσπερεί ([64\.13](#64.13)) in contrast with ὡς\[a] and ὡσεί\[a] ([64\.12](#64.12)), so καθάπερ and καθώσπερ appear to be somewhat more emphatic than καθά and καθώς\[c] ([64\.14](#64.14)).

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 5:4

89\.93 · Relations · Addition

and, and also, also, in addition, even a marker of an additive relation which is not coordinate

91\.1 · Discourse Markers · Markers of Transition

and, then a marker of a new sentence, but often best left untranslated or reflected in the use of ‘and’ or the conjunctive adverb ‘then.’

89\.102 · Relations · Addition

**Collocation:** καί … καί · τε … καί · τε καί

both ... and a marker of a totality of two closely related elements The double use of καί in [MRK 9:13](https://ref.ly/Matt9:13) may merely reflect a Semitic tendency.

10:34](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:34)

1 MAT 8:33 In [MAT 8:33](https://ref.ly/Matt8:33) the phrase καὶ τὰ τῶν δαιμονιζομένων is semantically a part of what was told. It is not, however, coordinate but dependent, in that it forms only a part of the entire account. From the standpoint of the people who announced what had happened, the focus was evidently upon the loss of the herd of pigs, and the healing of the demoniacs was an additional, less important factor. Accordingly, one must treat καί in this structure as being a marker of a non\-coordinate relation.

## Καϊάφας (id: 002540000000000)

Καϊάφας
=======

Καϊάφας (G2533)

noun nom

93\.205 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Caiaphas the high priest who played a prominent role in the condemnation of Jesus

[MAT 26:3](https://ref.ly/Matt26:3) · [MAT 26:57](https://ref.ly/Matt26:57) · [LUK 3:2](https://ref.ly/Mark3:2) · [JHN 11:49](https://ref.ly/Luke11:49) · [JHN 18:13](https://ref.ly/Luke18:13) · [JHN 18:14](https://ref.ly/Luke18:14) · [JHN 18:24](https://ref.ly/Luke18:24) · [JHN 18:28](https://ref.ly/Luke18:28) · [ACT 4:6](https://ref.ly/John4:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:3; Matthew 26:57; Luke 3:2; John 11:49; John 18:13; John 18:14; John 18:24; John 18:28; Acts 4:6

Κάϊν
====

noun nom

93\.206 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

## καινός (id: 002543000000000)

καινός
======

καινός (G2537) — καινότερον

adj · ἀνακαινίζω · ἀνακαινόω · ἐγκαίνια · ἐγκαινίζω · καινότης · καίνωσις

67\.115 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

new, recent pertaining to having been in existence for only a short time

[MAT 13:52](https://ref.ly/Matt13:52) · [MAT 27:60](https://ref.ly/Matt27:60) · [MRK 2:22](https://ref.ly/Matt2:22) · [MRK 14:25](https://ref.ly/Matt14:25) · [LUK 22:20](https://ref.ly/Mark22:20) · [JHN 19:41](https://ref.ly/Luke19:41)

58\.71 · Nature, Class, Example · New, Old \[primarily non\-temporal]

new pertaining to that which is new or recent and hence superior to that which is old1

[MAT 9:17](https://ref.ly/Matt9:17) · [MAT 26:29](https://ref.ly/Matt26:29) · [MRK 2:21](https://ref.ly/Matt2:21) · [MRK 2:22](https://ref.ly/Matt2:22) · [LUK 5:36](https://ref.ly/Mark5:36) · [LUK 5:36](https://ref.ly/Mark5:36) · [LUK 5:36](https://ref.ly/Mark5:36) · [LUK 5:38](https://ref.ly/Mark5:38) · [1CO 11:25](https://ref.ly/Rom11:25) · [2CO 3:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:6) · [2CO 5:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:17) · [2CO 5:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:17) · [GAL 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:15) · [EPH 2:15](https://ref.ly/Gal2:15) · [EPH 4:24](https://ref.ly/Gal4:24) · [HEB 8:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:8) · [HEB 8:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:13) · [HEB 9:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:15) · [2PE 3:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:13) · [2PE 3:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:13) · [REV 2:17](https://ref.ly/Jude2:17) · [REV 3:12](https://ref.ly/Jude3:12) · [REV 3:12](https://ref.ly/Jude3:12) · [REV 5:9](https://ref.ly/Jude5:9) · [REV 14:3](https://ref.ly/Jude14:3) · [REV 21:1](https://ref.ly/Jude21:1) · [REV 21:1](https://ref.ly/Jude21:1) · [REV 21:2](https://ref.ly/Jude21:2) · [REV 21:5](https://ref.ly/Jude21:5)

28\.33 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

previously unknown, previously unheard of, new pertaining to not being well known previously but being significant

[MRK 1:27](https://ref.ly/Matt1:27)2 · [MRK 16:17](https://ref.ly/Matt16:17) · [JHN 13:34](https://ref.ly/Luke13:34) · [ACT 17:19](https://ref.ly/John17:19) · [ACT 17:21](https://ref.ly/John17:21) · [HEB 8:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:8) · [1JN 2:7](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:7) · [1JN 2:8](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:8) · [2JN 1:5](https://ref.ly/1John1:5)

67\.28 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Other Points of Time: Before, Long Ago, Now, At the Same Time, When, About, After

latest, newest pertaining to a point of time preceding another point of time, with a relatively short interval and with the implication of something different

[ACT 17:21](https://ref.ly/John17:21)

1 Some persons see in the use of καινός in contrast with νέος a distinction based upon that which is novel and different in contrast with that which is young and recent. Though this distinction may be applicable to certain contexts and is more in accordance with classical usage, it is not possible to find in all occurrences of καινός and νέος this type of distinction. 2 MRK 1:27 It is possible to treat καινός in [MRK 1:27](https://ref.ly/Matt1:27) as meaning ‘different’ and therefore related to Subdomain F Different Kind or Class in Domain 58 Nature, Class, Example. The phrase κατ᾽ ἐξουσίαν in [MRK 1:27](https://ref.ly/Matt1:27) may be related to the following statement about commanding unclean spirits.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:52; Matthew 27:60; Mark 2:22; Mark 14:25; Luke 22:20; John 19:41; Matthew 9:17; Matthew 26:29; Mark 2:21; Luke 5:36; Luke 5:38; 1 Corinthians 11:25; 2 Corinthians 3:6; 2 Corinthians 5:17; Galatians 6:15; Ephesians 2:15; Ephesians 4:24; Hebrews 8:8; Hebrews 8:13; Hebrews 9:15; 2 Peter 3:13; Revelation 2:17; Revelation 3:12; Revelation 5:9; Revelation 14:3; Revelation 21:1; Revelation 21:2; Revelation 21:5; Mark 1:27; Mark 16:17; John 13:34; Acts 17:19; Acts 17:21; 1 John 2:7; 1 John 2:8; 2 John 1:5


## καινότης (id: 002544000000000)

καινότης
========

καινότης (G2538)

noun · καινός

67\.101 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

newness the state of being relatively recent, with the implication of being appropriately contemporary

[ROM 7:6](https://ref.ly/Acts7:6)

58\.70 · Nature, Class, Example · New, Old \[primarily non\-temporal]

newness the state of being new and different, with the implication of superiority

[ROM 6:4](https://ref.ly/Acts6:4)1

1 ROM 6:4 Though in [ROM 6:4](https://ref.ly/Acts6:4) the focal semantic component is upon the distinctive superiority of the newness, there are contexts in which καινότης is primarily temporal in significance (see [67\.101](#67.101)).

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 7:6; Romans 6:4


## καίπερ (id: 002545000000000)

καίπερ
======

καίπερ (G2539)

cj

89\.71 · Relations · Concession

although, though, even though a marker of concession In some languages concession is marked not by a particle attached to the so\-called concessive clause, but by marking an unexpected contrast in the related clause. For example, the expression in [HEB 5:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:8) may be rendered in some languages as ‘he was God’s Son, but nevertheless he learned to be obedient,’ and the expression in [2PE 1:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:12) may be rendered as ‘you already know these matters, but nevertheless I will always remind you of them.’

[PHP 3:4](https://ref.ly/Eph3:4) · [HEB 5:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:8) · [HEB 7:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:5) · [HEB 12:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:17) · [2PE 1:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Philippians 3:4; Hebrews 5:8; Hebrews 7:5; Hebrews 12:17; 2 Peter 1:12


## καιρός (id: 002546000000000)

καιρός
======

καιρός (G2540)

noun · ἀκαιρέομαι · ἀκαίρως · εὐκαιρέω · εὐκαιρία · εὔκαιρος · εὐκαίρως · πρόσκαιρος

67\.1 · Time · A Point of Time without Reference to Other Points of Time: Time, Occasion, Ever, Often

time, occasion points of time consisting of occasions for particular events In a number of languages there is no general term for ‘time’ or ‘occasion.’ In some contexts it is simply not necessary to have such a term. For example, in rendering [MAT 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) one may translate ‘when the harvest comes, I will say to the reapers’ or ‘when people begin to harvest, I will say to the reapers.’ In other contexts, a term which normally refers to some unit is employed in a generic sense, as in the case of Greek ὥρα which means literally ‘hour’ but is frequently used as a generic expression for a point of time, as in [MAT 8:13](https://ref.ly/Matt8:13). In [ACT 7:17](https://ref.ly/John7:17) χρόνος may often be rendered by a generic expression such as ‘day,’ for example, ‘when it was almost the day for God to keep his promise.’ In the case of [MAT 26:45](https://ref.ly/Matt26:45), the nearness of the time may be indicated as ‘very soon the Son of Man will be handed over.’\|Though it seems quite ordinary in English for one to speak of ‘time coming’ or ‘... drawing near,’ this type of figurative usage is impossible in many languages. The equivalent may be simply ‘will soon be’ or ‘is about to happen.’ The expression οὔπω ἥκει ἡ ὥρα μου (literally ‘my time has not yet come’) in [JHN 2:4](https://ref.ly/Luke2:4) denotes that it is not yet the occasion for a particular event (see καιρός in [JHN 7:8](https://ref.ly/Luke7:8) and compare [JHN 7:10](https://ref.ly/Luke7:10)) but that it will soon be. In these contexts the expression may be rendered as ‘there is still time’ or ‘I will soon do it.’ In [JHN 7:30](https://ref.ly/Luke7:30) and [JHN 8:20](https://ref.ly/Luke8:20) (οὔπω ἐληλύθει ἡ ὥρα αὐτοῦ ‘his time has not yet come’) the reference is to the occasion of his eventual arrest, implying that it will indeed happen.

[MAT 8:29](https://ref.ly/Matt8:29) · [MAT 11:25](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25) · [MAT 12:1](https://ref.ly/Matt12:1) · [MAT 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) · [MAT 21:34](https://ref.ly/Matt21:34) · [MAT 21:41](https://ref.ly/Matt21:41) · [MAT 24:45](https://ref.ly/Matt24:45) · [MAT 26:18](https://ref.ly/Matt26:18) · [MRK 1:15](https://ref.ly/Matt1:15) · [MRK 11:13](https://ref.ly/Matt11:13) · [MRK 12:2](https://ref.ly/Matt12:2) · [MRK 13:33](https://ref.ly/Matt13:33) · [LUK 1:20](https://ref.ly/Mark1:20) · [LUK 4:13](https://ref.ly/Mark4:13) · [LUK 8:13](https://ref.ly/Mark8:13) · [LUK 12:42](https://ref.ly/Mark12:42) · [LUK 13:1](https://ref.ly/Mark13:1) · [LUK 19:44](https://ref.ly/Mark19:44) · [LUK 20:10](https://ref.ly/Mark20:10) · [LUK 21:24](https://ref.ly/Mark21:24) · [LUK 21:36](https://ref.ly/Mark21:36) · [ACT 1:7](https://ref.ly/John1:7) · [ACT 7:20](https://ref.ly/John7:20) · [ACT 14:17](https://ref.ly/John14:17) · [ACT 24:25](https://ref.ly/John24:25) · [ROM 5:6](https://ref.ly/Acts5:6) · [ROM 9:9](https://ref.ly/Acts9:9) · [ROM 11:5](https://ref.ly/Acts11:5) · [ROM 13:11](https://ref.ly/Acts13:11) · [1CO 4:5](https://ref.ly/Rom4:5) · [2CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:2) · [2CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:2) · [GAL 6:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:9) · [EPH 6:18](https://ref.ly/Gal6:18) · [1TH 5:1](https://ref.ly/Col5:1) · [2TH 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:6) · [1TI 2:6](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:6) · [1TI 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:15) · [2TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:3) · [2TI 4:6](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:6) · [TIT 1:3](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:3) · [HEB 9:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:9) · [1PE 1:11](https://ref.ly/Jas1:11) · [1PE 4:17](https://ref.ly/Jas4:17) · [1PE 5:6](https://ref.ly/Jas5:6)

67\.78 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

time, period of time an indefinite unit of time (the actual extent of time being determined by the context)1

[MAT 14:1](https://ref.ly/Matt14:1) · [ACT 12:1](https://ref.ly/John12:1) · [ACT 13:11](https://ref.ly/John13:11) · [ACT 19:23](https://ref.ly/John19:23) · [ROM 3:26](https://ref.ly/Acts3:26) · [2CO 8:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:14) · [GAL 4:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:10) · [EPH 2:12](https://ref.ly/Gal2:12) · [2TI 3:1](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:1) · [HEB 9:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:9) · [HEB 9:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:10) · [HEB 11:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:11) · [HEB 11:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:15) · [REV 12:12](https://ref.ly/Jude12:12) · [REV 12:14](https://ref.ly/Jude12:14) · [REV 12:14](https://ref.ly/Jude12:14) · [REV 12:14](https://ref.ly/Jude12:14)

22\.45 · Trouble, Hardship, Relief, Favorable Circumstances · Favorable Circumstances or State

opportunity, good occasion a favorable opportunity or occasion in view of propitious circumstances It is possible to interpret καιρός in [ACT 24:25](https://ref.ly/John24:25) merely as an ‘occasion’ (see [67\.1](#67.1)). In fact, one may translate simply as ‘and when I have time, I will call you.’

[JHN 7:6](https://ref.ly/Luke7:6) · [JHN 7:6](https://ref.ly/Luke7:6) · [JHN 7:8](https://ref.ly/Luke7:8) · [ACT 24:25](https://ref.ly/John24:25) · [ROM 5:6](https://ref.ly/Acts5:6) · [GAL 6:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:10) · [EPH 5:16](https://ref.ly/Gal5:16) · [COL 4:5](https://ref.ly/Phil4:5) · [HEB 11:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:15)

67\.109 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

not long, temporary, for a little while, for a while pertaining to a relatively short period of time, with emphasis upon the temporary nature of the event or state

[LUK 8:13](https://ref.ly/Mark8:13) · [1CO 7:5](https://ref.ly/Rom7:5)

67\.109 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** πρὸς καιρὸν ὥρας

not long, temporary, for a little while, for a while pertaining to a relatively short period of time, with emphasis upon the temporary nature of the event or state

[1TH 2:17](https://ref.ly/Col2:17)

1 χρόνος\[a] and καιρός\[b] denote essentially a duration of time, but without specified limits. One may, however, speak of a duration as simply a period of time, but this does not imply a unit such as hour, year, or generation.

93\.208 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Caesar, the Emperor the Greek transcription for a Latin word used as a name and title for a Roman emperor

[MAT 22:17](https://ref.ly/Matt22:17) · [MAT 22:21](https://ref.ly/Matt22:21) · [MAT 22:21](https://ref.ly/Matt22:21) · [MAT 22:21](https://ref.ly/Matt22:21) · [MRK 12:14](https://ref.ly/Matt12:14) · [MRK 12:16](https://ref.ly/Matt12:16) · [MRK 12:17](https://ref.ly/Matt12:17) · [MRK 12:17](https://ref.ly/Matt12:17) · [LUK 2:1](https://ref.ly/Mark2:1) · [LUK 3:1](https://ref.ly/Mark3:1) · [LUK 20:22](https://ref.ly/Mark20:22) · [LUK 20:24](https://ref.ly/Mark20:24) · [LUK 20:25](https://ref.ly/Mark20:25) · [LUK 20:25](https://ref.ly/Mark20:25) · [LUK 23:2](https://ref.ly/Mark23:2) · [JHN 19:12](https://ref.ly/Luke19:12) · [JHN 19:12](https://ref.ly/Luke19:12) · [JHN 19:15](https://ref.ly/Luke19:15) · [ACT 17:7](https://ref.ly/John17:7) · [ACT 25:8](https://ref.ly/John25:8) · [ACT 25:10](https://ref.ly/John25:10) · [ACT 25:11](https://ref.ly/John25:11) · [ACT 25:12](https://ref.ly/John25:12) · [ACT 25:12](https://ref.ly/John25:12) · [ACT 25:21](https://ref.ly/John25:21) · [ACT 26:32](https://ref.ly/John26:32) · [ACT 27:24](https://ref.ly/John27:24) · [ACT 28:19](https://ref.ly/John28:19) · [PHP 4:22](https://ref.ly/Eph4:22)

37\.74 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

the Emperor a title for the Roman Emperor In a number of languages it is not easy to distinguish between terms for rulers such as ‘governor,’ ‘king,’ and ‘emperor.’ Sometimes one can only attempt a measure of distinction by indicating relative power or dominion. For example, ‘emperor’ may be rendered as ‘the great ruler’ or ‘the most important chief of all.’

## καίω (id: 002551000000000)

καίω
====

καίω (G2545)

ἐκκαίομαι · κάμινος · κατακαίω · καῦμα · καυματίζω · καῦσις · καυσόομαι · καυστηριάζω · καύσων · ὁλοκαύτωμα

14\.63 · Physical Events and States · Burning

to burn, burning, to be on fire the process of burning In a number of languages important distinctions are made in the use of terms for burning. For example, the burning of a substance for light, as in the case of a lamp or candle, may be indicated by a term quite different from an expression indicating the destruction or burning up of something. Similarly, the burning of wood for cooking may require still another term. The extent or size of the fire involved may also require some distinctions in terms for burning.

[LUK 12:35](https://ref.ly/Mark12:35) · [LUK 24:32](https://ref.ly/Mark24:32) · [JHN 5:35](https://ref.ly/Luke5:35) · [JHN 15:6](https://ref.ly/Luke15:6) · [HEB 12:18](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:18) · [REV 4:5](https://ref.ly/Jude4:5) · [REV 8:8](https://ref.ly/Jude8:8) · [REV 8:10](https://ref.ly/Jude8:10) · [REV 19:20](https://ref.ly/Jude19:20) · [REV 21:8](https://ref.ly/Jude21:8)

14\.65 · Physical Events and States · Burning

to ignite, to kindle, to set ablaze, to start a fire, to light a lamp to cause the process of burning to begin As already noted in the series of terms listed in [14\.63](#14.63), languages differ appreciably in terms employed for different phases and results of burning. For example, to set something on fire for the sake of providing warmth may be expressed by quite a different term from that which is used in speaking of the process of setting something on fire in order to destroy it.\|In a number of languages one must not speak of ‘a lamp burning’ or ‘to burn a lamp,’ for this would imply burning up a lamp or destroying it. It may therefore be necessary to say ‘to cause the wick of a lamp to burn’ or ‘to light the wick of a lamp,’ and instead of saying ‘the lamp burns,’ one may say ‘the lamp gives light’ or ‘the lamp shows a flame.’

[MAT 5:15](https://ref.ly/Matt5:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 12:35; Luke 24:32; John 5:35; John 15:6; Hebrews 12:18; Revelation 4:5; Revelation 8:8; Revelation 8:10; Revelation 19:20; Revelation 21:8; Matthew 5:15


## κἀκεῖ (id: 002552000000000)

## κάκωσις (id: 002567000000000)

κάκωσις (G2561)

noun · κακόω

20\.12 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

mistreatment, oppression act of causing harm or injury to someone or something (a highly generic meaning involving a wide range of harm and injury) In translating terms meaning ‘to harm’ or ‘to injure,’ it may be necessary to specify suffering, for example, ‘to cause people to suffer’ or ‘to cause people to have pain.’\|In some languages it may be necessary to translate this expression in [ACT 7:34](https://ref.ly/John7:34) as passive, for example, ‘I have seen the harm done to my people in Egypt’ or, in the active form, ‘I have seen how the people in Egypt harmed my people.’

## καλάμη (id: 002568000000000)

καλάμη
======

καλάμη (G2562)

noun · κάλαμος

3\.58 · Plants · Non\-Fruit Parts of Plants

straw, thatch the dry stalks of grain or reeds κάλαμος It is difficult in [1CO 3:12](https://ref.ly/Rom3:12) to know precisely the distinction between χόρτον ‘grass’ and καλάμην ‘straw.’ It would seem clear that καλάμην would be less valuable than χόρτον, and this might be a reference to the use of straw as a very poor thatching material. On the other hand, it could be understood as a reference to the use of straw in place of grass in the making of sun\- dried bricks.

[1CO 3:12](https://ref.ly/Rom3:12)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 3:12


## κάλαμος (id: 002569000000000)

κάλαμος
=======

κάλαμος (G2563)

noun · καλάμη

3\.19 · Plants · Plants That Are Not Trees

reed a tall straight grass or sedge; growing in or near rivers and marshes

[MAT 11:7](https://ref.ly/Matt11:7) · [LUK 7:24](https://ref.ly/Mark7:24)

3\.55 · Plants · Non\-Fruit Parts of Plants

reed the stalk of a reed plant In some discussions of κάλαμος\[b] the meaning is given as cane, but the term cane must not be confused with the meaning of walking stick. In [MRK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:19) it may be important in some languages to use a phrase such as heavy reed or strong reed, in order to avoid the impression that the instrument used in striking Jesus was some flimsy or fragile stalk of a plant.

[MAT 12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20) · [MAT 27:29](https://ref.ly/Matt27:29) · [MAT 27:30](https://ref.ly/Matt27:30) · [MAT 27:48](https://ref.ly/Matt27:48) · [MRK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:19) · [MRK 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36)

6\.56 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

pen a reed especially cut for making marks with ink on writing material; abou 20 cm long, sharpened on one end

[3JN 1:13](https://ref.ly/2John1:13)

6\.213 · Artifacts · Instruments for Measuring

measuring rod a rod (possibly a reed) used for measuring length There is no indication as to the particular length of κάλαμος\[d], but it could have been as much as two meters (about seven feet), since this would not have been an unusual length for a reed. The equivalent of κάλαμος\[d] may be simply ‘a measuring stick’ or ‘a stick with which to count the distance.’

[REV 11:1](https://ref.ly/Jude11:1) · [REV 21:15](https://ref.ly/Jude21:15) · [REV 21:16](https://ref.ly/Jude21:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:7; Luke 7:24; Matthew 12:20; Matthew 27:29; Matthew 27:30; Matthew 27:48; Mark 15:19; Mark 15:36; 3 John 1:13; Revelation 11:1; Revelation 21:15; Revelation 21:16

33\.129 · Communication · Name

to call, to name to speak of a person or object by means of a proper name

33\.131 · Communication · Name

to call, to name to use an attribution in speaking of a person It is not always possible to determine from the context whether the act involved is an initial naming of a person or simply calling a person by a particular name. Likewise in the case of attributions or titles, it is not always possible to determine whether it is a matter of giving an attribution or title to a person or simply a matter of speaking of or to a person by means of such an attribution or title. In some instances the giving of a title may be made indirect. For example, in [MAT 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) the statement ‘and they will call his name Emmanuel’ suggests the giving of a title, but the process is stated in terms of how people will speak of this person.

[MAT 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) · [MAT 5:9](https://ref.ly/Matt5:9) · [MAT 5:19](https://ref.ly/Matt5:19) · [MAT 5:19](https://ref.ly/Matt5:19) · [MAT 21:13](https://ref.ly/Matt21:13) · [MAT 22:43](https://ref.ly/Matt22:43) · [MAT 22:45](https://ref.ly/Matt22:45) · [MAT 23:7](https://ref.ly/Matt23:7) · [MAT 23:8](https://ref.ly/Matt23:8) · [MAT 23:9](https://ref.ly/Matt23:9) · [MAT 23:10](https://ref.ly/Matt23:10) · [MRK 11:17](https://ref.ly/Matt11:17) · [LUK 1:32](https://ref.ly/Mark1:32) · [LUK 1:35](https://ref.ly/Mark1:35) · [LUK 1:36](https://ref.ly/Mark1:36) · [LUK 1:76](https://ref.ly/Mark1:76) · [LUK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Mark2:23) · [LUK 6:15](https://ref.ly/Mark6:15) · [LUK 6:46](https://ref.ly/Mark6:46) · [LUK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Mark15:19) · [LUK 15:21](https://ref.ly/Mark15:21) · [LUK 19:29](https://ref.ly/Mark19:29) · [LUK 20:44](https://ref.ly/Mark20:44) · [LUK 21:37](https://ref.ly/Mark21:37) · [LUK 22:25](https://ref.ly/Mark22:25) · [LUK 23:33](https://ref.ly/Mark23:33) · [JHN 1:42](https://ref.ly/Luke1:42) · [ACT 8:10](https://ref.ly/John8:10) · [ROM 9:7](https://ref.ly/Acts9:7) · [ROM 9:25](https://ref.ly/Acts9:25) · [ROM 9:26](https://ref.ly/Acts9:26) · [1CO 15:9](https://ref.ly/Rom15:9) · [HEB 2:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:11) · [HEB 3:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:13) · [HEB 11:18](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:18) · [JAS 2:23](https://ref.ly/Heb2:23) · [1PE 3:6](https://ref.ly/Jas3:6) · [1JN 3:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:1) · [REV 11:8](https://ref.ly/Jude11:8) · [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) · [REV 19:11](https://ref.ly/Jude19:11) · [REV 19:13](https://ref.ly/Jude19:13)

33\.307 · Communication · Call

to call, to summon to communicate directly or indirectly to someone who is presumably at a distance, in order to tell such a person to come1

[MAT 2:7](https://ref.ly/Matt2:7) · [MAT 2:15](https://ref.ly/Matt2:15) · [MAT 9:13](https://ref.ly/Matt9:13) · [MAT 20:8](https://ref.ly/Matt20:8) · [MAT 22:3](https://ref.ly/Matt22:3) · [MAT 25:14](https://ref.ly/Matt25:14) · [MRK 2:17](https://ref.ly/Matt2:17) · [MRK 3:31](https://ref.ly/Matt3:31) · [LUK 5:32](https://ref.ly/Mark5:32) · [LUK 19:13](https://ref.ly/Mark19:13) · [ACT 4:18](https://ref.ly/John4:18) · [ACT 24:2](https://ref.ly/John24:2) · [HEB 9:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:15) · [1PE 2:9](https://ref.ly/Jas2:9) · [1PE 5:10](https://ref.ly/Jas5:10)

33\.312 · Communication · Call

to call, to call to a task to urgently invite someone to accept responsibilities for a particular task, implying a new relationship to the one who does the calling2 It is rare that one can translate καλέω\[d], κλῆσις\[a], and προσκαλέω\[b] as simply ‘to call’ in the sense of ‘to speak to someone at a distance and tell them to come.’ For example, in [2TH 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:14) it may be necessary to render the above clause as ‘through the good news we preached, which summoned you to do this.’ Similarly, in [ACT 16:10](https://ref.ly/John16:10) one may translate ‘because God has urgently invited us to preach the good news to the people there.’

κάλυμμα
=======

noun · καλύπτω

6\.177 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

veil a piece of material worn over the face, thin enough for the wearer to see through, but not for observers to recognize facial features through it The cloth of a veil would be sufficiently thin that the wearer would be able to see through it, but others would find it difficult to recognize the features through the veil.

28\.79 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

to hide, to keep secret, to conceal to cause something not to be known1

[MAT 10:26](https://ref.ly/Matt10:26) · [2CO 4:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:3) · [2CO 4:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:3)

1 The series of meanings in [28\.79](#28.79) differs significantly from the meaning of ἐγκρύπτω in [85\.50](#85.50). In [28\.79](#28.79) the focus in concealment is upon preventing knowledge about something, while in [85\.50](#85.50) the concealment focuses upon something being in a place where it is no longer visible.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:24; Luke 8:16; Luke 23:30; James 5:20; 1 Peter 4:8; Matthew 10:26; 2 Corinthians 4:3


## καλῶς (id: 002578000000000)

καλῶς
=====

καλῶς (G2573)

adv · καλός

88\.4 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Goodness

good, fine, praiseworthy pertaining to a positive moral quality, with the implication of being favorably valued

[MAT 12:12](https://ref.ly/Matt12:12) · [LUK 6:27](https://ref.ly/Mark6:27) · [ACT 10:33](https://ref.ly/John10:33) · [1CO 7:37](https://ref.ly/Rom7:37) · [1CO 7:38](https://ref.ly/Rom7:38) · [2CO 11:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:4) · [GAL 4:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:17) · [PHP 4:14](https://ref.ly/Eph4:14) · [1TI 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:17) · [HEB 13:18](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:18) · [JAS 2:8](https://ref.ly/Heb2:8) · [JAS 2:19](https://ref.ly/Heb2:19) · [3JN 1:6](https://ref.ly/2John1:6)

65\.23 · Value · Good, Bad

fine, well, good, excellent, well done pertaining to events which measure up to their intended purpose In the [65\.23](#65.23) contexts, βελτίων, καλῶς\[b], εὖ\[b], and εὖγε occur in highly elliptical constructions.

[MRK 7:37](https://ref.ly/Matt7:37) · [MRK 12:32](https://ref.ly/Matt12:32) · [MRK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Matt16:18) · [LUK 6:26](https://ref.ly/Mark6:26) · [LUK 6:48](https://ref.ly/Mark6:48) · [1TI 3:4](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:4) · [1TI 3:12](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:12) · [1TI 3:13](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:13)

72\.12 · True, False · Accurate, Inaccurate

accurate, correctly, right pertaining to being accurate and right, with a possible implication of being commendable

[MAT 15:7](https://ref.ly/Matt15:7) · [MRK 7:6](https://ref.ly/Matt7:6) · [MRK 12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28) · [MRK 12:32](https://ref.ly/Matt12:32) · [LUK 20:39](https://ref.ly/Mark20:39) · [JHN 4:17](https://ref.ly/Luke4:17) · [JHN 8:48](https://ref.ly/Luke8:48) · [JHN 13:13](https://ref.ly/Luke13:13) · [JHN 18:23](https://ref.ly/Luke18:23) · [ACT 28:25](https://ref.ly/John28:25) · [ROM 11:20](https://ref.ly/Acts11:20) · [GAL 5:7](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:7) · [2PE 1:19](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:19)

87\.25 · Status · High Status or Rank \[including persons of high status]

high, important, fine pertaining to having high status, with the possible implication of its attractiveness It is also possible that καλῶς in [JAS 2:3](https://ref.ly/Heb2:3) has the meaning of a polite invitation, translatable as ‘please!’ (see [33\.177](#33.177)).

[JAS 2:3](https://ref.ly/Heb2:3)

33\.177 · Communication · Ask For, Request

please a marker of polite request For another interpretation of καλῶς in [JAS 2:3](https://ref.ly/Heb2:3), see [87\.25](#87.25).

[JAS 2:3](https://ref.ly/Heb2:3)

78\.21 · Degree · Much, Little \[Positive\-Negative Degree]

certainly, very well a positive degree (and even more emphatic in the comparative form κάλλιον) with an implication of correctness

[MRK 7:9](https://ref.ly/Matt7:9) · [1CO 14:17](https://ref.ly/Rom14:17)

23\.129 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

**Collocation:** καλῶς ἔχω

to be well, to be healthy (an idiom, literally: to have well) the state of being healthy, well (in contrast with sickness) In a number of languages health is expressed only in terms of strength, for ‘to be well’ is ‘to be strong.’ In other languages, however, to be well or to be healthy is a negation of illness or sickness, so that in [MRK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Matt16:18) one may translate ‘they will place their hands on those who are sick and these people will become not sick.’

[MRK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Matt16:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:12; Luke 6:27; Acts 10:33; 1 Corinthians 7:37; 1 Corinthians 7:38; 2 Corinthians 11:4; Galatians 4:17; Philippians 4:14; 1 Timothy 5:17; Hebrews 13:18; James 2:8; James 2:19; 3 John 1:6; Mark 7:37; Mark 12:32; Mark 16:18; Luke 6:26; Luke 6:48; 1 Timothy 3:4; 1 Timothy 3:12; 1 Timothy 3:13; Matthew 15:7; Mark 7:6; Mark 12:28; Luke 20:39; John 4:17; John 8:48; John 13:13; John 18:23; Acts 28:25; Romans 11:20; Galatians 5:7; 2 Peter 1:19; James 2:3; Mark 7:9; 1 Corinthians 14:17


## κάμηλος (id: 002579000000000)

κάμηλος
=======

κάμηλος (G2574)

noun

4\.30 · Animals · Animals

camel large quadruped mammal; Camelus dromedarius and Camelus bactrianus; bactrians may reach 2 m.; dromedaries are bigger and a uniform light fawn color; bactrians are darker; suited to life in desert areas; store excess food in their humps, can go without water for long periods; can make long journeys through dry areas; used for riding and for carrying heavy loads and pulling carts; hair woven into cloth used for making tents or outer robes; milk used as food and drink; symbol of wealth and commerce In most areas where camels are not known, a term for ‘camel’ has been borrowed from a dominant language. In other instances people may have constructed descriptive phrases. For example, in Timorese the first two expressions suggested for camel were ‘the horse with a crooked back’ or ‘the long\-legged horse,’ but finally people settled upon a more satisfactory rendering, namely, ‘the horse of the desert.’ In a number of languages a camel is simply called ‘the big humped animal.’ In a number of cases, however, it may be useful to have some kind of a description of a camel in a glossary or word list.\|In referring to the camel’s hair garment worn by John the Baptist, there are two problems. In the first place, it is important to translate the phrase ‘garment of camel’s hair’ in such a way as to indicate that the garment was made of cloth woven out of camel’s hair and did not consist of the entire skin nor of camel’s hair stuck onto John the Baptist’s body. In the second place, it is important to indicate that this camel’s hair garment was a kind of rough garment, since in a number of languages an expression such as ‘camel’s hair coat’ would refer to an expensive, luxury garment. See also [6\.216](#6.216).

[MAT 3:4](https://ref.ly/Matt3:4) · [MAT 19:24](https://ref.ly/Matt19:24) · [MAT 23:24](https://ref.ly/Matt23:24) · [MRK 1:6](https://ref.ly/Matt1:6) · [MRK 10:25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:25) · [LUK 18:25](https://ref.ly/Mark18:25)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:4; Matthew 19:24; Matthew 23:24; Mark 1:6; Mark 10:25; Luke 18:25


## κάμινος (id: 002580000000000)

κάμινος
=======

κάμινος (G2575)

noun · καίω

7\.73 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

furnace, kiln a construction used for the smelting of ore and burning of ceramic ware In [MAT 13:42](https://ref.ly/Matt13:42) and [MAT 13:50](https://ref.ly/Matt13:50) κάμινος is used figuratively of hell.\|In rendering the meaning of κάμινος, the emphasis should be upon the extreme heat, rather than upon the particular type of construction.

[MAT 13:42](https://ref.ly/Matt13:42) · [MAT 13:50](https://ref.ly/Matt13:50) · [REV 1:15](https://ref.ly/Jude1:15) · [REV 9:2](https://ref.ly/Jude9:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:42; Matthew 13:50; Revelation 1:15; Revelation 9:2


## καμμύω (id: 002581000000000)

καμμύω
======

καμμύω (G2576)

27\.50 · Learn · Be Willing To Learn

**Collocation:** καμμύω τοὺς ὀφθαλμούς

to refuse to learn, to refuse to recognize (an idiom, literally: to close the eyes) to be unwilling to learn and to evaluate something fairly In a number of languages there is a problem involved in a literal rendering of ‘to close the eyes,’ since this may be understood in a strictly literal sense or as denoting death.

## κάμνω (id: 002582000000000)

κάμνω
=====

κάμνω (G2577)

23\.142 · Physiological Processes and States · Sickness, Disease, Weakness

to be sick, to be very sick to be ill, with a possible implication of being worn\-out or wasting away As in the case of expressions for health and vigor, it may also be necessary in some languages to specify more precisely the nature of the illness, disease, or weakness. Often the context provides a clue, but in some instances this is not possible, in which case it is important to try to employ a term for sickness or illness which will be the most generalized.

[JAS 5:15](https://ref.ly/Heb5:15)

25\.291 · Attitudes and Emotions · Discouragement

**Collocation:** κάμνω τῇ ψυχῇ

to become discouraged, to become tired of (an idiom, literally: to become tired in spirit) to gradually lose one’s motivation to accomplish some goal

[HEB 12:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:3) · [JAS 5:15](https://ref.ly/Heb5:15)

* **Associated Passages:** James 5:15; Hebrews 12:3


## κάμπτω (id: 002583000000000)

κάμπτω
======

κάμπτω (G2578)

ἀνακάμπτω · συγκάμπτω

53\.61 · Religious Activities · Worship, Reverence

**Collocation:** κάμπτω τὸ γόνυ

to worship, to bow before (a Semitic idiom, literally: the knee bends, or: the knee bows) to bend or bow the knee as a symbol of religious devotion1

[ROM 11:4](https://ref.ly/Acts11:4) · [ROM 14:11](https://ref.ly/Acts14:11) · [EPH 3:14](https://ref.ly/Gal3:14) · [PHP 2:10](https://ref.ly/Eph2:10)

1 One may also interpret the idiom κάμπτω τὸ γόνυ as consisting of a metonymy in the case of τὸ γόνυ (in other words, knee as a substitute for person). Accordingly, κάμπτω to bend or to bow could then be interpreted as meaning simply to worship.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 11:4; Romans 14:11; Ephesians 3:14; Philippians 2:10

## Καναναῖος (id: 002586000000000)

Καναναῖος
=========

Καναναῖος (G2581a)

noun nom

11\.88 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

zealot, nationalist (the Aramaic equivalent of ζηλωτής\[b] and not in any way related to the geographical terms Cana or Canaan): a member of a Jewish nationalistic group seeking independence from Rome It is possible that ζηλωτής in [LUK 6:15](https://ref.ly/Mark6:15) and Καναναῖος in [MAT 10:4](https://ref.ly/Matt10:4) function not so much as a designation of an individual belonging to the particular Jewish nationalistic party (according to some scholars such a party may not have been organized at that time), but of one whjo is simply zealous for national independence (see ζηλωτής\[a] ‘enthusiast, zealous person,’ [25\.77](#25.77)). Therefore, one might speak of Simon as ‘Simon the patriot’ (the same applies to [ACT 1:13](https://ref.ly/John1:13), the only other occurrence of ζηλωτής\[b] in the NT). To render ζηλωτής\[b] as ‘armed insurrectionist’ or ‘guerilla fighter’ (as some translators have suggested) would be reading into the text more than is specifically warranted.

[MAT 10:4](https://ref.ly/Matt10:4) · [MRK 3:18](https://ref.ly/Matt3:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:4; Mark 3:18

## καρδία (id: 002592000000000)

καρδία
======

καρδία (G2588)

noun · καρδιογνώστης · σκληροκαρδία

26\.3 · Psychological Faculties

heart, inner self, mind (a figurative extension of meaning of καρδία ‘heart,’ not occurring in the NT in its literal sense) the causative source of a person’s psychological life in its various aspects, but with special emphasis upon thoughts1 It is often possible to render καρδία\[a] by a number of different terms depending upon the immediate context, for example, ‘mind,’ ‘intention,’ ‘purpose,’ or ‘desire.’ In many languages it is quite impossible to use a term meaning ‘heart,’ since such a term may not lend itself to figurative extension in meaning. Often the equivalent of καρδία is ‘liver,’ while in a number of languages it is ‘stomach’ or ‘bowels.’

## καρπός (id: 002594000000000)

καρπός
======

καρπός (G2590)

noun · ἄκαρπος · καρποφορέω

3\.33 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

fruit any fruit part of plants, including grain as well as pulpy fruit A number of languages distinguish between different kinds of fruit. One common type of four\-way distinction involves (1\) nuts, (2\) grain, (3\) pulpy fruit surrounding a seed (the type of fruit primarily referred to in contexts containing καρπός\[a]), and (4\) fruit such as bananas, in which there is no noticeable seed. It is important in each instance to choose a term which will be applicable to the particular context.

[MAT 3:10](https://ref.ly/Matt3:10) · [MAT 7:17](https://ref.ly/Matt7:17) · [MAT 7:17](https://ref.ly/Matt7:17) · [MAT 7:18](https://ref.ly/Matt7:18) · [MAT 7:18](https://ref.ly/Matt7:18) · [MAT 7:19](https://ref.ly/Matt7:19) · [MAT 12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33) · [MAT 12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33) · [MAT 12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33) · [MAT 13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8) · [MAT 13:26](https://ref.ly/Matt13:26) · [MAT 21:19](https://ref.ly/Matt21:19) · [MRK 4:7](https://ref.ly/Matt4:7) · [MRK 4:8](https://ref.ly/Matt4:8) · [MRK 11:14](https://ref.ly/Matt11:14) · [LUK 3:9](https://ref.ly/Mark3:9) · [LUK 6:43](https://ref.ly/Mark6:43) · [LUK 6:43](https://ref.ly/Mark6:43) · [LUK 6:44](https://ref.ly/Mark6:44) · [LUK 8:8](https://ref.ly/Mark8:8) · [LUK 13:6](https://ref.ly/Mark13:6) · [LUK 13:7](https://ref.ly/Mark13:7) · [LUK 13:9](https://ref.ly/Mark13:9) · [JHN 12:24](https://ref.ly/Luke12:24) · [JHN 15:2](https://ref.ly/Luke15:2) · [JHN 15:2](https://ref.ly/Luke15:2) · [JHN 15:2](https://ref.ly/Luke15:2) · [JHN 15:4](https://ref.ly/Luke15:4) · [1CO 9:7](https://ref.ly/Rom9:7) · [REV 22:2](https://ref.ly/Jude22:2) · [REV 22:2](https://ref.ly/Jude22:2)

13\.86 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Exist

**Collocation:** ποιέω καρπόν

to produce results, to cause results (an idiom, literally: to make fruit) to cause results to exist

[MAT 3:8](https://ref.ly/Matt3:8) · [LUK 3:8](https://ref.ly/Mark3:8)

1 By setting up certain highly generic meanings for βλαστάνω, δίδωμι, ἀποδίδωμι, and ποιέω, it would be possible to treat the phrase compounds in this series as being semantically endocentric. However, it seems more satisfactory to regard them as what might be called low\-grade idioms with specialized meanings of the semantically head expressions.

67\.33 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Other Points of Time: Before, Long Ago, Now, At the Same Time, When, About, After

90\.29 · Case · Guarantor Participant with Oaths

by, in the name of (with the genitive) a marker of a supernatural person or force called upon to guarantee the carrying out of an oath or vow Depending upon the context, it may be necessary to be quite specific in some languages in marking the relations between swearing and the supernatural power invoked to guarantee the fulfillment of an oath. For example, in swearing that something is true, it may be necessary to translate ‘I swear that this is true and call upon God to punish me if it is not true,’ or if the swearing involves a promise, then one may translate ‘I promise to do this, but if I do not, may God punish me.’

[MAT 26:63](https://ref.ly/Matt26:63) · [HEB 6:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:13) · [HEB 6:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:16)

56\.10 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Accusation

**Collocation:** κατὰ λόγον ἀνέχομαι

to accept a complaint in court, to admit a complaint to judgment (an idiom, literally: to accept in accordance with a charge) to accept a complaint against someone for a legal review It is also possible to understand the expression κατὰ λόγον ἀνέχομαι in [ACT 18:14](https://ref.ly/John18:14) not as an idiom, but as meaning ‘to be reasonably patient with.’ See [25\.171](#25.171) and [89\.18](#89.18).

[ACT 18:14](https://ref.ly/John18:14)

63\.16 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Part

**Collocation:** κατὰ μέρος

in detail, one item after another (an idiom, literally: in accordance with a part) pertaining to an activity which proceeds part by part

[HEB 9:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:5)

58\.51 · Nature, Class, Example · Distinctive, Unique

**Collocation:** κατὰ μόνας

alone, all by oneself (an idiom, literally: throughout only places) the only item of a class in a place

[MRK 4:10](https://ref.ly/Matt4:10) · [LUK 9:18](https://ref.ly/Mark9:18)

83\.38 · Spacial Positions · In Front Of, Face To Face, In Back Of, Behind

**Collocation:** κατὰ πρόσωπον

face to face, in person, to one’s face (an idiom, literally: according to face) the position of one person facing another, with or without the implication of opposition

[ACT 25:16](https://ref.ly/John25:16) · [2CO 10:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:1) · [GAL 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:11)

89\.56 · Relations · Purpose

**Collocation:** κατὰ σκοπὸν διώκω

to strive toward a goal, to press on with the purpose of (an idiom, literally: to pursue to a goal, to press toward a goal) to strive energetically for some purpose

[PHP 3:14](https://ref.ly/Eph3:14)

31\.31 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Suppose, Think Possible

**Collocation:** τὰ κατὰ πρόσωπον

outward appearance, what things seem to be (an idiom, literally: those things according to the face) that which seems to be so

[2CO 10:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:7)

1 κατά\[e] differs in meaning from μέσος\[a], ἀνὰ μέσον\[a],ἐντός\[a], εν\[b], μετά\[h], εἰς\[e], ἐπί\[c], πρός\[d], and παρά\[b] ([83\.9](#83.9)) in that the focus of meaning is upon distribution rather than upon inclusion within any defined area or set. 2 ACT 27:5 It is possible that κατά in [ACT 27:5](https://ref.ly/John27:5) refers to a position parallel with the coast and possibly involving a type of extension. 3 The difference in meaning between the set κατά\[g], ἐπί\[s], ἐν\[s], ἐκ\[k], and καθώς\[d] and the set πότε, ποτέ\[b], ὁπότε, ὅτε\[a], and ὅταν\[b] ([67\.30](#67.30)) is largely a matter of class meanings, but there may be certain subtle rhetorical differences as well. 4 It would seem that the meanings of items in subdomains [70\.1](#70.1)\-[70\.4](#70.4) (ὅλως\[b], ὄντως, ἀληθής\[b], ἀληθινός\[a], ἀληθῶς, and idioms with ἀλήθεια) do reflect certain subtle differences, but it is not at all easy to determine precisely how they differ. 5 It is possible to interpret κατ ἰδίαν as being primarily an element of setting, that is to say, without the presence of other persons, but in some contexts the focus seems to shift from setting to the fact that such events take place without the general knowledge of the public. Depending therefore upon the context, one may render κατ ἰδίαν by such expressions as without others knowing or without other people being present.

## καταβαίνω (id: 002602000000000)

καταβαίνω
=========

καταβαίνω (G2597)

βαίνω

15\.107 · Linear Movement · Come/Go Down, Descend

to move down, to come down, to go down, to descend to move down, irrespective of the gradient In a number of languages there is a series of terms for going down or descending, depending upon the gradient and the rapidity with which someone or something descends. There may also be distinct terms depending upon the extent of the descent. Rain coming down would be regarded as an extensive descent, while getting out of a boat to walk on the water would be a very limited descent.\|Movement downward may, of course, involve more than physical objects, for example, οὐκ ἔστιν αὕτη ἡ σοφία ἄνωθεν κατερχομένη ‘this is not the wisdom that comes down from above’ [JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15). Since in [JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15) ἄνωθεν is a substitute for God, it may be necessary to restructure this statement as ‘this wisdom does not come from God’ or ‘God is not the source of this wisdom.’

## καταβάλλω (id: 002603000000000)

καταβάλλω
=========

καταβάλλω (G2598) — καταβάλλομαι

βάλλω

19\.10 · Physical Impact · Hit, Strike

to knock down to hit or strike with sufficient impact so as to knock an object down It is possible to interpret καταβάλλω in [2CO 4:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:9) as meaning ‘to hurt badly’ (see [20\.21](#20.21)).

[2CO 4:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:9)

20\.21 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

to hurt badly, to cause to suffer considerably to cause someone to suffer considerable pain or injury It is possible that in [2CO 4:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:9) καταβάλλω should be understood as ‘to knock down’ (see [19\.10](#19.10)).

[2CO 4:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:9)

85\.49 · Existence in Space · Put, Place

to put down, to lay to put or place something down, with the implication of permanence

[HEB 6:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:1)1

1 HEB 6:1 The context of καταβάλλομαι in [HEB 6:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:1) is, of course, figurative.

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 4:9; Hebrews 6:1


## καταβαπτίζω (id: 002604000000000)

καταβαπτίζω
===========

καταβαπτίζω

53\.31 · Religious Activities · Purify, Cleanse

to wash, to purify, washing, purification to wash (in some contexts, possibly by dipping into water), with a view to making objects ritually acceptable See [MRK 7:4](https://ref.ly/Matt7:4) apparatus.\|
There is some doubt as to the precise extent to which βαπτίζω, καταβαπτίζω, and βαπτισμός in [MRK 7:4](https://ref.ly/Matt7:4) involve ritual cleansing, but the context would seem to imply this, particularly in view of the relationship of such washing to the rules followed by Jews in general and Pharisees in particular.

[MRK 7:4](https://ref.ly/Matt7:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 7:4


## καταβαρέω (id: 002605000000000)

βαρέω

22\.26 · Trouble, Hardship, Relief, Favorable Circumstances · Cause Trouble, Hardship

to overburden, to cause undue hardship to overburden someone by causing undue hardship The meaning of ‘to cause undue hardship’ or ‘to overburden someone’ may be expressed in some languages as ‘to cause more trouble to someone than that person should have’ or ‘to cause more suffering than what is right.’

[2CO 12:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:16)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 12:16

**Collocation:** ἦσαν οἱ ὀφθαλμοὶ καταβαρυνόμενοι

to have become very sleepy, to be very sleepy (an idiom, literally: their eyes were weighed down) to become excessively or exceedingly sleepy In some languages the equivalent of ἦσαν οἱ ὀφθαλμοὶ βεβαρημένοι (or καταβαρυνόμενοι) would be ‘they could no longer keep their eyes open’ or ‘they could not drive sleep away.’

## κατάβασις (id: 002607000000000)

κατάβασις
=========

κατάβασις (G2600)

noun · βαίνω

15\.109 · Linear Movement · Come/Go Down, Descend

slope, descent (derivative of καταβαίνω ‘to move down, to descend,’ [15\.107](#15.107)) the slope or declivity of an object which one may descend ἐγγίζοντος δὲ αὐτοῦ ἤδη πρὸς τῇ καταβάσει τοῦ Ὄρους τῶν Ἐλαιῶν ‘he was already approaching the slope of the Mount of Olives’ or ‘he was already approaching the descent of the Mount of Olives’ [LUK 19:37](https://ref.ly/Mark19:37). The latter translation could represent the means of descent, namely, ‘the road leading down from the Mount of Olives.’

[LUK 19:37](https://ref.ly/Mark19:37)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 19:37

15\.108 · Linear Movement · Come/Go Down, Descend

to bring down, to make go down to cause to move down This word is only found in three variant readings: ἐκ δὲ τοῦ ὄχλου κατεβίβασαν Ἀλέξανδρονπροβαλόντων αὐτὸν τῶν Ἰουδαίων ‘some of the crowd brought Alexander down, since he had been put forward by the Jews’ [ACT 19:33](https://ref.ly/John19:33) (apparatus); ἕως ᾅδου καταβιβασθήσω ‘you will be brought down to hell’ [MAT 11:23](https://ref.ly/Matt11:23) (apparatus). ## καταβολή (id: 002609000000000)

καταβολή
========

καταβολή (G2602)

noun · βάλλω

42\.37 · Perform, Do · Make, Create

creation creation, particularly of the world, with focus upon the beginning phase

[MAT 13:35](https://ref.ly/Matt13:35) · [MAT 25:34](https://ref.ly/Matt25:34) · [LUK 11:50](https://ref.ly/Mark11:50) · [JHN 17:24](https://ref.ly/Luke17:24) · [EPH 1:4](https://ref.ly/Gal1:4) · [HEB 4:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:3) · [HEB 9:26](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:26) · [1PE 1:20](https://ref.ly/Jas1:20) · [REV 13:8](https://ref.ly/Jude13:8) · [REV 17:8](https://ref.ly/Jude17:8)

23\.49 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

**Collocation:** καταβολὴ σπέρματος

to conceive, to become pregnant an idiom, literally: sowing of seed In many languages the process of becoming pregnant is expressed in different ways: ‘to begin to become large,’ ‘to receive sperm,’ ‘to let a child enter,’ or ‘to stop bleeding’ (a reference to the cessation of menstrual periods).\|There are a number of textual problems involved in this expression in [HEB 11:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:11), and many scholars have concluded that the reference is not to Sarah’s conceiving but to Abraham’s being able to become a father (see Today’s English Version).

[HEB 11:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:11)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:35; Matthew 25:34; Luke 11:50; John 17:24; Ephesians 1:4; Hebrews 4:3; Hebrews 9:26; 1 Peter 1:20; Revelation 13:8; Revelation 17:8; Hebrews 11:11

## καταγγέλλω (id: 002612000000000)

καταγγέλλω
==========

καταγγέλλω (G2605)

ἀγγέλλω

## κατακαυχάομαι (id: 002631000000000)

κατακαυχάομαι
=============

κατακαυχάομαι (G2620)

καυχάομαι

33\.370 · Communication · Boast

to boast against, to degrade to boast about something by downgrading something else In many languages it may not be possible to use an expression such as ‘to boast against.’ Therefore, in rendering μὴ κατακαυχῶ τῶν κλάδων in [ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18) one may use ‘you must not say that you are so much better than the branches.’ For another interpretation of κατακαυχάομαι in [ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18), see [88\.194](#88.194).

[ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18) · [ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18) · [JAS 3:14](https://ref.ly/Heb3:14)

88\.194 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Despise, Scorn, Contempt

to despise, to look down on to despise, with the implication of regarding oneself as superior For another interpretation of κατακαυχάομαι in [ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18), see [33\.370](#33.370).

[ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18) · [ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18) · [JAS 3:14](https://ref.ly/Heb3:14)

74\.11 · Able, Capable

to be more powerful than, to triumph over to have greater power or potential than The reference to ‘mercy’ and ‘judgment’ in [JAS 2:13](https://ref.ly/Heb2:13) must be related to God’s mercy and judgment.\|In a number of languages it is not possible to personify mercy and judgment, and therefore one must relate these two expressions to God, for example, ‘the extent to which God shows mercy is even more than the way in which he judges’ or ‘God shows mercy even more than he judges.’

[JAS 2:13](https://ref.ly/Heb2:13)

## κατάκειμαι (id: 002632000000000)

κατάκειμαι
==========

κατάκειμαι (G2621)

κεῖμαι

17\.27 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Lie

to lie, lying down to lie down, often with the implication of some degree of incapacity

[MRK 1:30](https://ref.ly/Matt1:30) · [MRK 2:4](https://ref.ly/Matt2:4) · [LUK 5:25](https://ref.ly/Mark5:25) · [JHN 5:3](https://ref.ly/Luke5:3) · [JHN 5:6](https://ref.ly/Luke5:6) · [ACT 9:33](https://ref.ly/John9:33) · [ACT 28:8](https://ref.ly/John28:8)

17\.23 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Recline \[to eat]

to recline, to eat, to be at table, to eat, to dine, to sit down to eat to be in a reclining position as one eats (with the focus either upon the position or the act of eating) For the interpretation of ἀνάκειμαι and κατάκειμαι focusing upon eating, see [23\.21](#23.21).

[MRK 2:15](https://ref.ly/Matt2:15) · [MRK 14:3](https://ref.ly/Matt14:3)

23\.21 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

to eat a meal to eat a meal, with possible reference to the fact of the people reclining to eat1 In biblical times there were apparently three different positions involved in the eating of a meal. People might, for example, (1\) be seated on cushions around a low table or (2\) be seated on chairs around a table or (3\) recline on couches facing a table. Meals which involved reclining on couches would normally have been more elaborate, but the verbs ἀνάκειμαι\[b] and κατάκειμαι\[c] have been generalized in meaning to denote the eating of a meal without necessarily specifying the particular reclining position of those who participated in the meal.\|For the translator, it may be extremely awkward to speak of ‘reclining to eat,’ since this may have connotations of people who are too lazy to sit up at the table or who are too sick to partake of an ordinary meal. It is for that reason that instead of rendering ἀνάκειμαι\[b] or κατάκειμαι\[c] as ‘to recline to eat,’ translators use expressions such as ‘to sit down to eat’ or ‘to eat a meal.’

[LUK 5:29](https://ref.ly/Mark5:29) · [LUK 7:37](https://ref.ly/Mark7:37) · [1CO 8:10](https://ref.ly/Rom8:10)

1 One would assume that ἀνάκειμαι\[b] and κατάκειμαι\[c] would have almost opposite meanings in view of the prefixes ἀνα and κατα. It is, of course, possible that ἀνάκειμαι\[b] refers to being propped up on a couch where one was eating and κατάκειμαι\[c] refers specifically to reclining, that is to say, lying down, but the contexts in which these two expressions occur do not provide a clear basis for such a distinction in meaning. In fact, the two are largely generalized to simply mean to eat a meal, though their etymological history may be significantly different. See also Domain 17, footnote 8\.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 1:30; Mark 2:4; Luke 5:25; John 5:3; John 5:6; Acts 9:33; Acts 28:8; Mark 2:15; Mark 14:3; Luke 5:29; Luke 7:37; 1 Corinthians 8:10

1 The series κατακρίνω, κατάκρισις, and κατάκριμα probably differs slightly in meaning from καταδικάζω and καταδίκη in that the first series focuses more upon the actual process of judging rather than upon the verdict, but it is not possible to determine this from existing NT contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:41; Matthew 12:42; Matthew 20:18; Matthew 27:3; Mark 10:33; Mark 14:64; Mark 16:16; Luke 11:31; Luke 11:32; John 8:10; Romans 2:1; Romans 8:3; Romans 8:34; Romans 14:23; 1 Corinthians 11:32; Hebrews 11:7; 2 Peter 2:6

[1TH 5:4](https://ref.ly/Col5:4)

1 It is difficult to determine the extent to which καταλαμβάνω\[e] should be classified as a figurative extension of meaning. ## καταλλαγή (id: 002654000000000)

καταλλαγή
=========

καταλλαγή (G2643)

noun · ἀλλάσσω

40\.1 · Reconciliation, Forgiveness · Reconciliation

to reconcile, to make things right with one another, reconciliation to reestablish proper friendly interpersonal relations after these have been disrupted or broken (the componential features of this series of meanings involve (1\) disruption of friendly relations because of (2\) presumed or real provocation (3\) overt behavior designed to remove hostility, and (4\) restoration of original friendly relations)1 Because of the variety and complexity of the components involved in reconciliation, it is often necessary to use an entire phrase in order to communicate satisfactorily the meanings of the terms in this subdomain. In some languages, however, reconciliation is often spoken of in idiomatic terms, for example, ‘to cause to become friends again,’ ‘to cause to snap fingers again’ (a symbol of friendly interpersonal relations in many parts of Africa), ‘to cause to be one again,’ or ‘to take away the separation.’ A particularly crucial element in terms for reconciliation is the assigning of responsibility for original guilt in causing the estrangement. Some terms, for example, imply that the individual who initiates reconciliation is by doing so admitting his guilt in causing the estrangement. This, of course, provides a completely untenable meaning for reconciliation in speaking of God reconciling people to himself through Christ.\|In a number of languages the contextual basis for an expression for reconciliation is often found in terms relating to the reconciliation of husbands and wives. Such expressions fit in well with many contexts in the Scriptures, especially in speaking of reconciliation of people to God, since God is frequently referred to as the husband and the believers as the wife.

[ROM 5:11](https://ref.ly/Acts5:11) · [ROM 11:15](https://ref.ly/Acts11:15) · [2CO 5:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:18) · [2CO 5:19](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:19)

1 It may be that there are certain subtle distinctions of meaning in the series in [40\.1](#40.1), but there appears to be no contextual indication to justify setting up completely separate meanings.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 5:11; Romans 11:15; 2 Corinthians 5:18; 2 Corinthians 5:19
