## κατανεύω (id: 002664000000000)

κατανεύω
========

κατανεύω (G2656)

νεύω

33\.485 · Communication · Non\-Verbal Communication

to gesture, to motion, to nod, to beckon to signal to someone by means of part of the body, especially by means of the head or hands1 In a number of languages it is necessary to be quite specific with regard to types of gestures or motions of the head or hands and arms. For example, in [JHN 13:24](https://ref.ly/Luke13:24) there is an obvious question involved, and this may require in some languages a particular signal by means of the hands or face. The same would be true in the case of [LUK 1:62](https://ref.ly/Mark1:62). In [LUK 1:22](https://ref.ly/Mark1:22) the gesture would have to be something which would explain or indicate Zechariah’s inability to speak, while in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) quite another gesture would no doubt be called for, since the persons involved were at quite a distance from one another.

[LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning between νεύω, ἐννεύω, διανεύω, and κατανεύω, but such distinctions are not evident from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 5:7

καταντάω
========

καταντάω (G2658)

ἀντάω

15\.84 · Linear Movement · Come, Come To, Arrive

to come to, to reach, to arrive to move toward and to arrive at a point1

[ACT 16:1](https://ref.ly/John16:1) · [ACT 18:19](https://ref.ly/John18:19) · [ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24) · [ACT 20:15](https://ref.ly/John20:15) · [ACT 21:7](https://ref.ly/John21:7) · [ACT 25:13](https://ref.ly/John25:13) · [ACT 27:12](https://ref.ly/John27:12) · [ACT 28:13](https://ref.ly/John28:13) · [1CO 14:36](https://ref.ly/Rom14:36)

13\.16 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to come to be, to attain, to achieve to attain or arrive at a particular state2

[ACT 26:7](https://ref.ly/John26:7) · [EPH 4:13](https://ref.ly/Gal4:13) · [PHP 3:11](https://ref.ly/Eph3:11)

13\.121 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Happen

to come upon to happen to, with the implication of something definitive and final

[1CO 10:11](https://ref.ly/Rom10:11)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle distinctions of meaning in ἐφικνέομαιφθάνω\[a], καταντάω\[a], and ἥκω\[a], but it is not possible to determine what the distinctive features are on the basis of existing contexts. 2 In the case of meanings involving to attain to a state, there is obviously a change in state implied, but the focus seems to be primarily on the end point, and hence these meanings are classified in this subdomain rather than in the following subdomain.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 16:1; Acts 18:19; Acts 18:24; Acts 20:15; Acts 21:7; Acts 25:13; Acts 27:12; Acts 28:13; 1 Corinthians 14:36; Acts 26:7; Ephesians 4:13; Philippians 3:11; 1 Corinthians 10:11

## καταξιόω (id: 002669000000000)

65\.18 · Value · Worthy, Not Worthy

[LUK 20:35](https://ref.ly/Mark20:35) · [ACT 5:41](https://ref.ly/John5:41) · [2TH 1:5](https://ref.ly/1Thess1:5)

23\.81 · Physiological Processes and States · Tire, Rest

## καταπέτασμα (id: 002673000000000)

καταπέτασμα
===========

καταπέτασμα (G2665)

noun · πέτομαι

6\.160 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

drape, curtain, veil a hanging of cloth over an opening The καταπέτασμα of the Temple has been traditionally called in English a ‘veil,’ but a literal correspondence of ‘veil’ would be misleading, since it would suggest something which merely covers the face. At the same time a typical correspondence of ‘curtain’ could be misleading, since it would suggest something which covers a window. In some languages the most appropriate equivalent for καταπέτασμα in the context of [MAT 27:51](https://ref.ly/Matt27:51) is ‘drape,’ but frequently it is necessary to use some kind of descriptive equivalent, for example, ‘a large piece of cloth hanging down from the ceiling’ or ‘a large piece of cloth covering the entrance.’

[MAT 27:51](https://ref.ly/Matt27:51) · [MRK 15:38](https://ref.ly/Matt15:38) · [LUK 23:45](https://ref.ly/Mark23:45) · [HEB 6:19](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:19) · [HEB 9:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:3) · [HEB 10:20](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:51; Mark 15:38; Luke 23:45; Hebrews 6:19; Hebrews 9:3; Hebrews 10:20

## καταπίνω (id: 002675000000000)

καταπίνω
========

καταπίνω (G2666) — καταπίνομαι

πίνω

23\.45 · Physiological Processes and States · Processes Involving the Mouth, Other Than Eating and Drinking

to swallow to cause something to pass through the mouth and into the stomach The saying about ‘straining out a fly and swallowing a camel’ refers to gross unawareness of inconsistencies in one’s behavior, but in translating it is far better to preserve the intentional hyperbole, since it is one which can be readily grasped. As an aid to the reader, one can refer to the fact that in the list of unclean animals in [LEV 11:0](https://ref.ly/Lev11:0), the fly or gnat is the smallest and the camel is the largest.

[MAT 23:24](https://ref.ly/Matt23:24)

20\.52 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Destroy

to destroy, to ruin completely (a figurative extension of meaning of καταπίνω\[a] ‘to swallow,’ [23\.45](#23.45)) to cause the complete and sudden destruction of someone or something

[HEB 11:29](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:29) · [1PE 5:8](https://ref.ly/Jas5:8)

13\.43 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to cause the end of, to swallow up (a figurative extension of meaning of καταπίνω\[a] ‘to swallow,’ [23\.45](#23.45)) to cause the complete cessation of a state

[1CO 15:54](https://ref.ly/Rom15:54) · [2CO 5:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:4) · [REV 12:16](https://ref.ly/Jude12:16)

25\.285 · Attitudes and Emotions · Sorrow, Regret

**Collocation:** καταπίνομαι λύπῃ

to grieve to the point of giving up, to grieve and despair (an idiom, literally: to be swallowed up by grief) to be so overcome with grief as to despair1

[2CO 2:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:7)

1 In view of the element of despair in the idiom καταπίνομαι λύπω, it would be possible to classify this meaning under Subdomain X Discouragement in Domain 25 Attitudes and Emotions.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:24; Hebrews 11:29; 1 Peter 5:8; 1 Corinthians 15:54; 2 Corinthians 5:4; Revelation 12:16; 2 Corinthians 2:7

76\.26 · Power, Force

to invalidate, to abolish, to cause not to function to render ineffective the power or force of something In rendering this expression in [1CO 1:28](https://ref.ly/Rom1:28) it may be quite necessary to stipulate the reference to τὰ ὄντα, and in this context the contrast between τὰ ὄντα and τὰ μὴ ὄντα may perhaps be best expressed as ‘those things that are not regarded as important in order to abolish those that are regarded as important.’ The rendering of these expressions depends, of course, upon the manner in which the preceding context from verse 26 is rendered.

37\.136 · Control, Rule · Release, Set Free

to be freed, to be released to cause the release from an association with a person or an institution on the basis that the earlier obligation or restriction is no longer relevant or in force In a number of languages it may be difficult to speak of being freed from a law which stipulates the relationship a woman has to her husband. Accordingly, it may be appropriate to translate this statement in [ROM 7:2](https://ref.ly/Acts7:2) as ‘if a woman’s husband dies, the law no longer ties her to her husband’ or even ‘... the law says she is free to marry someone else.’

13\.162 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Happen

noun · κατασκηνόω

6\.146 · Artifacts · Containers

nest a construction built by birds in connection with brooding and raising their young1 It is possible to understand κατασκήνωσις in [MAT 8:20](https://ref.ly/Matt8:20) as simply a sheltered place, but the most natural interpretation would appear to be ‘nest.’

[MAT 8:20](https://ref.ly/Matt8:20) · [LUK 9:58](https://ref.ly/Mark9:58)

1 κατασκήνωσις in the sense of nest is the only artifact in this domain which is not made by humans, but this in no way precludes it from being classified in this domain.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:20; Luke 9:58

## καταφιλέω (id: 002713000000000)

=========

καταφιλέω (G2705)

φιλέω

34\.62 · Association · Kiss, Embrace

to kiss to kiss, either as an expression of greeting or as a sign of special affection and appreciation1 Since in so many societies kissing is not a form of greeting, it may be necessary to add some kind of classifier to contexts such as [MAT 26:48](https://ref.ly/Matt26:48) and [MAT 26:49](https://ref.ly/Matt26:49) in order to indicate clearly the intention involved; otherwise, the use of a term meaning merely ‘to kiss’ might suggest a kind of erotic display. The clause in [MAT 26:49](https://ref.ly/Matt26:49) may be translated as ‘the man I greet by kissing is the one you want.’

1 Though the act of kissing may have different functions, the nature of the event is essentially the same. In some languages, however, a distinction is made between kissing on the cheek and kissing on the lips. Additional distinctions may be made as to whether one is kissing a person of the same sex or of a different sex.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:49; Mark 14:45; Luke 7:38; Luke 7:45; Luke 15:20; Acts 20:37

[ROM 4:15](https://ref.ly/Acts4:15) · [ROM 5:3](https://ref.ly/Acts5:3) · [ROM 7:8](https://ref.ly/Acts7:8) · [ROM 7:13](https://ref.ly/Acts7:13) · [2CO 4:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:17) · [2CO 7:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:10) · [2CO 7:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:11) · [2CO 9:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:11) · [PHP 2:12](https://ref.ly/Eph2:12) · [JAS 1:3](https://ref.ly/Heb1:3)

77\.6 · Ready, Prepared

[2CO 5:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:5)

1 Any meaning involving ‘to cause to be’ implies some change in state, and therefore one could classify these meanings under Subdomain B Change of State in Domain 13 Be, Become, Exist, Happen. However, the focus seems to be primarily upon the changed state rather than upon the process of moving from one state to another. The fact that a change of state has taken place seems to be semantically incidental.

==========

κατέρχομαι (G2718)

ἔρχομαι

15\.107 · Linear Movement · Come/Go Down, Descend

to move down, to come down, to go down, to descend to move down, irrespective of the gradient In a number of languages there is a series of terms for going down or descending, depending upon the gradient and the rapidity with which someone or something descends. There may also be distinct terms depending upon the extent of the descent. Rain coming down would be regarded as an extensive descent, while getting out of a boat to walk on the water would be a very limited descent.\|Movement downward may, of course, involve more than physical objects, for example, οὐκ ἔστιν αὕτη ἡ σοφία ἄνωθεν κατερχομένη ‘this is not the wisdom that comes down from above’ [JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15). Since in [JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15) ἄνωθεν is a substitute for God, it may be necessary to restructure this statement as ‘this wisdom does not come from God’ or ‘God is not the source of this wisdom.’

[LUK 4:31](https://ref.ly/Mark4:31) · [LUK 9:37](https://ref.ly/Mark9:37) · [ACT 8:5](https://ref.ly/John8:5) · [ACT 9:32](https://ref.ly/John9:32) · [ACT 11:27](https://ref.ly/John11:27) · [ACT 12:19](https://ref.ly/John12:19) · [ACT 13:4](https://ref.ly/John13:4) · [ACT 15:1](https://ref.ly/John15:1) · [ACT 15:30](https://ref.ly/John15:30) · [ACT 18:5](https://ref.ly/John18:5) · [ACT 21:10](https://ref.ly/John21:10) · [JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15)

54\.15 · Maritime Activities

to arrive at land, to put in at (technical, nautical term) to go by ship toward the shore

[ACT 18:22](https://ref.ly/John18:22) · [ACT 21:3](https://ref.ly/John21:3) · [ACT 27:5](https://ref.ly/John27:5)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 4:31; Luke 9:37; Acts 8:5; Acts 9:32; Acts 11:27; Acts 12:19; Acts 13:4; Acts 15:1; Acts 15:30; Acts 18:5; Acts 21:10; James 3:15; Acts 18:22; Acts 21:3; Acts 27:5

## κατευθύνω (id: 002727000000000)

κατευθύνω
=========

κατευθύνω (G2720)

εὐθύς

36\.1 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Guide, Lead

to guide, to direct, to lead to so influence others as to cause them to follow a recommended course of action In some languages it is difficult to distinguish readily between expressions for ‘leading’ and those which refer to ‘ruling’ or ‘governing,’ but it is important to try to distinguish clearly between these two different sets of interpersonal relations. In some languages, the concept of ‘leading’ can be expressed by ‘showing how to’ or ‘demonstrating how one ought to.’ In other languages it is possible to speak of ‘leading’ as simply ‘going ahead of,’ but too often such an expression may designate only ‘a scout’ who goes ahead to see whether things are safe, or it may refer only to a person who insists on his prerogative as the most distinguished person in a group.

[1TH 3:11](https://ref.ly/Col3:11) · [2TH 3:5](https://ref.ly/1Thess3:5)

41\.17 · Behavior and Related States · Behavior, Conduct

**Collocation:** κατευθύνω τοὺς πόδας

to guide, to direct, to make to live (an idiom, literally: to guide the feet properly) to guide or direct behavior in an appropriate manner

[LUK 1:79](https://ref.ly/Mark1:79)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Thessalonians 3:11; 2 Thessalonians 3:5; Luke 1:79

37\.17 · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

to control, to restrain to exercise continuous control over someone or something There is usually no difficulty in speaking of ‘control’ if it is performed by a person as in [1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13). However, it may not be possible to speak of ‘death’ having control, unless the language in question can personify death. In some instances [ACT 2:24](https://ref.ly/John2:24) (see [37\.16](#37.16)) must be rendered as ‘it was impossible for him to continue to be dead,’ and in [2CO 5:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:14) ‘Christ’s love controls us’ may be rendered as ‘the fact that Christ loves us causes us to act as we do.’

1 Ownership usually entails to a greater or lesser degree the social sanctions of the right by the owner to use the object in question and the obligation by non\-owners to recognize that right and to desist from such usage. 2 This meaning of have/possess contrasts with hold, grasp (Domain 18\), the whole/part relation (Domain 63\), to be in a relationship to (Domain 89\), to be in a state or condition (Domain 13\), and to have authority, power, or control over persons or objects, either sociologically or physically (Domain 37\).

## κατηχέω (id: 002736000000000)

κατηχέω
=======

κατηχέω (G2727)

ἠχέω

33\.225 · Communication · Teach

to instruct, to teach to teach in a systematic or detailed manner It is also possible to understand κατηχέω in [LUK 1:4](https://ref.ly/Mark1:4) as denoting merely what has been told rather than what has been taught (see κατηχέω\[b], [33\.190](#33.190)). This distinction is an important one since it implies a quite different relationship of Theophilus to the text of the Gospel of Luke. If [LUK 1:4](https://ref.ly/Mark1:4) pertains merely to Theophilus ‘being told’ something, then one might assume that Theophilus was not a Christian, in which case he may have been a government official to whom the joint publications (the Gospel of Luke and the Acts of the Apostles) would have been directed as a defense of Christianity. On the other hand, if one understands κατηχέω in the sense of ‘to be taught’ or ‘to be instructed,’ then one would assume that Theophilus was a Christian who had been instructed in the faith. The relationship of Theophilus to the message would then determine in a number of contexts the difference between ‘we’ inclusive and ‘we’ exclusive.

[LUK 1:4](https://ref.ly/Mark1:4) · [ACT 18:25](https://ref.ly/John18:25) · [ROM 2:18](https://ref.ly/Acts2:18) · [1CO 14:19](https://ref.ly/Rom14:19) · [GAL 6:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:6) · [GAL 6:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:6)

33\.190 · Communication · Inform, Announce

to report, to tell, to in form to report in a relatively detailed manner It is also possible to understand κατηχέω in [LUK 1:4](https://ref.ly/Mark1:4) as systematic teaching (see [33\.225](#33.225)).

[LUK 1:4](https://ref.ly/Mark1:4) · [ACT 21:21](https://ref.ly/John21:21) · [ACT 21:24](https://ref.ly/John21:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:4; Acts 18:25; Romans 2:18; 1 Corinthians 14:19; Galatians 6:6; Acts 21:21; Acts 21:24

## κατοπτρίζω (id: 002744000000000)

κατοπτρίζω
==========

κατοπτρίζω (G2734) — κατοπτρίζομαι

ὀπτρίζομαι

24\.44 · Sensory Events and States · See

to see as in a mirror, to see by reflection to see indirectly or by reflection as in a mirror The phrase ‘as in a mirror’ may be translated in some languages as ‘as though we were looking into a mirror’ or ‘as though what we saw was in a mirror.’ In some languages, however, one does not say ‘in a mirror’ but ‘through a mirror’ or ‘by means of a mirror.’ For another interpretation of κατοπτρίζομαι in [2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18), see [14\.52](#14.52).

[2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18)

14\.52 · Physical Events and States · Light

to reflect to reflect light or visual patterns coming from some source In order to speak of a reflection of light, it may be necessary to say ‘to throw back the light’ or ‘to shine back the form.’ Sometimes it is necessary to stipulate a type of object which reflects such light, for example, ‘we are a shining object that shows back the glory of the Lord.’ For another interpretation of κατοπτρίζομαι in [2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18), see [24\.44](#24.44).

[2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 3:18


## κάτω (id: 002745000000000)

κάτω
====

κάτω (G2736)

adv · κατά

83\.53 · Spacial Positions · Above, Below

below a position immediately or directly below a point of orientation, which is often left implicit In a number of languages it is not possible to speak of something ‘below’ without indicating precisely what is involved, but in the case of [ACT 2:19](https://ref.ly/John2:19) it would be irrelevant to say ‘marvels on the earth below the sky.’ Therefore, one may perhaps most satisfactorily translate this expression in [ACT 2:19](https://ref.ly/John2:19) as ‘marvels here on the earth.’

[MRK 14:66](https://ref.ly/Matt14:66) · [MRK 15:38](https://ref.ly/Matt15:38) · [JHN 8:23](https://ref.ly/Luke8:23) · [ACT 2:19](https://ref.ly/John2:19)

84\.26 · Spacial Extensions · Extension To a Goal

down, down to, below to extension toward a goal which is down or below

[MAT 4:6](https://ref.ly/Matt4:6) · [MAT 27:51](https://ref.ly/Matt27:51) · [LUK 4:9](https://ref.ly/Mark4:9) · [JHN 8:6](https://ref.ly/Luke8:6) · [ACT 20:9](https://ref.ly/John20:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 14:66; Mark 15:38; John 8:23; Acts 2:19; Matthew 4:6; Matthew 27:51; Luke 4:9; John 8:6; Acts 20:9

## καῦμα (id: 002749000000000)

καῦμα
=====

καῦμα (G2738)

noun · καίω

14\.67 · Physical Events and States · Burning

heat, scorching heat heat sufficiently intense to cause suffering or burning In some languages the effect of heat may be described simply as ‘heat will not scorch them’ or ‘they will not suffer because of heat’ ([REV 7:16](https://ref.ly/Jude7:16)). Such expressions, however, may be ambiguous because they might mean that the individuals involved would be able to easily withstand the heat. The meaning of the biblical passage, however, is that there would be no heat to cause them harm.

[REV 7:16](https://ref.ly/Jude7:16) · [REV 16:9](https://ref.ly/Jude16:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 7:16; Revelation 16:9

## καῦσις (id: 002751000000000)

καῦσις
======

καῦσις (G2740)

noun · καίω

14\.63 · Physical Events and States · Burning

to burn, burning, to be on fire the process of burning In a number of languages important distinctions are made in the use of terms for burning. For example, the burning of a substance for light, as in the case of a lamp or candle, may be indicated by a term quite different from an expression indicating the destruction or burning up of something. Similarly, the burning of wood for cooking may require still another term. The extent or size of the fire involved may also require some distinctions in terms for burning.

[HEB 6:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 6:8

89\.53 · Relations · Result

without result, without effect pertaining to being lacking in results In [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14), one may understand purpose rather than result, and hence one can translate ‘our message is indeed without purpose’ (see [89\.64](#89.64)). For yet another interpretation of κενός in [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14), see [72\.10](#72.10).

[1CO 15:10](https://ref.ly/Rom15:10) · [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14) · [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14) · [1CO 15:58](https://ref.ly/Rom15:58) · [2CO 6:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:1) · [GAL 2:2](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:2) · [PHP 2:16](https://ref.ly/Eph2:16) · [PHP 2:16](https://ref.ly/Eph2:16) · [COL 2:8](https://ref.ly/Phil2:8) · [1TH 2:1](https://ref.ly/Col2:1) · [1TH 3:5](https://ref.ly/Col3:5)

89\.64 · Relations · Purpose

in vain, for no purpose pertaining to being totally without purpose For other interpretations of κενός in [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14), see [72\.10](#72.10) and [89\.53](#89.53).

[1CO 15:10](https://ref.ly/Rom15:10) · [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14) · [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14) · [2CO 6:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:1) · [1TH 2:1](https://ref.ly/Col2:1)

72\.10 · True, False · True, False

untrue, lacking in truth pertaining to being untrue in view of lacking truth For other interpretations of κενός in [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14), see [89\.53](#89.53) and [89\.64](#89.64).

[1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14) · [1CO 15:14](https://ref.ly/Rom15:14) · [EPH 5:6](https://ref.ly/Gal5:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 12:3; Luke 1:53; Luke 20:10; Luke 20:11; 1 Thessalonians 2:1; Acts 4:25; James 2:20; 1 Corinthians 15:10; 1 Corinthians 15:14; 1 Corinthians 15:58; 2 Corinthians 6:1; Galatians 2:2; Philippians 2:16; Colossians 2:8; 1 Thessalonians 3:5; Ephesians 5:6

## κέντρον (id: 002771000000000)

κέντρον
=======

κέντρον (G2759)

noun · ἐγκεντρίζω · ἐκκεντέω

8\.45 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

sting, stinger a sharp, pointed projection used in stinging

[REV 9:10](https://ref.ly/Jude9:10)

6\.9 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Agriculture and Husbandry

goad a pointed stick used in driving draft animals In the NT κέντρον\[b] occurs only in the idiom πρὸς κέντρον λακτίζειν 'to kick against the goad;' meaning to hurt oneself by active resistance.1 See [39\.19](#39.19).

[ACT 26:14](https://ref.ly/John26:14)

20\.69 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Kill

power to kill, power to destroy (a figurative extension of meaning of κέντρον\[a] ‘sting,’ [8\.45](#8.45)) the power or ability to kill or destroy For another interpretation of κέντρον in [1CO 15:55](https://ref.ly/Rom15:55), see [24\.86](#24.86).

1 κέντρον also occurs in the meaning of a sharp pointed object (typically a sting, stinger) which may cause pain and even death (see [8\.45](#8.45)).

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 9:10; Acts 26:14; 1 Corinthians 15:55; 1 Corinthians 15:56

## κεραμικός (id: 002776000000000)

κεραμικός
=========

κεραμικός (G2764)

adj · κεραμεύς

2\.19 · Natural Substances · Earth, Mud, Sand, Rock

made of clay, clay (derivative of κέραμος ‘potter’s clay,’ not occurring in the NT) pertaining to being made of potter’s clay In some languages it may seem unduly repetitious to speak of ‘clay pots’ in [REV 2:27](https://ref.ly/Jude2:27) since a term for pot may refer only to objects made of clay. In biblical times, however, some σκεύη were of metal and others were of stone and wood. It may be possible to translate this expression in [REV 2:27](https://ref.ly/Jude2:27) as ‘they shall be broken like pots’ or ‘... like dishes.’

[REV 2:27](https://ref.ly/Jude2:27)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 2:27

## κεράννυμι (id: 002779000000000)

κεράννυμι
=========

κεράννυμι (G2767)

ἀκέραιος · ἄκρατος · συγκεράννυμι

63\.9 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Mix

to mix to mix substances, normally liquids Note that in the process of mixing, the various substances become a single mass, and the constituent parts are indistinguishable. For another interpretation of κεράννυμι in [REV 14:10](https://ref.ly/Jude14:10), see [47\.3](#47.3).

[REV 14:10](https://ref.ly/Jude14:10) · [REV 18:6](https://ref.ly/Jude18:6) · [REV 18:6](https://ref.ly/Jude18:6)

47\.3 · Activities Involving Liquids or Masses · Movement of Liquids or Masses

to pour, to pour out to pour something out Since κεράννυμι normally means ‘to mix,’ it is possible to interpret the participial form κεκερασμένου in [REV 14:10](https://ref.ly/Jude14:10) as meaning ‘to be mixed’ (see [63\.9](#63.9)), but this would seem to contradict in some measure the following adjective ἄκρατος ‘full strength, pure’ ([79\.99](#79.99)).

[REV 14:10](https://ref.ly/Jude14:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 14:10; Revelation 18:6


## κέρας (id: 002780000000000)

κέρας
=====

κέρας (G2768)

noun · κεραία · κεράτιον

8\.17 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

horn the hard bony outgrowth on the heads of certain animals Finding a term for ‘horn’ is usually not at all difficult. The problem arises when a term for ‘horn’ is already employed in a receptor language as a euphemistic expression for the male genital organ. It may therefore be necessary in [REV 5:6](https://ref.ly/Jude5:6) to speak of ‘a lamb with seven horns on his head.’\|In speaking of the horn\-shaped corners of the altar ([REV 9:13](https://ref.ly/Jude9:13)), it is often better not to use a term meaning literally horn, since this might imply that the altar had the horns of animals stuck on to the corners. One can normally say ‘corners of the altar shaped like horns’ or ‘... looking like horns or projections on the corners of the altar.’ See [79\.105](#79.105).

[REV 5:6](https://ref.ly/Jude5:6) · [REV 12:3](https://ref.ly/Jude12:3) · [REV 13:1](https://ref.ly/Jude13:1) · [REV 13:1](https://ref.ly/Jude13:1) · [REV 13:11](https://ref.ly/Jude13:11) · [REV 17:3](https://ref.ly/Jude17:3) · [REV 17:7](https://ref.ly/Jude17:7) · [REV 17:12](https://ref.ly/Jude17:12) · [REV 17:16](https://ref.ly/Jude17:16)

79\.105 · Features of Objects · Shapes

projection, corner a projection at the corner of an object

[REV 9:13](https://ref.ly/Jude9:13)

76\.16 · Power, Force

power, mighty power (a figurative extension of meaning of κέρας\[a] ‘horn,’ [8\.17](#8.17)) power of unusual significance In [LUK 1:69](https://ref.ly/Mark1:69) the reference of the phrase κέρας σωτηρίας is to the role of the Messiah, and accordingly one may often best render this phrase as ‘mighty Savior’ or ‘powerful Savior.’

[LUK 1:69](https://ref.ly/Mark1:69)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 5:6; Revelation 12:3; Revelation 13:1; Revelation 13:11; Revelation 17:3; Revelation 17:7; Revelation 17:12; Revelation 17:16; Revelation 9:13; Luke 1:69


## κεράτιον (id: 002781000000000)

κεράτιον
========

κεράτιον (G2769)

noun · κέρας

3\.46 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

carob pod (a diminutive derivative of κέρας\[a] ‘horn,’ [8\.17](#8.17)) the pod of the carob tree (which closely resembles a small horn) Carob pods were commonly used for fattening swine and were employed as an article of food by poor people. In translating [LUK 15:16](https://ref.ly/Mark15:16) it is not necessary, however, to identify specifically carob pods. In most languages some such expression as ‘edible pods’ is probably more satisfactory, since carob trees are unlikely to be known.

[LUK 15:16](https://ref.ly/Mark15:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 15:16

αἰσχροκερδής · αἰσχροκερδῶς · κέρδος

to earn, to gain, to make a profit to gain by means of one’s activity or investment

## κέρδος (id: 002783000000000)

κέρδος
======

κέρδος (G2771)

noun · κερδαίνω

57\.192 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Earn, Gain, Do Business

gain, profit (derivative of κερδαίνω\[a] ‘to earn, to gain,’ [57\.189](#57.189)) that which is gained or earned κέρδος in the sense of ‘gain’ is not restricted, however, to monetary gain or profit. It may refer to any kind of benefit or advantage, for example, ἐμοὶ γὰρ τὸ ζῆν Χριστὸς καὶ τὸ ἀποθανεῖν κέρδος ‘for me life is Christ, and death is a gain’ [PHP 1:21](https://ref.ly/Eph1:21).

## κεφαλή (id: 002787000000000)

κεφαλή
======

κεφαλή (G2776)

noun · κεφαλιόω

8\.10 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

head uppermost part of the human body, or the front or upper part of the body of an animal, typically separated from the rest of the body by a neck, and containing the brain, mouth, and sense organs; associated with the entire person, that person’s life and responsibilities In some languages it may be necessary to distinguish clearly between the head which is still a part of a body and a severed head. It is this latter meaning which is obviously involved in [MRK 6:25](https://ref.ly/Matt6:25).\|In rendering [1CO 11:4](https://ref.ly/Rom11:4), πᾶς ἀνὴρ προσευχόμενος ἢ προφητεύων κατὰ κεφαλῆς ἔχων ‘any man who prays or prophesies with his head covered,’ it may be important to indicate that the covering is not one which is designed to cover the entire head including the face, but only the top of the head. The same applies, of course, to [1CO 11:5](https://ref.ly/Rom11:5) and [1CO 11:7](https://ref.ly/Rom11:7).

[MAT 5:36](https://ref.ly/Matt5:36) · [MAT 6:17](https://ref.ly/Matt6:17) · [MAT 10:30](https://ref.ly/Matt10:30) · [MAT 14:8](https://ref.ly/Matt14:8) · [MAT 14:11](https://ref.ly/Matt14:11) · [MAT 18:19](https://ref.ly/Jude18:19) · [REV 19:12](https://ref.ly/Jude19:12)

87\.51 · Status · High Status or Rank \[including persons of high status]

one who is the head of, one who is superior to, one who is supreme over (a figurative extension of meaning of κεφαλή\[a] ‘head,’ [8\.10](#8.10)) one who is of supreme or pre\-eminent status, in view of authority to order or command

[1CO 11:3](https://ref.ly/Rom11:3) · [1CO 11:3](https://ref.ly/Rom11:3) · [1CO 11:3](https://ref.ly/Rom11:3) · [EPH 1:22](https://ref.ly/Gal1:22) · [EPH 4:15](https://ref.ly/Gal4:15) · [EPH 5:23](https://ref.ly/Gal5:23) · [EPH 5:23](https://ref.ly/Gal5:23) · [COL 1:18](https://ref.ly/Phil1:18) · [COL 2:10](https://ref.ly/Phil2:10) · [COL 2:19](https://ref.ly/Phil2:19)

7\.44 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

**Collocation:** κεφαλὴ γωνίας

cornerstone, important stone (a set phrase, literally: head of the corner) the cornerstone or capstone of a building, essential to its construction (κεφαλὴ γωνίας occurs in the NT only figuratively in reference to Christ) Though some scholars have thought that κεφαλὴ γωνίας refers to a keystone of an arch or the lintel stone over a door, it is highly probable that κεφαλὴ γωνίας has essentially the same meaning as ἀκρογωνιαῖος.

[MAT 21:42](https://ref.ly/Matt21:42) · [MRK 12:10](https://ref.ly/Matt12:10) · [LUK 20:17](https://ref.ly/Mark20:17) · [ACT 4:11](https://ref.ly/John4:11) · [1PE 2:7](https://ref.ly/Jas2:7)

23\.83 · Physiological Processes and States · Tire, Rest

**Collocation:** τὴν κεφαλὴν κλίνω

to lie down to rest, to lie down to sleep (an idiom, literally: to lay down the head) to experience the rest which comes from sleep ὁ δὲ υἱὸς τοῦ ἀνθρώπου οὐκ ἔχει ποῦ τὴν κεφαλὴν κλίνω ‘the Son of Man has no place to lie down to rest’ [MAT 8:20](https://ref.ly/Matt8:20), implies that Jesus possessed no permanent home. In [JHN 19:30](https://ref.ly/Luke19:30) this same expression must be understood not as an idiom but as a case of literally bowing the head (see [16\.16](#16.16)).

[MAT 8:20](https://ref.ly/Matt8:20) · [LUK 9:58](https://ref.ly/Mark9:58)

49\.16 · Activities Involving Clothing and Adorning

**Collocation:** κατὰ κεφαλῆς ἔχω

to have one’s head covered, to cover one’s head (an idiom, literally: to have down on the head) to wear a covering over one’s head

[1CO 11:4](https://ref.ly/Rom11:4)

## κεφαλίς (id: 002789000000000)

κεφαλίς
=======

κεφαλίς (G2777)

noun · κεφαλιόω

6\.67 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

section, scroll section of a scroll or of a long composition Long compositions often involved several scrolls, and a κεφαλίς would form one section or scroll of such a composition.\|In the case of practically all terms for documents (for example, ‘letter,’ ‘book,’ ‘scroll’) the meaning involves not only the object on which the writing was done, but also the contents of the writing. In some languages a distinction must be made between these two aspects of such objects, and one must make certain that the particular expression used in a receptor language will at least include the contents and not refer merely to the materials on which the words may have been written.

## κηρίον (id: 002794000000000)

κηρίον
======

κηρίον

noun

5\.21 · Foods and Condiments · Food

honeycomb This word is found as a variant reading only: οἱ δὲ ἐπέδωκαν αὐτῷ ... ἀπὸ μελισσίου κηρίου ‘and they gave him ... some honeycomb’ [LUK 24:42](https://ref.ly/Mark24:42) (apparatus); see [4\.50](#4.50). In rendering κηρίον it is important to employ an expression which will include both the honey and the comb. A literal rendering of ‘honeycomb’ might refer only to the wax container without the honey, but for many languages a term meaning simply ‘honey’ also refers to the honeycomb.

[LUK 24:42](https://ref.ly/Mark24:42)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 24:42

## κιβωτός (id: 002800000000000)

κιβωτός
=======

κιβωτός (G2787)

noun

6\.44 · Artifacts · Boats and Parts of Boats

boat, ship, the ark a large box\-like structure (the vessel built by Noah) The central meaning of κιβωτός is ‘box’ or ‘chest,’ but it was apparently applied to Noah’s ark in view of the type of construction and the fact that Noah’s ark resembled more a barge than a seagoing vessel. However, in view of the size of Noah’s ark, it is probably best in most languages to speak of it as a ‘ship.’

[MAT 24:38](https://ref.ly/Matt24:38) · [LUK 17:27](https://ref.ly/Mark17:27) · [HEB 11:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:7) · [1PE 3:20](https://ref.ly/Jas3:20)

6\.139 · Artifacts · Containers

box, chest, coffer any box\-like container, whether plain or elaborate; here, refers to the box used to hold the tablets of the Law In the NT κιβωτός\[b] occurs only in the phrase κιβωτὸς τῆς διαθήκης ‘the box of the covenant,’ which was placed in the Holy of Holies of the Temple in Jerusalem and referred to also as being in the heavenly temple ([REV 11:19](https://ref.ly/Jude11:19)).\|In the case of English some persons object to speaking of the so\-called ‘ark of the Covenant’ as ‘the Covenant Box,’ since they assume that the English word ‘ark’ has some special meaning equivalent to the corresponding Greek or Hebrew terms. However, the term ‘ark’ in Old English and Middle English is simply a borrowing of Latin arca meaning ‘box, chest, coffer.’ In present\-day English the term ark is known primarily from the context of ‘Noah’s ark.’

[HEB 9:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:4) · [REV 11:19](https://ref.ly/Jude11:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:38; Luke 17:27; Hebrews 11:7; 1 Peter 3:20; Hebrews 9:4; Revelation 11:19

## κινέω (id: 002807000000000)

κινέω
=====

κινέω (G2795)

ἀμετακίνητος · κίνησις · μετακινέω · συγκινέω

15\.1 · Linear Movement · Move, Come/Go

to move, to come, to go to make a change of location in space (a highly generic meaning) A strictly literal translation of κινέω in [ACT 17:28](https://ref.ly/John17:28) might imply merely moving from one place to another. The meaning, however, is generalized movement and activity; therefore, it may be possible to translate κινούμεθα as ‘we come and go’ or ‘we move about’ or even ‘we do what we do.’

[ACT 17:28](https://ref.ly/John17:28)

15\.3 · Linear Movement · Move, Come/Go

to move, to remove to cause something to be moved from a place It is also possible to translate κινέω in [REV 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jude2:5) as ‘I will take away.’

[MAT 23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4) · [REV 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jude2:5) · [REV 6:14](https://ref.ly/Jude6:14)

16\.2 · Non\-Linear Movement

to shake (as of the head) to set something in motion, with the nature of the movement dependent upon the object in question In [MRK 15:29](https://ref.ly/Matt15:29) the shaking of the head signifies derision and scorn, but in some languages this meaning is expressed by quite different gestures, for example, pointing with the finger, throwing back the head, or shrugging the shoulders. In fact, in some languages shaking the head from side to side means assent, while nodding shows opposition.

[MAT 27:39](https://ref.ly/Matt27:39) · [MRK 15:29](https://ref.ly/Matt15:29)

39\.44 · Hostility, Strife · Riot

to stir up against, to start a riot, to cause an uproar to cause people to riot against

[ACT 21:30](https://ref.ly/John21:30)

90\.53 · Case · Agent in a Causative Role Marked by Verbs

to cause a marker of a causative relation, with the implication of significant activity

[ACT 24:5](https://ref.ly/John24:5)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 17:28; Matthew 23:4; Revelation 2:5; Revelation 6:14; Matthew 27:39; Mark 15:29; Acts 21:30; Acts 24:5


## κίνησις (id: 002808000000000)

κίνησις
=======

κίνησις

adj · κινέω

16\.1 · Non\-Linear Movement

to be in motion, to move, movement the motion of a solid or mass, without indication of movement in space This word is found as a variant reading only: ἐκδεχομένων τὴν τοῦ ὕδατος κίνησιν ‘waiting for the water to move’ [JHN 5:3](https://ref.ly/Luke5:3) (apparatus).\|In a number of languages it may be necessary to indicate clearly the kind of motion which would be implied in [JHN 5:3](https://ref.ly/Luke5:3). Perhaps the most satisfactory rendering would involve the kind of motion resulting from the bubbling up of water, but not with the implication of being caused by heat. It would be inappropriate to use a term meaning merely ‘to shake,’ since this might suggest an earthquake.

[JHN 5:3](https://ref.ly/Luke5:3)

* **Associated Passages:** John 5:3

5\.24 · Foods and Condiments · Condiments

cinnamon a type of spice derived from the bark of certain aromatic plants In most languages κιννάμωμον is simply borrowed in a transliterated form. However, it is also possible to use a type of descriptive phrase, for example, ‘good\-tasting bark’ or ‘flavoring bark.’

## κλάδος (id: 002812000000000)

κλάδος
======

κλάδος (G2798)

noun · κλαίω

3\.49 · Plants · Non\-Fruit Parts of Plants

branch (of a tree or woody shrub) a secondary woody stem arising from the trunk or bough of a tree or shrub Some languages distinguish carefully between two major types of branches those which are essentially leaves (as in the case of palms) and those which have a number of buds or potential branches. Other languages may make a distinction between branches of a plant which is woody (a perennial) and those which are relatively soft and flexible, typical of an annual plant.

[MAT 13:32](https://ref.ly/Matt13:32) · [MAT 21:8](https://ref.ly/Matt21:8) · [MAT 24:32](https://ref.ly/Matt24:32) · [MRK 4:32](https://ref.ly/Matt4:32) · [MRK 13:28](https://ref.ly/Matt13:28) · [LUK 13:19](https://ref.ly/Mark13:19) · [ROM 11:16](https://ref.ly/Acts11:16) · [ROM 11:17](https://ref.ly/Acts11:17) · [ROM 11:18](https://ref.ly/Acts11:18) · [ROM 11:19](https://ref.ly/Acts11:19) · [ROM 11:21](https://ref.ly/Acts11:21)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:32; Matthew 21:8; Matthew 24:32; Mark 4:32; Mark 13:28; Luke 13:19; Romans 11:16; Romans 11:17; Romans 11:18; Romans 11:19; Romans 11:21


## κλαίω (id: 002813000000000)

κλαίω
=====

κλαίω (G2799)

κλάδος

25\.138 · Attitudes and Emotions · Laugh, Cry, Groan

to weep, to wail, to lament, weeping, crying to weep or wail, with emphasis upon the noise accompanying the weeping In [MAT 2:18](https://ref.ly/Matt2:18) κλαίω occurs with a so\-called ‘direct object,’ for example, Ραχὴλ κλαίουσα τὰ τέκνα αὐτῆς ... ὅτι οὐκ εἰσίν ‘Rachel weeps for her children ... because they are all dead.’ The so\-called direct object is, however, the cause of the weeping, and the so\-called transitive usage of κλαίω does not alter the meaning.

[MAT 2:18](https://ref.ly/Matt2:18) · [MAT 26:75](https://ref.ly/Matt26:75) · [MRK 5:38](https://ref.ly/Matt5:38) · [MRK 5:39](https://ref.ly/Matt5:39) · [MRK 14:72](https://ref.ly/Matt14:72) · [MRK 16:10](https://ref.ly/Matt16:10) · [LUK 6:21](https://ref.ly/Mark6:21) · [LUK 6:25](https://ref.ly/Mark6:25) · [LUK 7:13](https://ref.ly/Mark7:13) · [LUK 7:32](https://ref.ly/Mark7:32) · [LUK 7:38](https://ref.ly/Mark7:38) · [LUK 8:52](https://ref.ly/Mark8:52) · [LUK 8:52](https://ref.ly/Mark8:52) · [LUK 19:41](https://ref.ly/Mark19:41) · [LUK 22:62](https://ref.ly/Mark22:62) · [LUK 23:28](https://ref.ly/Mark23:28) · [LUK 23:28](https://ref.ly/Mark23:28) · [JHN 11:31](https://ref.ly/Luke11:31) · [JHN 11:33](https://ref.ly/Luke11:33) · [JHN 11:33](https://ref.ly/Luke11:33) · [JHN 16:20](https://ref.ly/Luke16:20) · [JHN 20:11](https://ref.ly/Luke20:11) · [JHN 20:11](https://ref.ly/Luke20:11) · [JHN 20:13](https://ref.ly/Luke20:13) · [JHN 20:15](https://ref.ly/Luke20:15) · [ACT 9:39](https://ref.ly/John9:39) · [ACT 21:13](https://ref.ly/John21:13) · [ROM 12:15](https://ref.ly/Acts12:15) · [ROM 12:15](https://ref.ly/Acts12:15) · [1CO 7:30](https://ref.ly/Rom7:30) · [1CO 7:30](https://ref.ly/Rom7:30) · [PHP 3:18](https://ref.ly/Eph3:18) · [JAS 4:9](https://ref.ly/Heb4:9) · [JAS 5:1](https://ref.ly/Heb5:1) · [REV 5:4](https://ref.ly/Jude5:4) · [REV 5:5](https://ref.ly/Jude5:5) · [REV 18:9](https://ref.ly/Jude18:9) · [REV 18:11](https://ref.ly/Jude18:11) · [REV 18:15](https://ref.ly/Jude18:15) · [REV 18:19](https://ref.ly/Jude18:19)

## κλάσις (id: 002814000000000)

κλάσις
======

κλάσις (G2800)

noun · κλάω

19\.34 · Physical Impact · Break, Break Through

to break, to break bread to break an object into two or more parts (in the NT κλάω and κλάσις are used exclusively for breaking bread) In some languages important distinctions are made for terms meaning ‘to break’ depending on the substance involved. For example, the breaking of a stick or a bone would require quite a different term from that used in speaking of breaking bread. Furthermore, the action of breaking bread would probably imply breaking into several pieces rather than a single break. Such a distinction may likewise require a special term.

[LUK 24:35](https://ref.ly/Mark24:35) · [ACT 2:42](https://ref.ly/John2:42)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 24:35; Acts 2:42

## κλάω (id: 002820000000000)

κλάω
====

κλάω (G2806)

ἐκκλάω · κατακλάω · κλάσις · κλάσμα · κλῆμα

19\.34 · Physical Impact · Break, Break Through

to break, to break bread to break an object into two or more parts (in the NT κλάω and κλάσις are used exclusively for breaking bread) In some languages important distinctions are made for terms meaning ‘to break’ depending on the substance involved. For example, the breaking of a stick or a bone would require quite a different term from that used in speaking of breaking bread. Furthermore, the action of breaking bread would probably imply breaking into several pieces rather than a single break. Such a distinction may likewise require a special term.

[MAT 14:19](https://ref.ly/Matt14:19) · [MAT 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36) · [MAT 26:26](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26) · [MRK 8:6](https://ref.ly/Matt8:6) · [MRK 8:19](https://ref.ly/Matt8:19) · [MRK 14:22](https://ref.ly/Matt14:22) · [LUK 22:19](https://ref.ly/Mark22:19) · [LUK 24:30](https://ref.ly/Mark24:30) · [ACT 27:35](https://ref.ly/John27:35) · [1CO 10:16](https://ref.ly/Rom10:16) · [1CO 11:24](https://ref.ly/Rom11:24)

23\.20 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

**Collocation:** ἄρτον κλάω

to eat a meal, to have a meal (an idiom, literally: to break bread) to eat a meal, without reference to any particular time of the day or to the type of food involved In some languages it is impossible to speak of ‘having a meal’ without indicating the time of day or the nature of the food consumed.\|The implication of ‘eating together’ comes from the total context. ἐν δὲ τῇ μιᾷ τῶν σαββάτων συνηγμένων ἡμῶν κλάσαι ἄρτον ‘on the first day of the week we gathered together for a meal’ [ACT 20:7](https://ref.ly/John20:7). No doubt the reference in [ACT 20:7](https://ref.ly/John20:7) is to the ‘fellowship meal,’ called ‘agape,’ which constituted the early Christian form of the ‘Lord’s Supper.’ See [23\.28](#23.28).

[ACT 2:46](https://ref.ly/John2:46) · [ACT 20:7](https://ref.ly/John20:7) · [ACT 20:11](https://ref.ly/John20:11)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 14:19; Matthew 15:36; Matthew 26:26; Mark 8:6; Mark 8:19; Mark 14:22; Luke 22:19; Luke 24:30; Acts 27:35; 1 Corinthians 10:16; 1 Corinthians 11:24; Acts 2:46; Acts 20:7; Acts 20:11

[ROM 4:13](https://ref.ly/Acts4:13) · [ROM 4:14](https://ref.ly/Acts4:14) · [TIT 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:7)1 · [HEB 6:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:17) · [JAS 2:5](https://ref.ly/Heb2:5)1

57\.139 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Receive

heir (derivative of κληρονομέω\[b] ‘to inherit,’ [57\.138](#57.138)) the person who inherits possessions

[MAT 21:38](https://ref.ly/Matt21:38) · [MRK 12:7](https://ref.ly/Matt12:7) · [LUK 20:14](https://ref.ly/Mark20:14) · [ROM 8:17](https://ref.ly/Acts8:17) · [ROM 8:17](https://ref.ly/Acts8:17) · [GAL 3:29](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:29) · [GAL 4:1](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:1) · [GAL 4:7](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:7) · [HEB 1:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:2) · [HEB 11:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:7)

1 TIT 3:7 · JAS 2:5 It is possible to interpret κληρονόμος in [JAS 2:5](https://ref.ly/Heb2:5) (and particularly in [TIT 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:7)) as identifying essentially a future experiencer, but with the additional components of the experience being valuable and not having been worked for. In this respect κληρονόμος overlaps between Subdomain I, Receive, in Domain 57 Possess, Transfer, Exchange, and Domain 90 Case.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 4:13; Romans 4:14; Titus 3:7; Hebrews 6:17; James 2:5; Matthew 21:38; Mark 12:7; Luke 20:14; Romans 8:17; Galatians 3:29; Galatians 4:1; Galatians 4:7; Hebrews 1:2; Hebrews 11:7


## κλῆρος (id: 002833000000000)

κλῆρος
======

κλῆρος (G2819)

noun · κληρόω

6\.219 · Artifacts · Miscellaneous

lot a specially marked pebble, piece of pottery, or stick employed in making decisions based upon chance Both in form as well as in function, the closest equivalent of κλῆρος\[a] is frequently a term which refers to dice. In [LUK 23:34](https://ref.ly/Mark23:34) a term for dice would be particularly appropriate.\|It is not possible to know the particular method employed in ‘choosing by lot,’ for evidently various devices were used. In [ACT 1:26](https://ref.ly/John1:26) (ἔδωκαν κλήρους αὐτοῖς ‘they drew lots,’ literally ‘they gave them lots’), it is probable that small sticks were handed out. See also footnote under κληρόω.

[MAT 27:35](https://ref.ly/Matt27:35) · [MRK 15:24](https://ref.ly/Matt15:24) · [LUK 23:34](https://ref.ly/Mark23:34) · [JHN 19:24](https://ref.ly/Luke19:24) · [ACT 1:26](https://ref.ly/John1:26)

57\.88 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

possession, what is possessed that which is given as a rightful possession (often in the sense of an inheritance)

[COL 1:12](https://ref.ly/Phil1:12)

37\.101 · Control, Rule · Assign to a Role or Function

ministry, task a responsibility, function, or ministry which has been assigned to a person For another interpretation of κλῆρος in [ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17), see [63\.18](#63.18).

[ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17)

35\.49 · Help, Care For · Entrust To the Care Of

responsibility to care for what has been assigned as someone’s responsibility to take care of

[1PE 5:3](https://ref.ly/Jas5:3)

63\.18 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Part

part, share a share or portion which has been assigned or granted For another interpretation of κλῆρος in [ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17), see [37\.101](#37.101).

[ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17) · [ACT 8:21](https://ref.ly/John8:21) · [ACT 26:18](https://ref.ly/John26:18)

30\.107 · Think · To Choose, To Select, To Prefer

**Collocation:** ὁ κλῆρος πίπτει ἐπί τινα

to choose by lot, to select by lot (an idiom, literally: the lot falls upon someone) the process of choosing, with the probable implication of discerning God’s will in this manner In some societies the closest natural equivalents of deciding by lot are procedures involving ‘drawing straws’ or ‘throwing dice’ or ‘throwing down sticks’ or ‘dropping pebbles.’

[ACT 1:26](https://ref.ly/John1:26)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:35; Mark 15:24; Luke 23:34; John 19:24; Acts 1:26; Colossians 1:12; Acts 1:17; 1 Peter 5:3; Acts 8:21; Acts 26:18


## κληρόω (id: 002834000000000)

κληρόω
======

κληρόω (G2820)

κατακληρονομέω · κληρονομέω · κληρονομία · κληρονόμος · κλῆρος · ναύκληρος · ὁλοκληρία · ὁλόκληρος · προσκληρόομαι · συγκληρονόμος

30\.105 · Think · To Choose, To Select, To Prefer

to choose in accordance with the will of God (a figurative extension of meaning of κληρόω ‘to be chosen by lot,’ not occurring in the NT) to choose, with the implication of supernatural or divine intervention or guidance1

[EPH 1:11](https://ref.ly/Gal1:11)

1 The phrases δίδωμι κλήρους in [ACT 1:26](https://ref.ly/John1:26) and βάλλω κλήρους in [LUK 23:34](https://ref.ly/Mark23:34) (βάλλω κλῆρον in [MAT 27:35](https://ref.ly/Matt27:35)) refer to choosing someone by means of casting lots, but these expressions may be interpreted in a strictly literal sense and thus are not treated here as idioms (see [6\.219](#6.219)).

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 1:11


## κλῆσις (id: 002835000000000)

κλῆσις
======

κλῆσις (G2821)

noun · καλέω

33\.312 · Communication · Call

to call, to call to a task to urgently invite someone to accept responsibilities for a particular task, implying a new relationship to the one who does the calling It is rare that one can translate καλέω\[d], κλῆσις\[a], and προσκαλέω\[b] as simply ‘to call’ in the sense of ‘to speak to someone at a distance and tell them to come.’ For example, in [2TH 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:14) it may be necessary to render the above clause as ‘through the good news we preached, which summoned you to do this.’ Similarly, in [ACT 16:10](https://ref.ly/John16:10) one may translate ‘because God has urgently invited us to preach the good news to the people there.’

[ROM 11:29](https://ref.ly/Acts11:29) · [EPH 1:18](https://ref.ly/Gal1:18) · [EPH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Gal4:4) · [PHP 3:14](https://ref.ly/Eph3:14) · [HEB 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:1) · [2PE 1:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:10)

33\.313 · Communication · Call

calling the state of having been called to a particular task and/or relation As in the case of καλέω\[d], κλῆσις\[a], and προσκαλέω\[b] ([33\.312](#33.312)), it may be entirely impossible to use a term in a receptor language which means literally ‘to call.’ Therefore, it may be necessary to translate [EPH 4:1](https://ref.ly/Gal4:1) as ‘I ask you then ... live worthy of the responsibility which God has urgently invited you to accept’ or ‘... live worthy of the task which God has given you to do.’

[1CO 1:26](https://ref.ly/Rom1:26) · [EPH 4:1](https://ref.ly/Gal4:1) · [2TH 1:11](https://ref.ly/1Thess1:11) · [2TI 1:9](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:9) · [HEB 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:1)

87\.2 · Status · Position, Rank

station, role the station in life or social role which one has In this context, κλῆσις refers to the status or role of being either a slave or a free person. In a number of languages this expression in [1CO 7:20](https://ref.ly/Rom7:20) can be best translated as ‘everyone should continue to be the same kind of person that he was when he was called.’ Such an expression must, of course, refer to one’s position in society and in the total social structure, not to particular aspects of moral or immoral behavior.

[1CO 7:20](https://ref.ly/Rom7:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 11:29; Ephesians 1:18; Ephesians 4:4; Philippians 3:14; Hebrews 3:1; 2 Peter 1:10; 1 Corinthians 1:26; Ephesians 4:1; 2 Thessalonians 1:11; 2 Timothy 1:9; 1 Corinthians 7:20


## κλητός (id: 002836000000000)

κλητός
======

κλητός (G2822)

adj · καλέω

33\.314 · Communication · Call

called pertaining to having been called As in the case of the translation of meanings in [33\.312](#33.312) and [33\.313](#33.313), it may be necessary likewise to make certain semantic adjustments in the translation of κλητός\[a] . For example, the phrase in [ROM 1:1](https://ref.ly/Acts1:1) may be rendered as ‘urgently invited to be an apostle’ or even ‘summoned and commissioned to be an apostle.’

[ROM 1:1](https://ref.ly/Acts1:1) · [ROM 1:6](https://ref.ly/Acts1:6) · [ROM 1:7](https://ref.ly/Acts1:7) · [ROM 8:28](https://ref.ly/Acts8:28) · [1CO 1:1](https://ref.ly/Rom1:1) · [1CO 1:2](https://ref.ly/Rom1:2) · [1CO 1:24](https://ref.ly/Rom1:24) · [JUD 1:1](https://ref.ly/3John1:1) · [REV 17:14](https://ref.ly/Jude17:14)

33\.318 · Communication · Invite

invited pertaining to having been invited It is possible that this expression in [MAT 22:14](https://ref.ly/Matt22:14) was a common popular saying, namely, an adage. There are certain problems in the understanding of this adage in [MAT 22:14](https://ref.ly/Matt22:14), for it would seem as though many persons are invited to do something, but few are permitted to do it. Perhaps this should be understood in the sense of ‘many are invited to apply, but few are selected.’ In this context, of course, both the invitation and the selection would be by God.

[MAT 22:14](https://ref.ly/Matt22:14)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 1:1; Romans 1:6; Romans 1:7; Romans 8:28; 1 Corinthians 1:1; 1 Corinthians 1:2; 1 Corinthians 1:24; Jude 1:1; Revelation 17:14; Matthew 22:14


## κλίβανος (id: 002837000000000)

κλίβανος
========

κλίβανος (G2823)

noun

7\.74 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

oven a dome\-like structure made of clay, in which wood and dried grass were burned, and then after being heated, was used for baking bread The function of κλίβανος may be described as ‘a place heated for baking bread,’ and it may be useful in some instances to employ a more extensive description of a κλίβανος in a glossary, but this is rarely necessary since function is far more important than form.

[MAT 6:30](https://ref.ly/Matt6:30) · [LUK 12:28](https://ref.ly/Mark12:28)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 6:30; Luke 12:28


## κλίμα (id: 002838000000000)

κλίμα
=====

κλίμα (G2824)

noun · κλίνω

1\.79 · Geographical Objects and Features · Sociopolitical Areas

region, territory, land, district (though this might imply too precisely a governmental area) region or regions of the earth, normally in relation to some ethnic group or geographical center, but not necessarily constituting a unit of governmental administration1 The meanings of γῆ\[d], χώρα\[b], κλίμαὅριον, and μέρος\[c] are not to be regarded as completely synonymous, but in certain of their NT usages they are largely overlapping in reference.

[ROM 15:23](https://ref.ly/Acts15:23) · [2CO 11:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:10) · [GAL 1:21](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:21)

1 The overlapping features of meaning in γῆ\[d], χώρα\[b], κλίμα, ὅριον, and μέρος\[c] may be readily illustrated by the comparable overlapping of English terms such as region, territory, and land. For example, in the case of [MAT 15:21](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21) it would be possible to speak of the region of Tyre and Sidon, the territory of Tyre and Sidon, the land of Tyre and Sidon, and even the district of Tyre and Sidon. The English terms region, territory, land, and district do differ in certain nuances of meaning reflecting primarily supplementary components which are largely connotative.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 15:23; 2 Corinthians 11:10; Galatians 1:21


## κλινάριον (id: 002839000000000)

κλινάριον
=========

κλινάριον (G2825a)

noun · κλίνω

6\.107 · Artifacts · Furniture

cot, pallet, stretcher a relatively small and often temporary type of object on which a person may lie or recline; made of reeds or cloth; thin and light for carrying In a number of contexts the terms κλινίδιον, κλινάριον, and κράβαττος refer to cots or stretchers on which sick or convalescent persons might be resting or on which they could be transported. There is no NT context in which these terms refer to couches on which people reclined while eating.

[ACT 5:15](https://ref.ly/John5:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 5:15


## κλίνη (id: 002840000000000)

κλίνη
=====

κλίνη (G2825)

noun · κλίνω

6\.106 · Artifacts · Furniture

bed, couch, cot, stretcher, bier any piece of furniture employed for reclining or lying on In [MAT 9:2](https://ref.ly/Matt9:2) a rendering such as ‘stretcher’ or ‘cot’ is certainly more advisable than the traditional rendering ‘bed,’ which might imply a large piece of furniture. In each passage one must employ a term which is most likely to identify the type of object which fits the context.

[MAT 9:2](https://ref.ly/Matt9:2) · [MAT 9:6](https://ref.ly/Matt9:6) · [MRK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Matt4:21) · [MRK 7:4](https://ref.ly/Matt7:4) · [MRK 7:30](https://ref.ly/Matt7:30) · [LUK 5:18](https://ref.ly/Mark5:18) · [LUK 8:16](https://ref.ly/Mark8:16) · [LUK 17:34](https://ref.ly/Mark17:34) · [REV 2:22](https://ref.ly/Jude2:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:2; Matthew 9:6; Mark 4:21; Mark 7:4; Mark 7:30; Luke 5:18; Luke 8:16; Luke 17:34; Revelation 2:22

## κλίνω (id: 002842000000000)

κλίνω
=====

κλίνω (G2827)

ἀκλινής · ἀνακλίνω · ἀρχιτρίκλινος · ἐκκλίνω · κατακλίνω · κλίμα · κλινάριον · κλίνη · κλινίδιον · κλισία · προσκλίνομαι · πρόσκλισις · πρωτοκλισία

16\.16 · Non\-Linear Movement

to bow down (the head), to incline to cause something to incline See also [23\.83](#23.83).

[JHN 19:30](https://ref.ly/Luke19:30)

15\.65 · Linear Movement · Leave, Depart, Flee, Escape, Send

to cause to run away, to put to flight, to rout to cause to flee or run away from

[HEB 11:34](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:34)

67\.118 · Time · Duration of Time with Reference to Some Point of Time: Until, Delay, Still, From

to draw near, to draw to a close to extend in time, with focus upon the end point For another interpretation of κλίνω in [LUK 9:12](https://ref.ly/Mark9:12), see [68\.51](#68.51).

68\.51 · Aspect · Cease, Stop

to begin to end to begin to come to an end, with particular reference to the period of a day (a figurative meaning dependent upon the position of the sun) For another interpretation of κλίνω in [LUK 9:12](https://ref.ly/Mark9:12), see [67\.118](#67.118).

[LUK 9:12](https://ref.ly/Mark9:12) · [LUK 24:29](https://ref.ly/Mark24:29)

17\.21 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Prostrate as an Act of Reverence or Supplication

**Collocation:** κλίνω τὸ πρόσωπον εἰς τὴν γῆν

to prostrate oneself before (an idiom, literally: to incline the face to the ground) to prostrate oneself before someone as an act of reverence, fear, or supplication

[LUK 24:5](https://ref.ly/Mark24:5)

23\.83 · Physiological Processes and States · Tire, Rest

**Collocation:** τὴν κεφαλὴν κλίνω

to lie down to rest, to lie down to sleep (an idiom, literally: to lay down the head) to experience the rest which comes from sleep ὁ δὲ υἱὸς τοῦ ἀνθρώπου οὐκ ἔχει ποῦ τὴν κεφαλὴν κλίνω ‘the Son of Man has no place to lie down to rest’ [MAT 8:20](https://ref.ly/Matt8:20), implies that Jesus possessed no permanent home. In [JHN 19:30](https://ref.ly/Luke19:30) this same expression must be understood not as an idiom but as a case of literally bowing the head (see [16\.16](#16.16)).

[MAT 8:20](https://ref.ly/Matt8:20) · [LUK 9:58](https://ref.ly/Mark9:58)

* **Associated Passages:** John 19:30; Hebrews 11:34; Luke 9:12; Luke 24:29; Luke 24:5; Matthew 8:20; Luke 9:58

## κνήθω (id: 002848000000000)

κνήθω
=====

κνήθω (G2833) — κνήθομαι

25\.11 · Attitudes and Emotions · Desire, Want, Wish

**Collocation:** κνήθομαι τὴν ἀκοήν

to have itching ears, to desire to hear what one wants to hear, to be desirous of hearing (an idiom, literally: to itch with respect to hearing) to have one’s ears tickled by what is heard1

[2TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:3)

1 The idiom κνήθομαι τὴν ἀκοήν involves two quite distinct semantic features. One is the desire to be pleased, and the second is the means of such gratification, namely, what is heard. It would be possible to classify this idiom either under Sensory Events and States (Domain 24\) or in the domain of Attitudes and Emotions. Since in [2TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:3) the latter seems the more focal feature of meaning, the idiom is included in the domain of Attitudes and Emotions.

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Timothy 4:3

## κοιλία (id: 002851000000000)

κοιλία
======

κοιλία (G2836)

noun

8\.67 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

belly, internal organs the entire digestive apparatus, including stomach and intestines

[MAT 12:40](https://ref.ly/Matt12:40) · [MAT 15:17](https://ref.ly/Matt15:17) · [MRK 7:19](https://ref.ly/Matt7:19) · [1CO 6:13](https://ref.ly/Rom6:13) · [1CO 6:13](https://ref.ly/Rom6:13) · [REV 10:9](https://ref.ly/Jude10:9) · [REV 10:10](https://ref.ly/Jude10:10)

8\.69 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

womb the uterus

[MAT 19:12](https://ref.ly/Matt19:12) · [LUK 1:15](https://ref.ly/Mark1:15) · [LUK 1:41](https://ref.ly/Mark1:41) · [LUK 1:42](https://ref.ly/Mark1:42) · [LUK 1:44](https://ref.ly/Mark1:44) · [LUK 2:21](https://ref.ly/Mark2:21) · [LUK 23:29](https://ref.ly/Mark23:29) · [JHN 3:4](https://ref.ly/Luke3:4) · [ACT 3:2](https://ref.ly/John3:2) · [ACT 14:8](https://ref.ly/John14:8) · [GAL 1:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:15)

26\.11 · Psychological Faculties

heart, feelings, desires (figurative extension of meaning of κοιλία\[a] ‘belly,’ [8\.67](#8.67)) the psychological faculty of desire, intent, and feeling1 Though some persons have attempted to distinguish between σπλάγχνον\[b], κοιλία\[c], and νεφρός, it is extremely doubtful whether this is really possible or practical. The semantic focus in the use of these terms is clearly the deeper and more intimate feelings and emotions. In some languages one can use a term which literally means ‘belly’ or ‘bowels,’ but more often than not, these emotions are associated with some particular organ of the body such as heart, spleen, liver, etc. Rather, however, than attempting to employ a figurative expression which may or may not be fully equivalent, it is often preferable to refer to the emotional content by using terms such as ‘feelings,’ ‘intents,’ ‘desires,’ or ‘compassion,’ depending upon the context.

[JHN 7:38](https://ref.ly/Luke7:38)

25\.28 · Attitudes and Emotions · Desire Strongly

physical desires, desires of the body desire for gratification of the body It is also possible that κοιλία in [ROM 16:18](https://ref.ly/Acts16:18) refers to Jewish dietary laws and regulations.

[ROM 16:18](https://ref.ly/Acts16:18) · [PHP 3:19](https://ref.ly/Eph3:19)

23\.51 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

**Collocation:** ἡ κοιλία βαστάζει

to be pregnant with, to carry in the womb (an idiom, literally: the womb carries) to experience the process of pregnancy It may, however, be necessary in some languages to render [LUK 11:27](https://ref.ly/Mark11:27) as ‘fortunate is the woman who gave you birth,’ since a literal reference to carrying in the womb may seem unduly crude.

[LUK 11:27](https://ref.ly/Mark11:27)

1 It would be possible to treat σπλάγχνα\[b], κοιλία\[c], and νεφρός in this figurative sense in Domain 25 Attitudes and Emotions, but these meanings have been assigned to this domain of Psychological Faculties since the meanings involve aspects of personality which function as agents or presumed locations of psychological dispositions.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:40; Matthew 15:17; Mark 7:19; 1 Corinthians 6:13; Revelation 10:9; Revelation 10:10; Matthew 19:12; Luke 1:15; Luke 1:41; Luke 1:42; Luke 1:44; Luke 2:21; Luke 23:29; John 3:4; Acts 3:2; Acts 14:8; Galatians 1:15; John 7:38; Romans 16:18; Philippians 3:19; Luke 11:27


## κοιμάομαι (id: 002852000000000)

κοιμάομαι
=========

κοιμάομαι (G2837)

κεῖμαι

23\.66 · Physiological Processes and States · Sleep, Waking

to sleep, to be asleep, sleep the state of being asleep In some languages sleep is expressed by an idiom, for example, ‘his soul had wandered away’ or ‘his eyes had disappeared.’ Though an expression such as ‘his soul had wandered away’ might appear in some languages to have misleading theological implications, it really means only ‘to sleep.’

[MAT 28:13](https://ref.ly/Matt28:13) · [LUK 22:45](https://ref.ly/Mark22:45) · [JHN 11:12](https://ref.ly/Luke11:12) · [ACT 12:6](https://ref.ly/John12:6)

23\.104 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

to be dead, to have died (figurative extension of meaning of κοιμάομαι\[a] ‘to sleep,’ [23\.66](#23.66)) to sleep, as a euphemistic expression for the state of being dead Some translators have attempted to preserve the figure of speech in καθεύδω\[b] and κοιμάομαι\[b] by translating ‘to sleep’ rather than ‘to have died’ or ‘to be dead.’ Such a practice, however, has resulted in misunderstanding in a number of instances and has sometimes led to the doctrine of so\-called ‘soul\-sleep.’

[MAT 27:52](https://ref.ly/Matt27:52) · [JHN 11:11](https://ref.ly/Luke11:11) · [ACT 7:60](https://ref.ly/John7:60) · [ACT 13:36](https://ref.ly/John13:36) · [1CO 7:39](https://ref.ly/Rom7:39) · [1CO 11:30](https://ref.ly/Rom11:30) · [1CO 15:6](https://ref.ly/Rom15:6) · [1CO 15:18](https://ref.ly/Rom15:18) · [1CO 15:20](https://ref.ly/Rom15:20) · [1CO 15:51](https://ref.ly/Rom15:51) · [1TH 4:13](https://ref.ly/Col4:13) · [1TH 4:14](https://ref.ly/Col4:14) · [1TH 4:15](https://ref.ly/Col4:15) · [2PE 3:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 28:13; Luke 22:45; John 11:12; Acts 12:6; Matthew 27:52; John 11:11; Acts 7:60; Acts 13:36; 1 Corinthians 7:39; 1 Corinthians 11:30; 1 Corinthians 15:6; 1 Corinthians 15:18; 1 Corinthians 15:20; 1 Corinthians 15:51; 1 Thessalonians 4:13; 1 Thessalonians 4:14; 1 Thessalonians 4:15; 2 Peter 3:4


## κοίμησις (id: 002853000000000)

κοίμησις
========

κοίμησις (G2838)

noun · κεῖμαι

23\.66 · Physiological Processes and States · Sleep, Waking

to sleep, to be asleep, sleep the state of being asleep In some languages sleep is expressed by an idiom, for example, ‘his soul had wandered away’ or ‘his eyes had disappeared.’ Though an expression such as ‘his soul had wandered away’ might appear in some languages to have misleading theological implications, it really means only ‘to sleep.’\|In [JHN 11:13](https://ref.ly/Luke11:13) κοίμησις is combined with ὕπνος apparently to stress the fact that the sleep was an ordinary or natural sleep.

[JHN 11:13](https://ref.ly/Luke11:13)

* **Associated Passages:** John 11:13


## κοινός (id: 002854000000000)

κοινός
======

κοινός (G2839)

adj · κοινόω

57\.9 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Have, Possess, Property, Owner

shared, mutual, common pertaining to sharing with someone else in a possession or a relationship implying mutual interest Since the emphasis in [TIT 1:4](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:4) is upon the fact that Paul and Titus have the same faith, one may also translate as ‘... the faith that you and I have’ or ‘... the faith we both believe in.’

[ACT 2:44](https://ref.ly/John2:44) · [TIT 1:4](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:4)

53\.39 · Religious Activities · Defile, Unclean, Common

defiled, ritually unclean pertaining to being ritually unacceptable, either as the result of defilement or because of the very nature of the object itself (for example, ritually unacceptable animals) It is possible that there is some subtle distinction in meaning, particularly on a connotative level, between κοινός\[b] and ἀκάθαρτος in [ACT 10:14](https://ref.ly/John10:14), but it is difficult to determine the precise differences of meaning on the basis of existing contexts. The two terms are probably used in [ACT 10:14](https://ref.ly/John10:14) primarily for the sake of emphasis.

[MRK 7:2](https://ref.ly/Matt7:2) · [MRK 7:5](https://ref.ly/Matt7:5) · [ACT 10:14](https://ref.ly/John10:14) · [ACT 10:28](https://ref.ly/John10:28) · [ACT 11:8](https://ref.ly/John11:8) · [ROM 14:14](https://ref.ly/Acts14:14) · [ROM 14:14](https://ref.ly/Acts14:14) · [ROM 14:14](https://ref.ly/Acts14:14) · [REV 21:27](https://ref.ly/Jude21:27)

65\.15 · Value · Valuable, Lacking in Value

of little value, relatively worthless pertaining to being of little value, in view of being ordinary and common

[HEB 10:29](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:29)

89\.118 · Relations · Association

in common pertaining to being in common between two or more persons It is also possible to understand κοινός in [JUD 1:3](https://ref.ly/3John1:3) as κοινός\[a] ‘shared, mutual’ (see [57\.9](#57.9)).

[ACT 4:32](https://ref.ly/John4:32) · [JUD 1:3](https://ref.ly/3John1:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 2:44; Titus 1:4; Mark 7:2; Mark 7:5; Acts 10:14; Acts 10:28; Acts 11:8; Romans 14:14; Revelation 21:27; Hebrews 10:29; Acts 4:32; Jude 1:3


## κοινόω (id: 002855000000000)

κοινόω
======

κοινόω (G2840)

κοινός · κοινωνέω · κοινωνία · κοινωνικός · κοινωνός · συγκοινωνέω · συγκοινωνός

53\.33 · Religious Activities · Defile, Unclean, Common

to make unclean, to defile, to profane to cause something to become unclean, profane, or ritually unacceptable1 In a number of languages it is quite impossible to translate literally the concept of unclean, for physical cleanliness and ritual acceptability are completely unrelated. In some languages it is necessary to translate κοινόω\[a] or βεβηλόω as to take away its holiness or to make something unacceptable to God. In many cultures one must express this concept as involving so\-called negative taboo.

[MAT 15:11](https://ref.ly/Matt15:11) · [MAT 15:11](https://ref.ly/Matt15:11) · [MAT 15:18](https://ref.ly/Matt15:18) · [MAT 15:20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:20) · [MAT 15:20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:20) · [MRK 7:15](https://ref.ly/Matt7:15) · [MRK 7:15](https://ref.ly/Matt7:15) · [MRK 7:18](https://ref.ly/Matt7:18) · [MRK 7:20](https://ref.ly/Matt7:20) · [MRK 7:23](https://ref.ly/Matt7:23) · [ACT 21:28](https://ref.ly/John21:28) · [HEB 9:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:13)

53\.40 · Religious Activities · Defile, Unclean, Common

to call something common, to regard something as defiled to call or to regard something as common or defiled

[ACT 10:15](https://ref.ly/John10:15) · [ACT 11:9](https://ref.ly/John11:9)

1 βεβηλόω may differ significantly from κοινόω\[a] in denoting a more serious degree of defilement, but this cannot be readily determined from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 15:11; Matthew 15:18; Matthew 15:20; Mark 7:15; Mark 7:18; Mark 7:20; Mark 7:23; Acts 21:28; Hebrews 9:13; Acts 10:15; Acts 11:9

## κοίτη (id: 002860000000000)

κοίτη
=====

κοίτη (G2845)

noun · κεῖμαι

6\.108 · Artifacts · Furniture

bed a piece of furniture used for sleeping It is not necessary to understand [LUK 11:7](https://ref.ly/Mark11:7) to mean that the children were in the same bed with the man, but it is, of course, possible that the reference here is to a relatively humble house in which all the members of the family would sleep on a single raised platform. See also [10\.37](#10.37).

[LUK 11:7](https://ref.ly/Mark11:7)

23\.62 · Physiological Processes and States · Sexual Relations

sexual activity, sexual life, marriage relations (a figurative extension of meaning of κοίτη\[a] ‘bed,’ [6\.108](#6.108)) to have sexual relations In some languages one may speak of ‘sexual life’ as ‘the way one lives with one’s wife’ or ‘how one treats one’s wife.’

[HEB 13:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:4)

88\.273 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

sexual immorality, lasciviousness to engage in immoral sexual excess1

[ROM 13:13](https://ref.ly/Acts13:13)

23\.50 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

**Collocation:** κοίτην ἔχω

pregnant, to be pregnant (an idiom, literally: to have bed, though in combination with ἔχω, κοίτη early acquired the metonymic meaning of sexual relations) to be in a state of pregnancy This expression contrasts with the meaning of συλλαμβάνω\[b], [23\.49](#23.49), in that it seems to focus more upon the state of pregnancy rather than the event of conception.

[ROM 9:10](https://ref.ly/Acts9:10)

1 κοίτη\[c] sexual immorality is a peripheral extension of meaning of κοίτη\[b] sexual relations (see [23\.62](#23.62)). This is due to a process of semantic narrowing.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 11:7; Hebrews 13:4; Romans 13:13; Romans 9:10


## κοιτών (id: 002861000000000)

κοιτών
======

κοιτών (G2846)

noun · κεῖμαι

7\.29 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

bedroom a room in a house for sleeping It would be wrong to render the expression ‘who was in charge of the king’s bedroom’ in [ACT 12:20](https://ref.ly/John12:20) as meaning simply one who kept the bedroom clean. A person such as Blastus would have been a highly respected person with considerable responsibility for the king’s living quarters and personal affairs. The expression may be adequately rendered in [ACT 12:20](https://ref.ly/John12:20) by speaking of Blastus as ‘a high official.’

[ACT 12:20](https://ref.ly/John12:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 12:20

adj · κόκκος

79\.29 · Features of Objects · Color

scarlet, red a dye obtained from egg\-clusters of a cochineal, collected from the leaves of Quercus coccifera In [MAT 27:28](https://ref.ly/Matt27:28) ‘scarlet robe’ may have implied high military rank.

scarlet cloth a reddish\-purple cloth dyed with a substance obtained from the murex shellfish; expensive to produce; associated with wealth and royalty

## κόκκος (id: 002863000000000)

κόκκος
======

κόκκος (G2848)

noun · κόκκινος

3\.35 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

seed the kernel part of fruit, usually grain A number of languages make distinctions between two quite different types of seed: (1\) those produced by grasses (that is to say, grains) and (2\) those produced by other types of plants, for example, beans, squash, apples, etc. In all passages employing the Greek terms in this subdomain (κόκκος, σπέρμα\[a], σπόρος), it is best to use some expression referring to ‘grain.’

[MAT 13:31](https://ref.ly/Matt13:31) · [MAT 17:20](https://ref.ly/Matt17:20) · [MRK 4:31](https://ref.ly/Matt4:31) · [LUK 13:19](https://ref.ly/Mark13:19) · [LUK 17:6](https://ref.ly/Mark17:6) · [JHN 12:24](https://ref.ly/Luke12:24) · [1CO 15:37](https://ref.ly/Rom15:37)

## κολάζω (id: 002864000000000)

κολάζω
======

κολάζω (G2849)

κόλασις · κολαφίζω

38\.2 · Punish, Reward · Punish

to punish to punish, with the implication of resulting severe suffering In a number of languages punishment is often expressed as a causative of suffering, that is to say, ‘to cause to suffer’ or ‘to cause to endure harm.’ In some languages, however, there are a number of different types of punishment, and clear distinctions must be made between various degrees of punishment as well as between physical versus mental punishment.

[ACT 4:21](https://ref.ly/John4:21) · [2PE 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:9)

20\.27 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

to cause harm to (a figurative extension of meaning of κολαφίζω\[a] ‘to beat with the fist,’ [19\.7](#19.7)) to cause injury or weakness or possibly a circumstantial difficulty Though differences of interpretation exist concerning the meaning of ‘a thorn in my flesh’ ([2CO 12:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:7)), especially since some scholars have felt that this must refer to some kind of physical disability, it seems more likely to assume that it refers to some special personal circumstance such as the opposition Paul encountered in preaching the gospel, a reference suggested by [2CO 12:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:10) (see also [22\.20](#22.20)).\|Without some clear understanding of the reference of ‘a thorn in my flesh,’ it is difficult to determine precisely how κολαφίζω is to be interpreted in [2CO 12:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:7).

## κολλάω (id: 002868000000000)

προσκολλάομαι

34\.22 · Association · Join, Begin To Associate

to join, to join oneself to, to become a part of to begin an association with someone, whether temporary or permanent1 Though the Greek text of [ACT 8:29](https://ref.ly/John8:29) says literally ‘join this carriage,’ in reality, of course, the association is not directly with the carriage, but with the man riding in the carriage. ## κολοβόω (id: 002871000000000)

59\.71 · Quantity · Increase, Decrease

to shorten, to decrease, to reduce in number to cause something to be reduced in number or extent There may be difficulties involved in a strictly literal rendering of ‘those days will be shortened,’ for it might appear that each day would become shorter rather than that the number of days would be decreased.
