## κόλπος (id: 002873000000000)

κόλπος
======

κόλπος (G2859)

noun

8\.39 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

bosom, lap the region of the body extending from the breast to the legs, especially when a person is in a seated position The term κόλπος occurs in several idiomatic phrases in the NT. For example, the expression ‘who was in the bosom of the Father’ in [JHN 1:18](https://ref.ly/Luke1:18) denotes an association of intimacy and affection (see [34\.18](#34.18)). In a context referring to the position of a person at a meal (as in [JHN 13:23](https://ref.ly/Luke13:23)), κόλπος indicates an honored place (see [17\.25](#17.25)). In [LUK 16:22](https://ref.ly/Mark16:22) κόλπος Ἀβραάμ signifies the heavenly abode (see [1\.16](#1.16)).

[LUK 16:22](https://ref.ly/Mark16:22) · [LUK 16:23](https://ref.ly/Mark16:23) · [JHN 1:18](https://ref.ly/Luke1:18) · [JHN 13:23](https://ref.ly/Luke13:23)

6\.181 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

fold the fold of a garment forming a type of pocket or container

[LUK 6:38](https://ref.ly/Mark6:38)

1\.74 · Geographical Objects and Features · Bodies of Water

bay, gulf a part of the sea which is partially enclosed by land A ‘bay’ may be described as ‘a protected area of the sea’ or ‘a part of the sea protected by land.’

[ACT 27:39](https://ref.ly/John27:39)

1\.16 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Above the Earth

**Collocation:** ὁ κόλπος Ἀβραάμ

Abraham’s bosom, heaven (an idiom, literally: Abraham’s bosom) the heavenly abode, with the implication of close interpersonal relations A literal rendering of κόλπος Ἀβραάμ as ‘the bosom of Abraham’ or ‘the lap of Abraham’ is often misleading. In some languages it may even suggest homosexuality, and in other cases it implies that Lazarus was either a baby or was changed into a baby in heaven. Since κόλπος Ἀβραάμ is generally interpreted as a reference to the eschatological heavenly feast,1 one may be justified in rendering [LUK 16:22](https://ref.ly/Mark16:22) as in TEV ‘the poor man died and was carried by the angels to sit beside Abraham at the feast in heaven.’ In some languages κόλπος Ἀβραάμ in this context is translated as ‘he was carried by the angels to Abraham’s side’ or ‘... to be with Abraham.’

[LUK 16:22](https://ref.ly/Mark16:22) · [LUK 16:23](https://ref.ly/Mark16:23)

1 According to ancient Jewish tradition, the end of the age would be characterized by a heavenly feast to be enjoyed by the righteous. This would be presided over by Abraham, and therefore to go to Abrahams bosom would be equivalent to being an honored guest at this celestial banquet.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 16:22; Luke 16:23; John 1:18; John 13:23; Luke 6:38; Acts 27:39


## κολυμβάω (id: 002874000000000)

========

κολυμβάω (G2860)

ἐκκολυμβάω · κολυμβήθρα

15\.246 · Linear Movement · Swim

to swim movement through water by the use of limbs A number of languages have several different terms for ‘swim’ depending on whether it is a person, an animal, a fish, or an eel (or a snake). Care must be exercised in choosing the appropriate term for this context.

[ACT 27:43](https://ref.ly/John27:43)

noun

colony a city or town with special privileges in that the inhabitants of such a town were regarded as Roman citizens (such towns were originally colonized by citizens of Rome) A translational equivalent of ‘colony’ is frequently a phrase, for example, ‘a city where people were Romans’ or ‘a city of people who regarded Rome as their hometown.’

## κοπετός (id: 002884000000000)

κοπετός
=======

κοπετός (G2870)

noun · κόπτω

52\.1 · Funerals and Burial

mourning, lamentation beating the breast and lamenting as an expression of sorrow1 In a number of languages it is entirely impossible to use an expression such as ‘to beat the breast’ in referring to mourning or grief, since ‘to beat the breast’ is often employed as a gesture of self\-congratulation or pride in accomplishment. In a number of instances the closest equivalent of ‘to beat the breast’ is ‘to beat the head’ or even ‘to pull out the hair.’

[ACT 8:2](https://ref.ly/John8:2)

1 The meanings of κόπτομαι and κοπετός in Domain 52 differ from related meanings in Domain 23 Physiological Processes and States and Domain 25 Attitudes and Emotions, since the expressions of grief in [LUK 8:52](https://ref.ly/Mark8:52) and [ACT 8:2](https://ref.ly/John8:2) reflect a form of ritualized and institutionalized mourning.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 8:2

ἀποκόπτω · ἀπρόσκοπος · ἀργυροκόπος · ἐγκοπή · ἐγκόπτω · ἐκκόπτω · εὐκοπώτερος · κατακόπτω · κοπάζω · κοπετός · κοπή · κοπιάω · κόπος · κωφός · προκοπή · πρόσκομμα · προσκοπή · προσκόπτω

19\.17 · Physical Impact · Pierce, Cut

to cut to cut, by means of a sharp\-edged instrument (for example, knife, sword, or ax) In a number of languages important distinctions are made for various types of cutting. For example, terms referring to the cutting of flesh may be different from those involving wood or stone. Similarly, important distinctions may be made as to whether there is simply an incision by cutting or whether a particular object is cut in two or cut off.

[MAT 21:8](https://ref.ly/Matt21:8) · [MRK 11:8](https://ref.ly/Matt11:8)

52\.1 · Funerals and Burial

to mourn, to lament, to beat the breast, mourning, lamentation to beat the breast and lament as an expression of sorrow1 In a number of languages it is entirely impossible to use an expression such as ‘to beat the breast’ in referring to mourning or grief, since ‘to beat the breast’ is often employed as a gesture of self\-congratulation or pride in accomplishment. 1 The meanings of κόπτομαι and κοπετός in Domain 52 differ from related meanings in Domain 23 Physiological Processes and States and Domain 25 Attitudes and Emotions, since the expressions of grief in [LUK 8:52](https://ref.ly/Mark8:52) and [ACT 8:2](https://ref.ly/John8:2) reflect a form of ritualized and institutionalized mourning.

## κόραξ (id: 002891000000000)

κόραξ
=====

κόραξ (G2876)

noun

4\.43 · Animals · Birds

crow, raven large black bird with thick strong beak, and fairly short legs; highly intelligent; Corvus family; crows and ravens belong to the same family of birds but differ in size, ravens being somewhat larger and being more inclined to feed on dead bodies In some languages one must be especially sensitive to connotations relating to terms for ‘crow’ or ‘raven,’ since these birds may be either particularly disliked or may be regarded as symbols of death and sickness. If such is the case, it may be preferable to simply use a more generic term for birds.

[LUK 12:24](https://ref.ly/Mark12:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 12:24


## κοράσιον (id: 002892000000000)

κοράσιον
========

κοράσιον (G2877)

noun

9\.40 · People · Females

girl (a diminutive derivative of κόρη ‘girl,’ not occurring in the NT, but seemingly having lost the diminutive feature of meaning) a girl about the age of puberty In [MRK 5:41](https://ref.ly/Matt5:41) κοράσιον is equated in meaning with the Aramaic term ταλιθα (see [9\.48](#9.48)), and in [MRK 5:42](https://ref.ly/Matt5:42) this girl is identified as being twelve years of age. Compare also ἠνέχθη ἡ κεφαλὴ αὐτοῦ ἐπὶ πίνακι καὶ ἐδόθη τῷ κορασίῳ ‘his head was brought in on a plate and given to the girl’ ([MAT 14:11](https://ref.ly/Matt14:11)). It is impossible to determine the age of Herodias’ daughter, but in view of her role as an attractive dancer, she was probably of the age of puberty.

[MAT 9:24](https://ref.ly/Matt9:24) · [MAT 9:25](https://ref.ly/Matt9:25) · [MAT 14:11](https://ref.ly/Matt14:11) · [MRK 5:41](https://ref.ly/Matt5:41) · [MRK 5:42](https://ref.ly/Matt5:42) · [MRK 6:22](https://ref.ly/Matt6:22) · [MRK 6:28](https://ref.ly/Matt6:28) · [MRK 6:28](https://ref.ly/Matt6:28)

## κορέννυμι (id: 002896000000000)

κορέννυμι
=========

κορέννυμι (G2880)

25\.80 · Attitudes and Emotions · Content, Satisfied

to be content, to be satisfied to be happy or content with what one has, with the implication of its being abundant Note that in this statement in [1CO 4:8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:8) there is evidently a significant element of irony, and it is for that reason that some translations employ a question, for example, ‘do you already have everything you need?’ For another interpretation of κορέννυμι in [1CO 4:8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:8), see [57\.22](#57.22).

[1CO 4:8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:8)

57\.22 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Have Sufficient

to have enough, to be satiated to have enough, often with the implication of even more than enough This first statement in [1CO 4:8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:8) is probably to be understood ironically, and therefore it may be readily translated as a question, for example, ‘do you already have everything you need?’ or as a statement referring to what the people of Corinth evidently presumed, for example, ‘you think you already have all you need.’ For another interpretation of κορέννυμι in [1CO 4:8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:8), see [25\.80](#25.80).

[ACT 27:38](https://ref.ly/John27:38) · [1CO 4:8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:8)

## κοσμοκράτωρ (id: 002904000000000)

κοσμοκράτωρ
===========

κοσμοκράτωρ (G2888)

noun

37\.73 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

world ruler one who rules over the whole world The expression ‘world ruler’ should not be understood in terms of merely ruling over the earth as a physical object but of ‘ruling over those who are on the earth.’ Most scholars, however, interpret κοσμοκράτωρ in [EPH 6:12](https://ref.ly/Gal6:12) as meaning a supernatural power (see [12\.44](#12.44)), though it is possible to understand κοσμοκράτωρ in this context as meaning a human ruler.

[EPH 6:12](https://ref.ly/Gal6:12)

12\.44 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

power, authority, lordship, ruler, wicked force (title for supernatural forces and powers) a supernatural power having some particular role in controlling the destiny and activities of human beings Some scholars have believed that it is possible to reconstruct at least in part some of the hierarchy represented by these various supernatural forces and powers, on the basis of the neoplatonic system of nine such powers arranged in three orders of three each. NT terminology and usage does not, however, lend itself to such a classification, and it is difficult, if not impossible, to determine what are the significant differences between these supernatural powers and forces.\|In the case of [EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21) some scholars apply the terms in question both to the supernatural and to the human sphere, thus emphasizing the totality of Christ’s rule. This has a considerable measure of justification in view of the concepts held by persons in the ancient world, since various earthly powers were supposed to reflect corresponding supernatural powers.\|For the most part, translators have endeavored to render the various terms in somewhat different ways, for example, ἐξουσία as ‘authority’; δύναμις as ‘power’; κυριότης as ‘ruler’; and phrases such as τὰ πνευματικὰ τῆς πονηρίας ἐν τοῖς ἐπουρανίοις as ‘wicked spiritual forces in the heavenly world.’ In a number of languages, however, there are simply not enough terms to designate various kinds of powers, authorities, and forces which could be employed in speaking of such supernatural impersonal powers. Accordingly, some translators have simply used a phrase such as ‘any and all kinds of supernatural powers.’ Where it is possible to make certain lexical distinctions between terms and phrases, this, of course, should be done, but in a number of contexts this may be impossible, and accordingly, some explanation in a marginal note may be required if the reader is to understand satisfactorily the intent of the passages in question.

[EPH 6:12](https://ref.ly/Gal6:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 6:12


## κόσμος (id: 002905000000000)

κόσμος
======

κόσμος (G2889)

noun · κοσμέω

1\.1 · Geographical Objects and Features · Universe, Creation

cosmos, universe the universe as an ordered structure In many languages there is no specific term for the universe. The closest equivalent may simply be ‘all that exists.’ In other instances one may use a phrase such as ‘the world and all that is above it’ or ‘the sky and the earth.’ The concept of the totality of the universe may be expressed in some languages only as ‘everything that is on the earth and in the sky.’

59\.55 · Quantity · Abundance, Excess, Sparing

a world of, a tremendous amount of (a figurative extension of meaning of κόσμος\[a] ‘world, universe,’ [1\.1](#1.1)) a great sum of something, implying an almost incredible totality In some languages the phrase ὁ κόσμος τῆς ἀδικίας may be rendered as ‘the very symbol of evil,’ ‘a sign of what is truly evil,’ or ‘what is completely evil.’

[JAS 3:6](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6)

12\.44 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

**Collocation:** αἰὼν τοῦ κόσμου τούτου

power, authority, lordship, ruler, wicked force title for supernatural forces and powers: a supernatural power having some particular role in controlling the destiny and activities of human beings Some scholars have believed that it is possible to reconstruct at least in part some of the hierarchy represented by these various supernatural forces and powers, on the basis of the neoplatonic system of nine such powers arranged in three orders of three each. NT terminology and usage does not, however, lend itself to such a classification, and it is difficult, if not impossible, to determine what are the significant differences between these supernatural powers and forces.\|For the most part, translators have endeavored to render the various terms in somewhat different ways, for example, ἐξουσία as ‘authority’; δύναμις as ‘power’; κυριότης as ‘ruler’; and phrases such as τὰ πνευματικὰ τῆς πονηρίας ἐν τοῖς ἐπουρανίοις as ‘wicked spiritual forces in the heavenly world.’ In a number of languages, however, there are simply not enough terms to designate various kinds of powers, authorities, and forces which could be employed in speaking of such supernatural impersonal powers. Accordingly, some translators have simply used a phrase such as ‘any and all kinds of supernatural powers.’ Where it is possible to make certain lexical distinctions between terms and phrases, this, of course, should be done, but in a number of contexts this may be impossible, and accordingly, some explanation in a marginal note may be required if the reader is to understand satisfactorily the intent of the passages in question.\|In some instances a measure of meaning may be obtained by somewhat paraphrastic expressions. For example, [EPH 2:2](https://ref.ly/Gal2:2) is rendered in some languages as ‘at that time you lived in the way in which the spirit that governs this world dictated you should live. This is the way the one who rules over the power in space commanded you to live. This is the very spirit that now commands the people who disobey God.’

[EPH 2:2](https://ref.ly/Gal2:2)

1 The occurrences of γῆ\[a], οἰκουμένη\[a], and κόσμος\[b] relate specifically to the known inhabited areas of the earth, which in the NT period included the countries bordering on the Mediterranean, the Fertile Crescent as far as the Indus Valley, and as far north in Europe as England and Scandinavia. This was the total known earth or world. Such a restriction to a known area of the earth is also true of terms used in some receptor languages, though the referents are obviously different. What is important is not the particular area of the earth, but the corresponding concept of the surface of the earth as the place of human habitation. It is possible that οἰκουμένη\[a] differs slightly in meaning from γῆ\[a] and κόσμος\[b] in view of a somewhat greater emphasis or focus upon the civilized part of earth. 2 1CO 6:2 · 1CO 6:2 It is possible to understand κόσμος in [1CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/Rom6:2) as referring to all mankind, but in view of certain contrasts which are implied in this context, it seems more satisfactory to understand κόσμος in a more limited sense of ‘people of the world.’ 3 κόσμος\[f] may be regarded as a highly generic term for any and all kinds of decorations and adornments; or it may be considered as the process whereby people may adorn themselves (see [79\.12](#79.12)). κόσμος\[f] is semantically complex, since it involves not only certain artifacts and the use of such artifacts, but also an abstract component of attractive appearance.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:21; Matthew 25:34; Luke 11:50; John 1:10; John 17:5; John 17:24; Acts 17:24; Romans 1:20; 1 Corinthians 3:22; 1 Corinthians 8:4; Ephesians 1:4; Hebrews 4:3; Hebrews 9:26; Revelation 13:8; Revelation 17:8; Matthew 4:8; Matthew 13:38; Matthew 16:26; Matthew 26:13; Mark 8:36; Mark 16:15; Luke 9:25; Luke 12:30; John 1:9; John 6:14; John 11:9; John 11:27; John 12:25; John 12:46; John 13:1; John 16:28; John 16:33; John 17:11; John 17:13; John 17:15; John 18:37; John 21:25; Romans 1:8; Romans 4:13; Romans 11:12; Romans 11:15; 1 Corinthians 1:28; 1 Corinthians 4:13; 1 Corinthians 7:34; 1 Corinthians 14:10; Colossians 1:6; 1 Timothy 1:15; 1 Timothy 3:16; 1 Timothy 6:7; Hebrews 10:5; James 2:5; 1 Peter 1:20; 1 Peter 5:9; 2 Peter 1:4; 2 Peter 2:5; 2 Peter 3:6; 1 John 2:15; 1 John 2:16; 1 John 2:17; 1 John 4:9; Revelation 11:15; John 8:23; John 9:39; John 12:31; John 14:27; John 14:30; John 15:19; John 16:11; John 17:14; John 17:16; John 18:36; 1 Corinthians 1:20; 1 Corinthians 1:21; 1 Corinthians 1:27; 1 Corinthians 2:12; 1 Corinthians 3:19; 1 Corinthians 5:10; 1 Corinthians 7:31; 1 Corinthians 7:33; 2 Corinthians 7:10; Galatians 4:3; Galatians 6:14; Ephesians 2:12; Colossians 2:8; Colossians 2:20; Hebrews 11:7; James 1:27; James 4:4; 2 Peter 2:20; 1 John 3:17; 1 John 4:4; 1 John 4:5; 1 John 4:17; 1 John 5:4; 1 John 5:5; 1 John 5:19; 2 John 1:7; Matthew 5:14; Matthew 18:7; Mark 14:9; John 1:29; John 3:16; John 3:17; John 3:19; John 4:42; John 6:33; John 6:51; John 7:4; John 7:7; John 8:12; John 8:26; John 9:5; John 10:36; John 12:19; John 12:47; John 14:17; John 14:19; John 14:22; John 14:31; John 15:18; John 16:8; John 16:20; John 16:21; John 17:6; John 17:9; John 17:18; John 17:21; John 17:23; John 17:25; John 18:20; Romans 3:6; Romans 3:19; Romans 5:12; Romans 5:13; 1 Corinthians 4:9; ## κουστωδία (id: 002908000000000)

κουστωδία
=========

κουστωδία (G2892)

noun

55\.13 · Military Activities · Army

## κόφινος (id: 002910000000000)

κόφινος
=======

κόφινος (G2894)

noun

6\.150 · Artifacts · Containers

large basket a relatively large basket used primarily for food or produce1 Translators often find it difficult to obtain satisfactory equivalents of σπυρίς ([6\.149](#6.149)) and κόφινος, since in various receptor languages there are highly specific terms for particular kinds of baskets depending upon type of construction and size. Unfortunately, there is no way of determining from the Greek text precisely the size or type of baskets involved in references to σπυρίς and κόφινος.

[MAT 14:20](https://ref.ly/Matt14:20) · [MAT 16:9](https://ref.ly/Matt16:9) · [MRK 6:43](https://ref.ly/Matt6:43) · [MRK 8:19](https://ref.ly/Matt8:19) · [LUK 9:17](https://ref.ly/Mark9:17) · [JHN 6:13](https://ref.ly/Luke6:13)

1 Neither from NT contexts nor from extrabiblical usage can one determine precisely the differences in meaning between these three terms for baskets: σαργάνη ([6\.148](#6.148)), σπυρίς ([6\.149](#6.149)), and κόφινος ([6\.150](#6.150)).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 14:20; Matthew 16:9; Mark 6:43; Mark 8:19; Luke 9:17; John 6:13


## κράβαττος (id: 002911000000000)

κράβαττος
=========

κράβαττος (G2895)

noun

6\.107 · Artifacts · Furniture

cot, pallet, stretcher a relatively small and often temporary type of object on which a person may lie or recline; made of reeds or cloth; thin and light for carrying In a number of contexts the terms κλινίδιον, κλινάριον, and κράβαττος refer to cots or stretchers on which sick or convalescent persons might be resting or on which they could be transported. There is no NT context in which these terms refer to couches on which people reclined while eating.

[MRK 2:4](https://ref.ly/Matt2:4) · [MRK 2:9](https://ref.ly/Matt2:9) · [MRK 2:11](https://ref.ly/Matt2:11) · [MRK 2:12](https://ref.ly/Matt2:12) · [MRK 6:55](https://ref.ly/Matt6:55) · [JHN 5:8](https://ref.ly/Luke5:8) · [JHN 5:9](https://ref.ly/Luke5:9) · [JHN 5:10](https://ref.ly/Luke5:10) · [JHN 5:11](https://ref.ly/Luke5:11) · [ACT 5:15](https://ref.ly/John5:15) · [ACT 9:33](https://ref.ly/John9:33)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 2:4; Mark 2:9; Mark 2:11; Mark 2:12; Mark 6:55; John 5:8; John 5:9; John 5:10; John 5:11; Acts 5:15; Acts 9:33

## κρανίον (id: 002914000000000)

κρανίον
=======

κρανίον (G2898)

noun

8\.11 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

skull (in the NT κρανίον is used only as a name for the hill of Golgotha) the bony framework of the head, especially the upper portion In rendering κρανίου τόπος ‘place of the skull’ it may be necessary to indicate clearly the relationship between place and skull. A literal rendering of such a phrase might simply mean ‘a place where there was a skull.’ However the meaning of Golgotha has been interpreted generally as ‘a hill resembling a skull’ and therefore κρανίου τόπος may be more satisfactorily rendered as ‘a place resembling a skull’ or ‘a hill looking like a skull.’ See [93\.453](#93.453).

[MAT 27:33](https://ref.ly/Matt27:33) · [MRK 15:22](https://ref.ly/Matt15:22) · [LUK 23:33](https://ref.ly/Mark23:33) · [JHN 19:17](https://ref.ly/Luke19:17)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:33; Mark 15:22; Luke 23:33; John 19:17


## κράσπεδον (id: 002915000000000)

κράσπεδον
=========

κράσπεδον (G2899)

noun

6\.180 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

fringe, edge, hem decorative tassel attached to the bottom edge of a long outer garment1 The edge of the garment designated by κράσπεδον\[a] could have been plain or decorated. In [MAT 23:5](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5) κράσπεδον denotes the tassels worn at the four corners of the outer garment (see [6\.194](#6.194)). It is also possible that in all instances in which κράσπεδον is used in reference to Jesus’ clothing, the reference may be specifically to the tassels and not merely to the fringe or edge of the garment. The interpretation of such passages depends upon how strictly Jesus may have followed the Mosaic law and the manner in which the authors may have understood the meaning of κράσπεδον.

[MAT 9:20](https://ref.ly/Matt9:20) · [MAT 14:36](https://ref.ly/Matt14:36) · [MRK 6:56](https://ref.ly/Matt6:56) · [LUK 8:44](https://ref.ly/Mark8:44)

6\.194 · Artifacts · Adornments

tassel the tassels which Jews were obliged to wear on the four corners of the outer garment (see [NUM 15:37](https://ref.ly/Num15:37)\-[NUM 15:41](https://ref.ly/Num15:41)) In some languages tassels may be described as ‘decorated corners’ or ‘ribbons at the corners.’ See the discussion at [6\.180](#6.180).

[MAT 23:5](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5)

1 It would be possible to treat κράσπεδον\[a] simply as an abstract of shape; however, since both biblical and extrabiblical uses of κράσπεδον seem primarily associated with cloth and garments, there is some justification for treating κράσπεδον\[a] in this subdomain.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:20; Matthew 14:36; Mark 6:56; Luke 8:44; Matthew 23:5

## κραταιόω (id: 002917000000000)

κραταιόω
========

κραταιόω (G2901) — κραταιόομαι

κρατέω

23\.134 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

to become strong to become strong and healthy, with the implication of physical vigor In employing an expression to translate ‘to become strong,’ it is important to avoid the impression of ‘to become muscular.’ The emphasis is upon total physical vigor, not mere muscular strength.

[LUK 2:40](https://ref.ly/Mark2:40)

76\.10 · Power, Force

to become strong, to become powerful (derivative of κραταιός ‘powerful,’ [76\.9](#76.9)) to become strong psychologically In [1CO 16:13](https://ref.ly/Rom16:13) κραταιόομαι must be understood in a non\-physical sense. The implication is that the believer is to be sufficiently strong as to be able to dominate any evil influence.

[LUK 1:80](https://ref.ly/Mark1:80) · [1CO 16:13](https://ref.ly/Rom16:13) · [EPH 3:16](https://ref.ly/Gal3:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 2:40; Luke 1:80; 1 Corinthians 16:13; Ephesians 3:16

## κρεμάννυμι (id: 002925000000000)

κρεμάννυμι
==========

κρεμάννυμι (G2910) — κρέμαμαι

ἐκκρέμαμαι · κατακρημνίζω · κρημνός

18\.23 · Attachment · Fasten, Stick To

to make to hang, to be hung from to cause to hang down from

[MAT 18:6](https://ref.ly/Matt18:6) · [MAT 22:40](https://ref.ly/Matt22:40) · [LUK 23:39](https://ref.ly/Mark23:39) · [ACT 28:4](https://ref.ly/John28:4)

20\.76 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Kill

**Collocation:** κρεμάννυμι ἐπὶ ξύλου

to crucify (an idiom, literally: to hang on a tree) to execute someone by nailing that person to a cross It is possible to understand ξύλου in [ACT 5:30](https://ref.ly/John5:30) as ξύλον\[f] ‘cross’ ([6\.28](#6.28)) and to interpret the expression literally as ‘... you seized and killed by hanging him on a cross.’

[ACT 5:30](https://ref.ly/John5:30) · [ACT 10:39](https://ref.ly/John10:39) · [GAL 3:13](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:13)

18\.22 · Attachment · Fasten, Stick To

to hang from, to hang down from to hang down from some point

[ACT 28:4](https://ref.ly/John28:4)

89\.2 · Relations · Dependency

to depend upon to be in a relation of dependency upon something In a number of languages dependency as in [MAT 22:40](https://ref.ly/Matt22:40) may be expressed as ‘to hang on’ or ‘to be tied together by’ or ‘only have meaning because of.’

[MAT 22:40](https://ref.ly/Matt22:40)

## κριθή (id: 002930000000000)

κριθή
=====

κριθή (G2915)

noun · κρίθινος

3\.44 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

barley a grain somewhat similar to wheat, but regarded as less desirable for food In a number of languages there is no specific term for barley, and therefore it may be useful simply to borrow a term from a dominant language. In certain instances, however, translators have used an expression such as ‘wheat\-like grain.’ It may even be useful to have a footnote to explain something of the nature of barley, but the fact that it was cheaper than wheat is clear from [REV 6:6](https://ref.ly/Jude6:6).

[REV 6:6](https://ref.ly/Jude6:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 6:6

## κρίμα (id: 002932000000000)

κρίμα
=====

κρίμα (G2917)

noun · κρίνω

56\.20 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judge, Condemn, Acquit

to decide a legal question, to act as a judge, making a legal decision, to arrive at a verdict, to try a case (in the passive to stand trial) to decide a question of legal right or wrong, and thus determine the innocence or guilt of the accused and assign appropriate punishment or retribution1 The process of legal judging is often expressed idiomatically. In Africa, one of the standard phrases for judging is ‘to cut a palaver,’ but other expressions in other languages may be ‘to find guilt,’ ‘to point the finger at wrong,’ or ‘to untangle strife.’

[JHN 9:39](https://ref.ly/Luke9:39) · [ACT 24:25](https://ref.ly/John24:25) · [HEB 6:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:2)

[REV 20:4](https://ref.ly/Jude20:4)

56\.24 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judge, Condemn, Acquit

verdict, sentence, judgment the legal decision rendered by a judge, whether for or against the accused

[ROM 5:16](https://ref.ly/Acts5:16) · [JAS 3:1](https://ref.ly/Heb3:1)

56\.30 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judge, Condemn, Acquit

to judge as guilty, to condemn, condemnation to judge a person to be guilty and liable to punishment2

[MAT 7:2](https://ref.ly/Matt7:2) · [MRK 12:40](https://ref.ly/Matt12:40) · [LUK 20:47](https://ref.ly/Mark20:47) · [LUK 23:40](https://ref.ly/Mark23:40) · [LUK 24:20](https://ref.ly/Mark24:20) · [ROM 2:2](https://ref.ly/Acts2:2) · [ROM 2:3](https://ref.ly/Acts2:3) · [ROM 3:8](https://ref.ly/Acts3:8) · [ROM 13:2](https://ref.ly/Acts13:2) · [1CO 11:29](https://ref.ly/Rom11:29) · [1CO 11:34](https://ref.ly/Rom11:34) · [GAL 5:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:10) · [1TI 3:6](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:6) · [1TI 5:12](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:12) · [JAS 3:1](https://ref.ly/Heb3:1) · [2PE 2:3](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:3) · [JUD 1:4](https://ref.ly/3John1:4) · [REV 17:1](https://ref.ly/Jude17:1) · [REV 18:20](https://ref.ly/Jude18:20)

56\.2 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Lawsuit, Case

lawsuit, case, legal action legal action taken in a court of law against someone3 In most languages there are technical terms for lawsuits or cases in court, but where these do not exist, one may always use a descriptive phrase, for example, ‘to accuse someone before a judge’ or ‘to argue against someone in court’ or ‘to say in court that someone has done a person harm.’

[1CO 6:7](https://ref.ly/Rom6:7)

30\.110 · Think · To Distinguish, To Evaluate, To Judge

judgment, decision, evaluation (derivative of κρίνω\[c] ‘to judge,’ [30\.108](#30.108)) the content of the process of judging

[ROM 11:33](https://ref.ly/Acts11:33) · [JAS 3:1](https://ref.ly/Heb3:1) · [1PE 4:17](https://ref.ly/Jas4:17)

1 κρίνω\[e], κρίσις\[a], and κρίμα\[a] often appear in contexts referring to the judgment of God, particularly in reference to the so\-called end times, but the limited differences in semantic components of meaning in contexts referring to God’s judgment do not warrant setting up a separate set of meanings. 2 One might argue that the meaning of κρίνω, κρίσις, and κρίμα in the cited contexts is only to make a judgment and that the negative or adverse character of the judgment depends entirely on the context. However, the frequency of the occurrence of κρίνωκρίσις, and κρίμα in the specific sense of adverse judgment or verdict of guilt is such as to justify setting up two different meanings, one involving simply the process of rendering a legal judgment ([56\.20](#56.20)) and the other, the process of legal condemnation ([56\.30](#56.30)). 3 It is possible that πρᾶγμα\[c] is somewhat more generic in meaning than κριτήριον\[b] or κρίμα\[e], but it is difficult to determine this from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** John 9:39; Acts 24:25; Hebrews 6:2; Revelation 20:4; Romans 5:16; James 3:1; Matthew 7:2; Mark 12:40; Luke 20:47; Luke 23:40; Luke 24:20; Romans 2:2; Romans 2:3; Romans 3:8; Romans 13:2; 1 Corinthians 11:29; 1 Corinthians 11:34; Galatians 5:10; 1 Timothy 3:6; 1 Timothy 5:12; 2 Peter 2:3; Jude 1:4; Revelation 17:1; Revelation 18:20; 1 Corinthians 6:7; Romans 11:33; 1 Peter 4:17

37\.49 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

to rule, to govern to rule over people Though it would be possible to understand κρίνω in [LUK 22:30](https://ref.ly/Mark22:30) as meaning ‘to judge’ (see [56\.30](#56.30)), the function of the twelve disciples seems to be far greater than that. Furthermore, there seems to be a significant Semitic influence in the meaning of κρίνω, since the corresponding Hebrew term likewise involved far more than merely making judicial decisions.

[MAT 19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28) · [LUK 22:30](https://ref.ly/Mark22:30) · [1CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/Rom6:2) · [1CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/Rom6:2)

1 It is possible that ἐπικρίνω differs from κρίνω\[a] in focusing greater attention upon what is decided. 2 The meanings of κρίνω\[c] ([30\.108](#30.108)), ἀνακρίνω\[d] and διακρίνω\[a] ([30\.109](#30.109)) are all closely related to the process of learning and of understanding, and in some contexts the meanings shade one into the other. 3 κρίνω\[e], κρίσις\[a], and κρίμα\[a] often appear in contexts referring to the judgment of God, particularly in reference to the so\-called end times, but the limited differences in semantic components of meaning in contexts referring to God’s judgment do not warrant setting up a separate set of meanings. 4 One might argue that the meaning of κρίνω, κρίσις, and κρίμα in the cited contexts is only to make a judgment and that the negative or adverse character of the judgment depends entirely on the context. However, the frequency of the occurrence of κρίνωκρίσις, and κρίμα in the specific sense of adverse judgment or verdict of guilt is such as to justify setting up two different meanings, one involving simply the process of rendering a legal judgment ([56\.20](#56.20)) and the other, the process of legal condemnation ([56\.30](#56.30)).

* **Associated Passages:** John 8:15; John 8:16; Acts 3:13; Acts 16:4; Acts 20:16; Acts 21:25; Acts 25:25; Acts 27:1; Romans 14:13; 1 Corinthians 2:2; 1 Corinthians 5:3; 1 Corinthians 7:37; 2 Corinthians 2:1; 2 Corinthians 5:14; Titus 3:12; Romans 14:5; Luke 7:43; Acts 4:19; Acts 13:46; Acts 16:15; Romans 3:4; 1 Corinthians 10:15; 1 Corinthians 11:13; Acts 15:19; Acts 26:8; Luke 12:57; Luke 19:22; John 5:22; John 5:30; John 8:26; John 8:50; John 18:31; Acts 17:31; Acts 23:3; Acts 23:6; Acts 24:21; Acts 25:9; Acts 25:10; Acts 25:20; Acts 26:6; Romans 2:12; Romans 2:16; Romans 3:6; Romans 3:7; 1 Corinthians 4:5; 1 Corinthians 6:1; 1 Corinthians 6:3; 1 Corinthians 6:6; 1 Corinthians 11:31; 1 Corinthians 11:32; 2 Thessalonians 2:12; 2 Timothy 4:1; Hebrews 10:30; Hebrews 13:4; James 2:12; 1 Peter 1:17; 1 Peter 2:23; 1 Peter 4:5; Revelation 6:10; Revelation 11:18; Revelation 16:5; Revelation 18:8; Revelation 19:11; Revelation 20:12; Revelation 20:13; Matthew 5:40; Matthew 7:1; Matthew 7:2; Luke 6:37; John 3:17; John 3:18; John 7:24; John 7:51; John 12:47; John 12:48; John 16:11; Acts 7:7; Acts 13:27; Romans 2:1; Romans 2:3; Romans 2:27; Romans 14:3; Romans 14:4; Romans 14:10; Romans 14:22; 1 Corinthians 5:12; 1 Corinthians 5:13; 1 Corinthians 6:2; 1 Corinthians 10:29; Colossians 2:16; James 4:11; James 4:12; James 5:9; 1 Peter 4:6; Revelation 18:20; Revelation 19:2; Matthew 19:28; Luke 22:30

56\.20 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judge, Condemn, Acquit

30\.110 · Think · To Distinguish, To Evaluate, To Judge

judgment, decision, evaluation (derivative of κρίνω\[c] ‘to judge,’ [30\.108](#30.108)) the content of the process of judging It may also be possible to translate ἀλλὰ τὴν δικαίαν κρίσιν κρίνετε ([JHN 7:24](https://ref.ly/Luke7:24)) as ‘judge in a righteous manner’ or ‘judge according to true standards.’

[MAT 12:41](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41) · [MAT 12:42](https://ref.ly/Matt12:42) · [LUK 10:14](https://ref.ly/Mark10:14) · [LUK 11:31](https://ref.ly/Mark11:31) · [LUK 11:32](https://ref.ly/Mark11:32) · [JHN 7:24](https://ref.ly/Luke7:24) · [JHN 8:16](https://ref.ly/Luke8:16) · [JHN 16:8](https://ref.ly/Luke16:8) · [JHN 16:11](https://ref.ly/Luke16:11) · [HEB 9:27](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:27) · [HEB 10:27](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:27) · [1JN 4:17](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:17) · [REV 16:7](https://ref.ly/Jude16:7) · [REV 19:2](https://ref.ly/Jude19:2)

30\.111 · Think · To Distinguish, To Evaluate, To Judge

basis of judging, basis for judgment the basis for rendering a judgment It is also possible to render κρίσις in [JHN 3:19](https://ref.ly/Luke3:19) as ‘how judgment works’ or ‘the reason for God judging.’

[JHN 3:19](https://ref.ly/Luke3:19)

38\.1 · Punish, Reward · Punish

punishment punishment, with the implication of having been judged guilty It is also possible, of course, to interpret κρίσις in [MAT 23:33](https://ref.ly/Matt23:33) as meaning ‘condemnation’ (see [56\.30](#56.30)), but as such, punishment is certainly implied.

[MAT 23:33](https://ref.ly/Matt23:33) · [HEB 10:27](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:27) · [REV 18:10](https://ref.ly/Jude18:10)

56\.32 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judge, Condemn, Acquit

**Collocation:** ὑπὸ κρίσιν πίπτω

to be condemned, to suffer condemnation, to be judged guilty (an idiom, literally: to fall under judgment) to be condemned for acting contrary to laws and regulations In the context of [JAS 5:12](https://ref.ly/Heb5:12) the condemnation refers to God’s judgment.

[JAS 5:12](https://ref.ly/Heb5:12)

1 κρίνω\[e], κρίσις\[a], and κρίμα\[a] often appear in contexts referring to the judgment of God, particularly in reference to the so\-called end times, but the limited differences in semantic components of meaning in contexts referring to God’s judgment do not warrant setting up a separate set of meanings. 2 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning in these terms (ἀγοραῖος\[b], κριτήριον\[a], κρίσις\[c], ἡμέρα\[e]), especially in their connotations, but it is not possible to specify the difference on the basis of existing contexts. 3 MAT 5:21 In [MAT 5:21](https://ref.ly/Matt5:21) κρίσις probably refers to a local court of justice. 4 One might argue that the meaning of κρίνω, κρίσις, and κρίμα in the cited contexts is only to make a judgment and that the negative or adverse character of the judgment depends entirely on the context. However, the frequency of the occurrence of κρίνωκρίσις, and κρίμα in the specific sense of adverse judgment or verdict of guilt is such as to justify setting up two different meanings, one involving simply the process of rendering a legal judgment ([56\.20](#56.20)) and the other, the process of legal condemnation ([56\.30](#56.30)).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:15; Matthew 11:22; Matthew 11:24; Matthew 12:36; John 5:24; John 5:27; John 12:31; James 2:13; 2 Peter 2:4; 2 Peter 2:9; 2 Peter 3:7; Revelation 14:7; John 5:22; Matthew 5:21; Matthew 5:22; John 5:30; 2 Thessalonians 1:5; Matthew 23:33; John 5:29; 1 Timothy 5:24; Hebrews 10:27; James 5:12; 2 Peter 2:11; Jude 1:6; Jude 1:9; Jude 1:15; Matthew 12:18; Matthew 12:20; Matthew 23:23; Luke 11:42; Acts 8:33; Matthew 12:41; Matthew 12:42; Luke 10:14; Luke 11:31; Luke 11:32; John 7:24; John 8:16; John 16:8; John 16:11; Hebrews 9:27; 1 John 4:17; Revelation 16:7; Revelation 19:2; John 3:19; Revelation 18:10

## κριτήριον (id: 002937000000000)

κριτήριον
=========

κριτήριον (G2922)

noun · κρίνω

56\.1 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Court of Justice

court, court of justice a court of justice for determining guilt or innocence1 For languages which do not have technical terms for a court, it is usually possible to use some such phrase as ‘to be brought before a judge’ or ‘to have judges decide one’s case.’

[JAS 2:6](https://ref.ly/Heb2:6)

56\.2 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Lawsuit, Case

lawsuit, case, legal action legal action taken in a court of law against someone2 In most languages there are technical terms for lawsuits or cases in court, but where these do not exist, one may always use a descriptive phrase, for example, ‘to accuse someone before a judge’ or ‘to argue against someone in court’ or ‘to say in court that someone has done a person harm.’

[1CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/Rom6:2) · [1CO 6:4](https://ref.ly/Rom6:4)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning in these terms, especially in their connotations, but it is not possible to specify the difference on the basis of existing contexts. 2 It is possible that πρᾶγμα\[c] is somewhat more generic in meaning than κριτήριον\[b] or κρίμα\[e], but it is difficult to determine this from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** James 2:6; 1 Corinthians 6:2; 1 Corinthians 6:4

## κρούω (id: 002940000000000)

κρούω
=====

κρούω (G2925)

19\.12 · Physical Impact · Hit, Strike

to knock to knock on a door, as a means of signaling one’s presence to those inside A literal rendering of κρούω in [MAT 7:7](https://ref.ly/Matt7:7) may be misleading in a number of languages, since in some areas only thieves knock on doors. This is done in order to determine whether anyone is at home, in which case, of course, the thief runs off. The more general practice for signaling one’s presence may be to cough, to clap the hands, or to call out one’s name.

[MAT 7:7](https://ref.ly/Matt7:7)1 · [MAT 7:8](https://ref.ly/Matt7:8) · [LUK 11:9](https://ref.ly/Mark11:9) · [LUK 11:10](https://ref.ly/Mark11:10) · [LUK 12:36](https://ref.ly/Mark12:36) · [LUK 13:25](https://ref.ly/Mark13:25) · [ACT 12:13](https://ref.ly/John12:13) · [ACT 12:16](https://ref.ly/John12:16) · [REV 3:20](https://ref.ly/Jude3:20)

1 MAT 7:7 In view of the fact that κρούω in [MAT 7:7](https://ref.ly/Matt7:7) involves an act of communication, it would be possible to classify this meaning of κρούω in Domain 33 Communication, but since the action of κρούω involves physical impact, it is listed here in Domain 19\.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:7; Matthew 7:8; Luke 11:9; Luke 11:10; Luke 12:36; Luke 13:25; Acts 12:13; Acts 12:16; Revelation 3:20

## κρυπτός (id: 002942000000000)

κρυπτός
=======

κρυπτός (G2927)

adj · κρύπτω

28\.69 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

secret, hidden, not able to be made known pertaining to not being able to be known, in view of the fact that it has been kept secret In a number of languages there may be complications involved in what could be regarded as a triple negation in the sense that ‘nothing,’ ‘secret’ (in the sense of ‘not known’), and ‘not be made known’ are all semantic negations. It may therefore be better to render [MAT 10:26](https://ref.ly/Matt10:26) as ‘everything that is now not known will be made known.’\|In a number of languages ‘secret’ is regularly expressed as ‘not known’ or ‘what is kept from being known.’

[MAT 6:4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:4) · [MAT 6:4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:4) · [MAT 6:6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6) · [MAT 6:6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6) · [MAT 10:26](https://ref.ly/Matt10:26) · [MRK 4:22](https://ref.ly/Matt4:22) · [LUK 8:17](https://ref.ly/Mark8:17) · [LUK 12:2](https://ref.ly/Mark12:2) · [JHN 7:4](https://ref.ly/Luke7:4) · [JHN 7:10](https://ref.ly/Luke7:10) · [JHN 18:20](https://ref.ly/Luke18:20) · [2CO 4:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:2)

26\.1 · Psychological Faculties

**Collocation:** ὁ ἐν τῷ κρυπτῷ (ἄνθρωπος)

the inner being, the inmost being, inwardly (idiom, literally: the hidden (person)) the psychological faculty, including intellectual, emotional, and spiritual aspects, in contrast with the purely physical aspects of human existence A strictly literal rendering of ἀλλ ὁ ἐν τῷ κρυπτῷ Ἰουδαῖος might be misunderstood in [ROM 2:29](https://ref.ly/Acts2:29) to refer only to the fact of circumcision, which would be something which would normally not be evident.\|In a number of languages it is quite impossible to speak of the psychological faculty of a person as being merely ‘that which is within.’ It is frequently necessary to refer to a particular organ of the body, for example, ‘the heart’ or ‘the liver’ or ‘the spleen.’ In some languages, however, one may refer to this faculty as being ‘the person who stands inside’ or ‘the real person’ or even ‘the other person.’\|In [LUK 17:21](https://ref.ly/Mark17:21) the phrase ἐντὸς ὑμῶν in the statement ἰδοὺ γὰρ ἡ βασιλεία τοῦ θεοῦ ἐντὸς ὑμῶν ἐστιν ‘look, God’s reign is within you’ may constitute a reference to the same inner being designated by the phrases ὁ ἔσω and ὁ ἐν τῷ κρυπτῷ. On this basis some scholars have suggested that the phrase ἐντὸς ὑμῶν can be interpreted as a potentiality for participation and hence be translated ‘within your grasp,’ but it is more likely that one should understand the phrase ἐντὸς ὑμῶν in [LUK 17:21](https://ref.ly/Mark17:21) as a spacial relationship, for example, ‘in your midst’ or ‘among you’ (see [83\.9](#83.9)).

[ROM 2:29](https://ref.ly/Acts2:29) · [1PE 3:4](https://ref.ly/Jas3:4)

28\.75 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

**Collocation:** τὰ κρυπτά

secret information, secret knowledge, secrets the content of what is not able to be known

[ROM 2:16](https://ref.ly/Acts2:16) · [1CO 4:5](https://ref.ly/Rom4:5) · [1CO 14:25](https://ref.ly/Rom14:25)

28\.71 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

**Collocation:** ἐν τῷ κρυπτῷ

in secret, in private, secretly, privately pertaining to not being able to be known by the public but known by some in\-group or by those immediately involved

[MAT 6:4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:4) · [MAT 6:4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:4) · [MAT 6:6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6) · [MAT 6:6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6) · [JHN 7:4](https://ref.ly/Luke7:4) · [JHN 7:10](https://ref.ly/Luke7:10) · [JHN 18:20](https://ref.ly/Luke18:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 6:4; Matthew 6:6; Matthew 10:26; Mark 4:22; Luke 8:17; Luke 12:2; John 7:4; John 7:10; John 18:20; 2 Corinthians 4:2; Romans 2:29; 1 Peter 3:4; Romans 2:16; 1 Corinthians 4:5; 1 Corinthians 14:25


## κρύπτω (id: 002943000000000)

κρύπτω
======

κρύπτω (G2928)

ἀποκρύπτω · ἀπόκρυφος · ἐγκρύπτω · κρύπτη · κρυπτός · κρυφαῖος · κρυφῇ · περικρύβω

21\.12 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Safe, Free from Danger

to keep safe, to cause to be protected, to protect, to hide to cause to be safe or protected by hiding, in some contexts with the intent of not being found Since κρύπτω also means ‘to make invisible,’ some scholars believe that this statement in [COL 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phil3:3) means that ‘your life is concealed in Christ’ or ‘... hidden from view ...’ (see [24\.30](#24.30)). For another interpretation of κρύπτω in [MAT 13:44](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44), see [24\.29](#24.29).

[MAT 13:44](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44) · [MAT 25:18](https://ref.ly/Matt25:18) · [MAT 25:25](https://ref.ly/Matt25:25) · [JHN 8:59](https://ref.ly/Luke8:59) · [JHN 12:36](https://ref.ly/Luke12:36) · [COL 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phil3:3) · [HEB 11:23](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:23) · [REV 6:15](https://ref.ly/Jude6:15) · [REV 6:16](https://ref.ly/Jude6:16)

24\.29 · Sensory Events and States · See

to make invisible, to hide to cause something to be invisible, with the intent of its being not found For another interpretation of κρύπτω in [MAT 13:44](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44), see [21\.12](#21.12).

[MAT 5:14](https://ref.ly/Matt5:14) · [MAT 13:44](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44) · [1TI 5:25](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:25)

24\.30 · Sensory Events and States · See

to hide, to make invisible, to make hidden and safe to cause something to be invisible (in the sense of being hidden), but for the purpose of safekeeping and protection The evident implication of this statement in [COL 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phil3:3) is to emphasize the fact that the true life of the believer is not some material, visible object or happening, but something spiritual and thus only visible to those spiritually enlightened or concerned. For another interpretation of κρύπτω in [COL 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phil3:3), see [21\.12](#21.12).

[MAT 13:44](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44) · [COL 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phil3:3)

28\.79 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

to hide, to keep secret, to conceal to cause something not to be known1 In a number of languages, the causative relationships involved in [MAT 11:25](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25) must be made somewhat more explicit, for example, ‘because you have kept the wise and learned people from knowing and have caused the unlearned to know.’ In [MAT 11:25](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25) νήπιος is used figuratively in reference to unlearned people.

[MAT 11:25](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25) · [MAT 13:35](https://ref.ly/Matt13:35) · [LUK 18:34](https://ref.ly/Mark18:34) · [LUK 19:42](https://ref.ly/Mark19:42) · [JHN 19:38](https://ref.ly/Luke19:38) · [REV 2:17](https://ref.ly/Jude2:17)

1 The series of meanings in [28\.79](#28.79) differs significantly from the meaning of ἐγκρύπτω in [85\.50](#85.50). In [28\.79](#28.79) the focus in concealment is upon preventing knowledge about something, while in [85\.50](#85.50) the concealment focuses upon something being in a place where it is no longer visible.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:44; Matthew 25:18; Matthew 25:25; John 8:59; John 12:36; Colossians 3:3; Hebrews 11:23; Revelation 6:15; Revelation 6:16; Matthew 5:14; 1 Timothy 5:25; Matthew 11:25; Matthew 13:35; Luke 18:34; Luke 19:42; John 19:38; Revelation 2:17

## κρύσταλλος (id: 002945000000000)

κρύσταλλος
==========

κρύσταλλος (G2930)

noun · κρυσταλλίζω

2\.46 · Natural Substances · Precious and Semiprecious Stones and Substances

crystal a very hard, translucent, and usually transparent type of quartz The equivalent of ‘crystal’ is often a descriptive phrase such as ‘a brilliant stone’ or ‘a shining stone’ or ‘a glass\-like stone.’ In developing a satisfactory term for crystal, it is important to avoid possible confusion with diamond.\|Some scholars, however, interpret κρύσταλλος in [REV 4:6](https://ref.ly/Jude4:6) as being a reference to ice (see [2\.11](#2.11)).

[REV 4:6](https://ref.ly/Jude4:6)

2\.11 · Natural Substances · Water

ice frozen water In both [REV 4:6](https://ref.ly/Jude4:6) and [REV 22:1](https://ref.ly/Jude22:1) (the only two passages in which κρύσταλλος occurs in the NT) the meaning may, however, be ‘rock crystal’ rather than ‘ice’ (see [2\.46](#2.46)).\|Though in the Arctic regions people may have a number of different terms for various kinds and forms of ice, there are many areas in the world in which there is no existing local term for ‘ice.’ Sometimes a descriptive phrase such as ‘hardened water’ is employed, and in a number of languages a term is simply borrowed from a dominant language of the region. However, in [REV 4:6](https://ref.ly/Jude4:6) and [REV 22:1](https://ref.ly/Jude22:1) it is possible to focus upon the brilliance of color rather than the particular substance and thus to speak of λαμπρὸς ὡς κρύσταλλος as ‘that which is sparkling white’ or ‘... bright white.’

[REV 4:6](https://ref.ly/Jude4:6) · [REV 22:1](https://ref.ly/Jude22:1)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 4:6; Revelation 22:1

## κτάομαι (id: 002948000000000)

κτάομαι
=======

κτάομαι (G2932)

κτῆμα · κτῆνος · κτήτωρ

57\.58 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Take, Obtain, Gain, Lose

to get, to acquire, to gain to acquire possession of something1

[MAT 10:9](https://ref.ly/Matt10:9) · [LUK 18:12](https://ref.ly/Mark18:12) · [ACT 1:18](https://ref.ly/John1:18) · [ACT 8:20](https://ref.ly/John8:20) · [ACT 22:28](https://ref.ly/John22:28) · [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4)

21\.20 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Cause To Be Safe, Free from Danger

**Collocation:** κτάομαι τὴν ψυχήν

to save oneself, to protect oneself (an idiom, literally: to acquire one’s soul, or: to acquire one’s life) to save oneself from grave danger or death

[LUK 21:19](https://ref.ly/Mark21:19)

23\.63 · Physiological Processes and States · Sexual Relations

**Collocation:** σκεῦος κτάομαι

sexual life (an idiom, literally: to possess a vessel) a euphemistic manner of referring to sexual relations It is also possible to understand σκεῦος in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) as one’s wife (see [10\.55](#10.55)). σκεῦος in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) may also be understood as one’s body, and therefore the phrase τὸ ἑαυτοῦ σκεῦος κτᾶσθαι may be rendered as ‘to control his own body’ (see [8\.6](#8.6)).

[1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4)

1 In several contexts κτάομαι refers to the acquiring of some possession or benefit by means of payment of money, as in [ACT 8:20](https://ref.ly/John8:20) (τὴν δωρεὰν τοῦ θεοῦ ἐνόμισας διὰ χρημάτων κτᾶσθαι you thought you could acquire God’s gift with money), but κτάομαι in itself does not mean to buy but simply to acquire, and if the reference is to buying, then the context must indicate the use of money as a means of acquisition.

## κτῆνος (id: 002950000000000)

κτῆνος
======

κτῆνος (G2934)

noun · κτάομαι

4\.6 · Animals · Animals

beast of burden, riding animal, cattle a larger type of domesticated animal, primarily one used for riding or carrying loads In [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) (ἄλλη δὲ σὰρξ κτηνῶν, ἄλλη δὲ σὰρξ πτηνῶν, ἄλλη δὲ ἰχθύων ‘another is the flesh of animals, another the flesh of birds, and another the flesh of fish’) one might argue that κτηνῶν is simply a highly generic expression for all kinds of animals, but in view of its meaning in so many other contexts, it probably applies even in [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) to large domesticated animals.\|As in so many instances, the translator must render passages in terms of expressions which are appropriate to particular contexts. For example, in [ACT 23:24](https://ref.ly/John23:24) a translation such as ‘horses’ would be appropriate, while in [LUK 10:34](https://ref.ly/Mark10:34) the term ‘donkey’ would be fitting, and in [REV 18:13](https://ref.ly/Jude18:13) κτήνη (in which κτῆνος contrasts with πρόβατα ‘sheep’) would perhaps best be translated as ‘cattle.’

[LUK 10:34](https://ref.ly/Mark10:34) · [ACT 23:24](https://ref.ly/John23:24) · [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) · [REV 18:13](https://ref.ly/Jude18:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 10:34; Acts 23:24; 1 Corinthians 15:39; Revelation 18:13


## κτήτωρ (id: 002951000000000)

κτήτωρ

## κτίσις (id: 002953000000000)

κτίσις
======

κτίσις (G2937)

noun · κτίζω

42\.35 · Perform, Do · Make, Create

creation (in the NT, used exclusively of God’s activity in creation) act of making or creating something which has not existed before

[MRK 10:6](https://ref.ly/Matt10:6) · [MRK 13:19](https://ref.ly/Matt13:19) · [ROM 1:20](https://ref.ly/Acts1:20) · [HEB 9:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:11) · [2PE 3:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:4)

42\.38 · Perform, Do · Make, Create

creation, creature, what has been created that which has been created

[MRK 16:15](https://ref.ly/Matt16:15) · [ROM 1:25](https://ref.ly/Acts1:25) · [ROM 8:39](https://ref.ly/Acts8:39) · [2CO 5:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:17) · [GAL 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:15) · [COL 1:15](https://ref.ly/Phil1:15) · [COL 1:23](https://ref.ly/Phil1:23) · [HEB 4:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:13)

1\.4 · Geographical Objects and Features · Universe, Creation

universe, creation, what was made the universe as the product of God’s activity in creation The meaning of κτίσις\[c] might very well be treated as a simple derivative of the verb κτίζω ‘to create’ ([42\.35](#42.35)), since the reference is to the result of God’s creative act. However, in a number of contexts, the process of creation is no longer focal, and what is in focus is the total physical universe. In some languages the meaning may be best expressed as ‘the world and all that is in it’ or even ‘everything that exists.’

[ROM 8:19](https://ref.ly/Acts8:19) · [ROM 8:20](https://ref.ly/Acts8:20) · [ROM 8:21](https://ref.ly/Acts8:21) · [ROM 8:22](https://ref.ly/Acts8:22) · [REV 3:14](https://ref.ly/Jude3:14)

42\.39 · Perform, Do · Make, Create

institution, structure (derivative of κτίζω ‘to create,’ [42\.35](#42.35)) a human institution or social structure as something which has been created It is possible that κτίσις in [1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13) may have the implication of authorized institution. It might even be possible to render κτίσις in such a context as ‘authority’ (compare κτίσις\[e] in [37\.43](#37.43)).

[1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13)1

37\.43 · Control, Rule · Exercise Authority

authority an instituted authority, with the implication that such an authority has been created or formed The expression ‘human authority’ may be rendered as ‘every person who has the right to rule.’ For another interpretation of κτίσις in [1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13), see [42\.39](#42.39).

[1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13)1

1 1PE 2:13 The meaning of κτίσις in [1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13) is by no means certain. Scholarly opinion is seriously divided in view of the obscurity of reference.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 10:6; Mark 13:19; Romans 1:20; Hebrews 9:11; 2 Peter 3:4; Mark 16:15; Romans 1:25; Romans 8:39; 2 Corinthians 5:17; Galatians 6:15; Colossians 1:15; Colossians 1:23; Hebrews 4:13; Romans 8:19; Romans 8:20; Romans 8:21; Romans 8:22; Revelation 3:14; 1 Peter 2:13

## κυκλόω (id: 002961000000000)

κυκλόω
======

κυκλόω (G2944)

κυκλεύω · κυκλόθεν · κύκλῳ · περικυκλόω

15\.146 · Linear Movement · Go Around, Surround

to go around to move around an object A strictly literal translation of the Greek text of [HEB 11:30](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:30) may be extremely difficult, since it is usually necessary to employ an active form involving movement so as to specify what entities go around. Therefore, it may be preferable to translate ‘the walls of Jericho fell after the Israelites had gone around them for seven days.’

[HEB 11:30](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:30)

15\.147 · Linear Movement · Go Around, Surround

to surround, to be around to move in such a way as to encircle an object1

[LUK 21:20](https://ref.ly/Mark21:20) · [JHN 10:24](https://ref.ly/Luke10:24) · [ACT 14:20](https://ref.ly/John14:20)

1 It is possible that περικυκλόω is somewhat more emphatic than κυκλόω\[b] and κυκλεύω in emphasizing the fact of being surrounded.

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 11:30; Luke 21:20; John 10:24; Acts 14:20

## κυλισμός (id: 002963000000000)

κυλισμός
========

κυλισμός (G2946)

noun · κυλίομαι

16\.17 · Non\-Linear Movement

to roll about, to wallow the motion of an object rolling back and forth or rolling about1 It is rare that one can use in a language the same or related terms for the rolling of a person in an epileptic fit and the wallowing of a pig in the mud. The first is chaotic and uncontrolled, while the second is both purposeful and slower.

[2PE 2:22](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:22)

1 It is, of course, impossible for an object to roll without some movement in space; however, the focus here is not upon the linear movement of an object from one place to another by means of rolling, but simply the motion in and of itself, and any movement in space is irrelevant.

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 2:22

## κύμινον (id: 002968000000000)

κύμινον
=======

κύμινον (G2951)

noun

3\.25 · Plants · Plants That Are Not Trees

cumin probably the plant Cuminum cyminum; same family as carrot; branches from the base and has similar leaves and flowers, though seeds have a sharper smell; planted and harvested each year, reaching a height of about 50–60 cm; seeds are used in cooking and as medicine In designating ‘cumin’ as well as ἄνηθον ‘dill,’ πήγανον ‘rue,’ and ἡδύοσμον ‘mint,’ it is probably wise to borrow a term and use a classifier, for example, ‘a seasoning herb called cumin.’

[MAT 23:23](https://ref.ly/Matt23:23)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:23

## κυριακός (id: 002977000000000)

κυριακός
========

adj · κυριεύω

12\.10 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

belonging to the Lord, Lord’s (derivative of κύριος\[a] ‘Lord,’ [12\.9](#12.9)) pertaining to the Lord A strictly literal rendering of ‘the Lord’s Supper’ might simply mean ‘the supper which the Lord ate,’ implying that no one else participated. Therefore, it may be necessary in some languages to translate ‘the meal at which the Lord presided’ or ‘the meal which the Lord had for his disciples’ or ‘the meal which the Lord ate with his followers.’

## κύριος (id: 002979000000000)

κύριος
======

κύριος (G2962)

noun · κυριεύω

12\.9{N:001} · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

Lord, Ruler, One who commands (a title for God and for Christ) one who exercises supernatural authority over mankind (see also [37\.51](#37.51)) The most common equivalent of ‘Lord’ is a term meaning ‘chief’ or ‘leader,’ but frequently this cannot be employed as a title for ‘God.’ One may, however, combine such an expression with a term for ‘God’ and employ a phrase meaning ‘God our leader’ or ‘God our chief.’ In some instances, however, a term for ‘Lord’ is related to a verb meaning ‘to command’ or ‘to order,’ and therefore ‘Lord’ is rendered as ‘the one who commands us’ and combined with ‘God’ may form a phrase such as ‘God, the one who commands us.’

[MAT 1:20](https://ref.ly/Matt1:20) · [MAT 1:22](https://ref.ly/Matt1:22) · [MAT 1:24](https://ref.ly/Matt1:24) · [MAT 2:13](https://ref.ly/Matt2:13) · [MAT 2:15](https://ref.ly/Matt2:15) · [MAT 57\.12 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Have, Possess, Property, Owner

owner, master, lord one who owns and controls property, including especially servants and slaves, with important supplementary semantic components of high status and respect

37\.51 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

ruler, master, lord one who rules or exercises authority over others For the meaning of κύριος as a title for God or for Christ, see [12\.9](#12.9).

87\.53 · Status · High Status or Rank \[including persons of high status]

sir, mister a title of respect used in addressing or speaking of a man

87\.56 · Status · High Status or Rank \[including persons of high status]

**Collocation:** τῷ ἰδίῳ κυρίῳ στήκει ἢ πίπτει

honor or disgrace depends on the person whom one serves (an idiom, literally: to his own master he stands or falls, probably a familiar adage) whether one maintains one’s status or relationship to a master depends on the master's judgment or evaluation

[ROM 14:4](https://ref.ly/Acts14:4)

1 Items [12\.4](#12.4)\-[12\.8](#12.8), ([12\.9](#12.9)), and [12\.12](#12.12) in this domain are titles for θεός\[a] God ([12\.1](#12.1)). As titles, they have precisely the same reference as θεός\[a], but they each contribute distinctive meanings which are legitimate qualifications of the referent in question.

## κυριότης (id: 002980000000000)

κυριότης
========

κυριότης (G2963)

noun · κυριεύω

37\.52 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

ruling power (derivative of κύριος\[c] ‘one who rules,’ [37\.51](#37.51)) a supernatural ruling power In general, the series of terms θρόνοι, κυριότητες, ἀρχαί, and ἐξουσίαι in [COL 1:16](https://ref.ly/Phil1:16) (as well as in [EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21)) are understood as being supernatural cosmic powers, whether angelic or demonic (see [12\.44](#12.44)), but it is possible that these should be understood in terms of human rulers.

[EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21) · [COL 1:16](https://ref.ly/Phil1:16) · [2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10) · [JUD 1:8](https://ref.ly/3John1:8)

12\.44 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

power, authority, lordship, ruler, wicked force (title for supernatural forces and powers) a supernatural power having some particular role in controlling the destiny and activities of human beings Some scholars have believed that it is possible to reconstruct at least in part some of the hierarchy represented by these various supernatural forces and powers, on the basis of the neoplatonic system of nine such powers arranged in three orders of three each. NT terminology and usage does not, however, lend itself to such a classification, and it is difficult, if not impossible, to determine what are the significant differences between these supernatural powers and forces.\|In the case of [EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21) some scholars apply the terms in question both to the supernatural and to the human sphere, thus emphasizing the totality of Christ’s rule. This has a considerable measure of justification in view of the concepts held by persons in the ancient world, since various earthly powers were supposed to reflect corresponding supernatural powers.\|For the most part, translators have endeavored to render the various terms in somewhat different ways, for example, ἐξουσία as ‘authority’; δύναμις as ‘power’; κυριότης as ‘ruler’; and phrases such as τὰ πνευματικὰ τῆς πονηρίας ἐν τοῖς ἐπουρανίοις as ‘wicked spiritual forces in the heavenly world.’ In a number of languages, however, there are simply not enough terms to designate various kinds of powers, authorities, and forces which could be employed in speaking of such supernatural impersonal powers. Accordingly, some translators have simply used a phrase such as ‘any and all kinds of supernatural powers.’ Where it is possible to make certain lexical distinctions between terms and phrases, this, of course, should be done, but in a number of contexts this may be impossible, and accordingly, some explanation in a marginal note may be required if the reader is to understand satisfactorily the intent of the passages in question.

[EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21) · [COL 1:16](https://ref.ly/Phil1:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 1:21; Colossians 1:16; 2 Peter 2:10; Jude 1:8


## κυρόω (id: 002981000000000)

κυρόω
=====

κυρόω (G2964)

κυριεύω

76\.18 · Power, Force

to give force to, to validate to invest something with power or force In order to express the meaning of this phrase in [GAL 3:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:15), it may be necessary in some languages to make more specific the arrangements involved, for example, ‘if people have signed an agreement, no one can disregard it’ or ‘if an agreement has been confirmed, no one can say it does not exist’ or, as in some languages, ‘if an agreement has been tied, no one can untie it.’

[GAL 3:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:15)

70\.6 · Real, Unreal

to show something to be real, to make something real to cause someone to recognize the reality of something

[2CO 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Galatians 3:15; 2 Corinthians 2:8


## κύων (id: 002982000000000)

κύων
====

κύων (G2965)

noun · κυνάριον

4\.34 · Animals · Animals

dog relatively small light brown domestic animal, feeding on anything from household refuse to animal carcasses and excreta; Canis familiaris putiatini; associated with all sorts of uncleanness, aggression, greediness, low status In Greek outside the NT κύων may be either masculine or feminine and in the plural may refer to both male and female dogs.

[MAT 7:6](https://ref.ly/Matt7:6) · [LUK 16:21](https://ref.ly/Mark16:21) · [2PE 2:22](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:22)

88\.122 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Bad, Evil, Harmful, Damaging

bad person, dog (a figurative extension of meaning of κύων\[a] ‘dog,’ [4\.34](#4.34)) a particularly bad person, perhaps specifically one who ridicules what is holy It is also possible that κύων in [PHP 3:2](https://ref.ly/Eph3:2) may be interpreted as meaning ‘pervert’ (see [88\.282](#88.282)).\|A term for ‘dog’ may have quite a different connotation than it does in English. For example, to call a person ‘a dog’ in some languages is to compliment him for his faithfulness, but in other languages it may be merely a way of attributing promiscuous sexual behavior.

[PHP 3:2](https://ref.ly/Eph3:2) · [REV 22:15](https://ref.ly/Jude22:15)

88\.282 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

pervert (a figurative extension of meaning of κύων\[a] ‘dog,’ [4\.34](#4.34)) one who is a sexual pervert or possibly one who is sexually promiscuous It is also possible, however, that in [REV 22:15](https://ref.ly/Jude22:15) κύων means ‘a wicked person’ who might have complete contempt for what is holy, a meaning which parallels the significance of the adage in [MAT 7:6](https://ref.ly/Matt7:6) (see [88\.122](#88.122)).

[PHP 3:2](https://ref.ly/Eph3:2) · [REV 22:15](https://ref.ly/Jude22:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:6; Luke 16:21; 2 Peter 2:22; Philippians 3:2; Revelation 22:15


## κῶλον (id: 002983000000000)

κῶλον
=====

κῶλον (G2966)

noun

8\.8 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Body

dead body, corpse the dead body of a person, especially one which is still unburied1 Though in [HEB 3:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:17) the Greek text reads literally ‘whose dead bodies fell in the wilderness,’ it would normally be a mistake to translate this clause literally, since it might suggest that the people died while they were still standing, and that only the corpses fell. A more natural equivalent is ‘they died in the wilderness’ or ‘they died and their bodies lay in the wilderness.’

[HEB 3:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:17)

1 In earlier Greek κῶλον designated a limb, but in the NT it occurs only in the plural and means corpses.

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 3:17


## κωλύω (id: 002984000000000)

κωλύω
=====

κωλύω (G2967)

ἀκωλύτως · διακωλύω · δύσκολος · δυσκόλως

13\.146 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Happen

to prevent, to hinder to cause something not to happen1

[MAT 19:14](https://ref.ly/Matt19:14) · [MRK 9:38](https://ref.ly/Matt9:38) · [MRK 9:39](https://ref.ly/Matt9:39) · [MRK 10:14](https://ref.ly/Matt10:14) · [LUK 6:29](https://ref.ly/Mark6:29) · [LUK 9:49](https://ref.ly/Mark9:49) · [LUK 9:50](https://ref.ly/Mark9:50) · [LUK 11:52](https://ref.ly/Mark11:52) · [LUK 18:16](https://ref.ly/Mark18:16) · [LUK 23:2](https://ref.ly/Mark23:2) · [ACT 8:36](https://ref.ly/John8:36) · [ACT 10:47](https://ref.ly/John10:47) · [ACT 11:17](https://ref.ly/John11:17) · [ACT 16:6](https://ref.ly/John16:6) · [ACT 24:23](https://ref.ly/John24:23) · [ACT 27:43](https://ref.ly/John27:43) · [ROM 1:13](https://ref.ly/Acts1:13) · [1CO 14:39](https://ref.ly/Rom14:39) · [1TH 2:16](https://ref.ly/Col2:16) · [1TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:3) · [HEB 7:23](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:23) · [2PE 2:16](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:16) · [3JN 1:10](https://ref.ly/2John1:10)

1 διακωλύω may be somewhat stronger in meaning than κωλύω, but this cannot be determined on the basis of existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 19:14; Mark 9:38; Mark 9:39; Mark 10:14; Luke 6:29; Luke 9:49; Luke 9:50; Luke 11:52; Luke 18:16; Luke 23:2; Acts 8:36; Acts 10:47; Acts 11:17; Acts 16:6; Acts 24:23; Acts 27:43; Romans 1:13; 1 Corinthians 14:39; 1 Thessalonians 2:16; 1 Timothy 4:3; Hebrews 7:23; 2 Peter 2:16; 3 John 1:10


## κώμη (id: 002985000000000)

κώμη
====

κώμη (G2968)

noun · κωμόπολις · κῶμος

1\.92 · Geographical Objects and Features · Population Centers

village a relatively unimportant population center (in contrast with πόλις\[b] ‘city,’ [1\.89](#1.89))

[MAT 9:35](https://ref.ly/Matt9:35) · [MAT 10:11](https://ref.ly/Matt10:11) · [MAT 14:15](https://ref.ly/Matt14:15) · [MAT 21:2](https://ref.ly/Matt21:2) · [MRK 6:6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6) · [MRK 6:36](https://ref.ly/Matt6:36) · [MRK 6:56](https://ref.ly/Matt6:56) · [MRK 8:23](https://ref.ly/Matt8:23) · [MRK 8:26](https://ref.ly/Matt8:26) · [MRK 8:27](https://ref.ly/Matt8:27) · [MRK 11:2](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2) · [LUK 5:17](https://ref.ly/Mark5:17) · [LUK 8:1](https://ref.ly/Mark8:1) · [LUK 9:6](https://ref.ly/Mark9:6) · [LUK 9:12](https://ref.ly/Mark9:12) · [LUK 9:52](https://ref.ly/Mark9:52) · [LUK 9:56](https://ref.ly/Mark9:56) · [LUK 10:38](https://ref.ly/Mark10:38) · [LUK 13:22](https://ref.ly/Mark13:22) · [LUK 17:12](https://ref.ly/Mark17:12) · [LUK 19:30](https://ref.ly/Mark19:30) · [LUK 24:13](https://ref.ly/Mark24:13) · [LUK 24:28](https://ref.ly/Mark24:28) · [JHN 7:42](https://ref.ly/Luke7:42) · [JHN 11:1](https://ref.ly/Luke11:1) · [JHN 11:30](https://ref.ly/Luke11:30)

11\.62 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

the people there, the people of a village the inhabitants of a village1 Though in English it may seem perfectly appropriate to speak of ‘announcing the good news to a town’ or ‘... a village,’ in a number of languages this is simply not possible, for any announcement of good news must be directed to people and not to a place or area.

[ACT 8:25](https://ref.ly/John8:25)

1 It is possible that in the case of such meanings as τόπος\[f] ([11\.59](#11.59)), πόλις\[c] ([11\.61](#11.61)), κώμη\[b] ([11\.62](#11.62)), and χώρα\[e] ([11\.64](#11.64)) one should count on certain more or less automatic semantic rules by which the meaning of inhabitants could be derived by metonymy from expressions of place. Since, however, such metonymic developments are far from universal, the distinct meanings are listed here as a practical guide to translators. The same type of problem occurs with Ιεροσόλυμα ‘Jerusalem,’ Ἰουδαία ‘Judea,’ and περίχωρος ‘region’ in [MAT 3:5](https://ref.ly/Matt3:5).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:35; Matthew 10:11; Matthew 14:15; Matthew 21:2; Mark 6:6; Mark 6:36; Mark 6:56; Mark 8:23; Mark 8:26; Mark 8:27; Mark 11:2; Luke 5:17; Luke 8:1; Luke 9:6; Luke 9:12; Luke 9:52; Luke 9:56; Luke 10:38; Luke 13:22; Luke 17:12; Luke 19:30; Luke 24:13; Luke 24:28; John 7:42; John 11:1; John 11:30; Acts 8:25

## κώνωψ (id: 002988000000000)

κώνωψ
=====

κώνωψ (G2971)

noun

4\.48 · Animals · Insects

gnat, mosquito small flying insect; feeds on human or animal blood; regarded as pest The straining of liquids referred to in [MAT 23:24](https://ref.ly/Matt23:24) is based on the regulations in Leviticus 11, in which the gnat is the smallest of the unclean creatures and the camel the largest.\|For the only occurrence of κώνωψ in the NT, one may use a term which refers to any small flying insect which might fall into a beverage and thus have to be strained out.

[MAT 23:24](https://ref.ly/Matt23:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:24

33\.106 · Communication · Speak, Talk

[MAT 9:32](https://ref.ly/Matt9:32) · [MAT 9:33](https://ref.ly/Matt9:33) · [MAT 12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22) · [MAT 12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22) · [MAT 15:30](https://ref.ly/Matt15:30) · [MAT 15:31](https://ref.ly/Matt15:31) · [LUK 1:22](https://ref.ly/Mark1:22) · [LUK 11:14](https://ref.ly/Mark11:14) · [LUK 11:14](https://ref.ly/Mark11:14)

24\.68 · Sensory Events and States · Hear

deaf pertaining to being unable to hear In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘deaf’ is an idiom, for example, ‘his ears are closed’ or ‘he has no ears’ or ‘his ears are stone.’

[MAT 11:5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5) · [MRK 7:32](https://ref.ly/Matt7:32) · [MRK 7:37](https://ref.ly/Matt7:37) · [MRK 9:25](https://ref.ly/Matt9:25) · [LUK 7:22](https://ref.ly/Mark7:22)
